تشریح شیخ ابو الحسن قدوری نے زکوۃ واجب ہونے کی چند شرطیں ذکر کی ہیں:
ا آزاد ہونا، (۲ عاقل ہونا، بالغ ہونا، (۴) مسلمان ہونا ، (۵) مقدار نصاب کا مالک ہونا، ملک نام ہونا ، ( مال نصاب پر حولان حول یعنی ایک سال کا گذر جاتا۔
وجوب زکوۃ کے دلائل : صاحب ہدایہ نے زکوۃ کے وجوب پر تین ویبیں ذکر کی ہیں ۔ (۱) کتاب اللہ یعنی واتوا الزكوة ( ۲) احادیث مشهوره ... ادوا زكوة أموالِكُمُ اور بُنِيَ الْإِسْلَامُ عَلَى خَمْس الحدیث (۳) اجماع امت یعنی رسول اللہ 18 کے زمانے سے آج تک کسی نے زکوۃ کے وجوب کا انکار نہیں کیا ہے۔ فاضل مصنف نے کہا ہے کہ متن کے اندر واجب سے فرض مراد ہے کیونکہ زکوۃ کا ثبوت دلیل قطعی سے ہے اور اس کے ثبوت میں جبہ برابر شبہ نہیں ہے اور جس چیز کا ثبوت دلیل قطعی سے ہو اور اس میں کوئی شبہ نہ ہو تو وہ فرض ہوتا ہے نہ کہ واجب۔ رہا یہ اعتراض کہ متن میں لفظ فرض سے واجب کی طرف عدول کیوں کیا گیا ہے؟ تو اس کا ایک جواب تو یہ ہے زکوۃ کی بعض مقادیر اور کیفیات اخبار و احادیث سے ثابت ہیں۔ دوسرا جواب یہ ہے کہ فرض اور واجب میں سے ہر ایک دوسرے کی جگہ مجاز استعمال کئے جاتے ہیں، پس یہاں بھی فرض کی جگہ لفظ واجب مجازا استعمال کیا گیا ہے۔
آزاد ہونے کی شرط کا فائدہ یہ ہے کہ غلام ، مدبر ، ام ولد اور مکاتب پر زکوۃ فرض نہ ہوگی۔ اور یہ شرط اس لئے لگائی ہے کہ کامل ملکیت آزادی کے ساتھ ہی محقق ہوتی ہے کیونکہ غلام تو کسی چیز کا سرے سے مالک ہی نہیں ہوتا اور مکاتب کو اپنی مملوکہ چیز پر ملک یا ( تصرف) تو حاصل ہوتی ہے لیکن ملک رقبہ ( گردن ، ذات شئے ) حاصل نہیں ہوتی ۔ مکاتب کے مال پر ملک رقبہ مولی کو حاصل ہوتی ہے۔ بہر حال مکاتب کی ملک ناقص ہوتی ہے اور وجوب زکوۃ کے لئے ملک کامل کا ہونا ضروری ہے اور ملک کامل حاصل ہوتی ہے آزادی سے اس لئے وجوب زکوۃ کے واسطے آزاد ہونا شرط قرار دیا گیا ہے۔
دوسری شرط ذی عقل ہونا اور تیسری شرط بالغ ہوتا ہے۔ دوسری شرط کا فائدہ یہ ہوگا کہ دیوانہ اور مجنون آدمی پر زکوۃ فرض نہ ہوگی اور تیسری شرط کا فائدہ یہ ہے کہ نابالغ بچہ پر زکوۃ فرض نہ ہوگی ۔ عقل اور بلوغ کے شرط ہونے پر دلیل اگلے صفحات پر ذکر کریں گے۔
لِمَا تَذْكُرُه سے صاحب بدایه ای طرف اشارہ فرما رہے ہیں ۔
مسلمان ہونا اس لئے شرط ہے کہ زکوۃ ایک عبادت ہے اور کافر سے کوئی عبادت متحقق نہیں ہوتی ۔ وجہ یہ ہے کہ عبادت کا امر اس لئے کیا جاتا ہے تا کہ عبادت کرنے والا ثواب حاصل کر سکے اور کافر ثواب حاصل کرنے کا کا اہل نہیں ہے اس لئے کافر پر زکوۃ فرض نہیں ہوئی ہے۔
اور متقدار نصاب کا مالک ہونا اس لئے شرط ہے کہ مال مالک کو مستغنی کر دینے کا سبب ہے ۔ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے حضرت معاذ رضی اللہ عنہ سے فرمایا تھا تم اعلمهم أن الله تَعَالَى فَرَضَ عَلَيْهِمْ صَدَقَةً تُؤخَذُ مِنْ أغنيائهم وتُرَدُّ فِی فُقَرائهم ، یعنی لوگوں کو با خبر کر دینا کہ اللہ جل شانہ نے ان پر صدقہ فرض کیا ہے ان کے مالداروں سے لے کر ان ہی کے فقراء کو دیدیا جائے ۔ بہر حال حدیث میں مالدار کو منی کہا گیا ہے اور مغنی کثرت مال سے متحقق ہوتا ہے اور کثرت کی کوئی حد معروف نہیں ہے بلکہ اس میں لوگوں کے احوال متفاوت ہیں ۔ پس چونکہ کثرتِ مال یعنی غنی کی کوئی حد مقرر نہیں تھی اس لئے صاحب شریعت صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے سبب زکوۃ یعنی غنی کو مقدار نصاب کے ساتھ مقدر کیا ہے، چنانچہ حدیث ابو سعید خدری ہے قَالَ قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم لَيْسَ فِيْمَا دُونَ حَمْسِ أَوَاقٍ صَدَقَةً وَلَيْسَ فِيْمَا دُونَ خَمْس دُودٍ صَدَقَةٌ وَلَيْسَ فِيْمَا دُونَ خَمْسَةَ اَوسق صَدَقَة " حضرت ابوسعید خدری نے کہا کہ رسول اللہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ پانچ اوقیہ سے کم میں زکوۃ نہیں اور پانچ راُس سے کم میں زکوۃ نہیں اور پانچ اوسق سے کم میں زکوۃ نہیں ہے، پس چونکہ رسول خدا صلى الله عليه وسلم نے سبب زکوۃ کو مقدار کے ساتھ مقدر کیا ہے اس لئے فقہاء کرام نے زکوۃ واجب ہونے کے لئے مقدار نصاب کا مالک ہونا شرط قرار دیا ہے۔
وجوب زکوۃ کی ایک شرط حولان حول ہے، یعنی مال نصاب پر سال گزرنا ضروری ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ زکوۃ مال نامی میں واجب ہوتی ہے نہ کہ غیر نامی میں، اور نمواور بڑھاوا دریافت کرنے کے لئے اتنی مدت کی ضرورت تھی جس میں نمو اور مال کا بڑھ جانا متفق ہو، اور شریعت نے اس مدت کو ایک سال کے ساتھ مقدر کیا ہے چنانچہ حدیث ہے لَا زَكوة فِي مَالِ حَتَّى يَحُولَ عَلَيْهِ الْحَوْلُ پس چونکہ نمو کے لئے شریعت نے ایک سال کی مدت مقرر کی ہے اس لئے فقہاء نے کہا کہ وجوب زکوۃ کے لئے مال نصاب پر ایک سال کا گذر نا ضروری ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے حولان حول کے شرط ہونے کی حکمت شرعی ذکر کرتے ہوئے فرمایا ہے کہ ایک سال کی مدت نمو اور مال بڑھ جانے پر قدرت دینے والی ہے یعنی ایک سال کے اندر آدمی تجارت وغیرہ کے ذریعہ مال کا بڑھا سکتا ہے کیونکہ سال مختلف فصلوں ( سردی گرمی ، ربیع اور خریف ) پر مشتمل ہوتا ہے اور اغلب یہی ہے کہ ان فصلوں میں نرخوں کا تفاوت ہوتا ہے مثلاً ایک چیز ایک فصل میں ارزاں اور دوسری فصل میں گراں ہو جاتی ہے ، پس اس طرح آدمی تجارت میں نفع حاصل کر کے اپنا مال بڑھا سکتا ہے۔ وجوب زکوۃ کا مدار اگر چہ نمؤ اور بڑھاوے پر ہے اور وہ ایک سال میں ہو جاتا ہے اس لئے وجوب زکوہ کا مدار ایک سال کی مدت کو قرار دیا گیا ہے خواہ اس میں حقیقتا نمو پایا جائے یا نہ پایا جائے۔ اب اگر کوئی یہ اعتراض کرے کہ کسی نے اگر اپنا مال زمین میں دفن کر دیا اس پر بھی زکوۃ ہے حالانکہ یہاں کوئی نمو اور بڑھاوا نہیں ہے، تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اس صورت میں حقیقتا اگر چہ نمونہیں لیکن تقدیر نمو ہے کیونکہ یہ مالک کی حماقت ہے کہ اس نے اپنا مال زمین کے حوالہ کیا حالانکہ اس کو اپنے مال پر تجارت وغیرہ کی قدرت حاصل ہے پس اس کی قدرت معتبر ہوگی اور حماقت معتبر نہ ہوگی۔
زکوۃ ادا کر نافی الفور واجب ہے یا تراخی کے ساتھ رہی یہ بات کہ سال گزرنے کے بعد زکوۃ جب واجب الادا ہوئی تو علی الفور واجب ہے یا علی التراخی یعنی فی الفور ادا کرنا واجب ہے یا تراخی بھی جائز ہے؟ اس بارے میں امام کرخی کا قول یہ ہے کہ سال پورا ہونے کے بعد فی الفور ادا کرنا واجب ہے۔ چنانچہ قدرت کے باوجود تا خیر کی صورت میں گنہ گار ہوگا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ اتوا الزَّکوۃ اور حدیث ادوا زكوة اَمْوَالِكُمْ میں امر مطلق ہے اور مطلق امر کا مقتضی مامور بہ کو فی الفور بجالانا ہے۔ اس لئے سال گزرنے کے بعد فی الفور ز کوۃ ادا کرنا جب ہوگا۔ اگر امکانی قدرت کے باوجود زکوۃ ادا کرنے میں تاخیر کی تو گنہگار ہو گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ کی بیان کردہ اس دلیل میں کوئی جان نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ مطلق امر نہ علی الفور کا تقاضا کرتا ہے اور نہ علی التراخی کا ۔ بلکہ محض اس کا تقاضا کرتا ہے کہ مامور بہ کو ادا کر لیا جائے خواہ علی الفور ہو یا خواه علی التراخی یہ پس مکلف کے لئے امتثال امر میں تراخی اور فور دونوں جائز ہوں گے۔ حضرت امام محمد بھی علی الفور زکوۃ واجب ہونے کے قائل ہیں۔ چنانچہ ان سے مروی ہے کہ جس نے بلا عذر ز کوۃ کو مؤخر کیا اس کی شہادت قبول نہیں ہوگی۔ اور تاخیر زکوۃ اور تاخیر حج کے درمیان فرق کرتے ہوئے فرمایا کہ وجوب کے بعد تاخیر حج سے گنہ گار نہیں ہوگا۔ اور تاخیر زکوۃ سے گنہگار ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ زکوۃ فقراء کا حق ہے جلد از جلد ادا کرنا چاہئے۔ اس لئے ان کے حق یعنی زکوۃ کو مؤخر کرنے میں گنہگار ہوگا۔ اور حج خلصتہ اللہ کا حق ہے اور اللہ کی ذات بے نیاز ہے۔ لہذا اس کو
Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on Hidayah Volume 3, section on the command of delay (?) is 28. And it has been said that it is obligatory with delay (ala al-tarakhi) because all of one's life is the time for its fulfillment, and for that reason, if the nisab is destroyed after the year, one is not liable for the amount of Zakat. Explanation: Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri has mentioned several conditions for Zakat being obligatory: (1) being free, (2) being sane, (3) being an adult, (4) being Muslim, (5) possessing the amount of nisab (complete ownership), (6) the passage of one year (hawalan al-hawl) over the nisab property. Proofs for the obligation of Zakat: The author of Al-Hidayah has mentioned three proofs for the obligation of Zakat: (1) The Book of Allah, i.e., 'and pay the Zakat' (Quran 2:43), (2) Well-known hadiths: 'Pay Zakat on your wealth' and 'Islam is built on five' (hadith), (3) Consensus of the Ummah: From the time of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) until today, no one has denied the obligation of Zakat. The eminent author (sahib al-Hidayah) has said that in the text, by 'wajib' is meant 'fard' because Zakat is proven by a definitive proof, and there is no doubt in its establishment. What is proven by a definitive proof without doubt is fard, not wajib. As for the objection: why was the word 'wajib' used instead of 'fard' in the text? One answer is that certain amounts and modalities of Zakat are proven by reports and hadiths (which are zanni). The second answer is that the terms 'fard' and 'wajib' are used figuratively in place of each other, so here 'wajib' is used figuratively in place of 'fard'. The benefit of the condition of being free is that Zakat is not obligatory upon a slave, mudabbar, umm walad, or mukatab. This condition is set because complete ownership (milk kamila) is only realized with freedom. A slave does not own anything at all. A mukatab has ownership of his possession (ownership of use/power of disposition) but not ownership of the essence (raqabah) of the object; the ownership of the essence of the mukatab's property belongs to the master. In any case, the mukatab's ownership is deficient, and for Zakat to be obligatory, complete ownership is necessary, and complete ownership is attained through freedom. Therefore, being free is made a condition for the obligation of Zakat. The second condition is being sane, and the third condition is being an adult. The benefit of the second condition is that Zakat is not obligatory upon an insane person. The benefit of the third condition is that Zakat is not obligatory upon a minor child. The proof for sanity and adulthood being conditions will be mentioned on the following pages. From 'lima tadhkuru' (what you mention), the author of Al-Bidayah is indicating. Being Muslim is a condition because Zakat is an act of worship, and no act of worship is realized from a disbeliever. The reason is that the command for worship is given so that the worshiper may obtain reward, and a disbeliever is not eligible for reward. Therefore, Zakat is not obligatory upon a disbeliever. Possessing the amount of nisab is a condition because wealth is the cause of making the owner independent (ghani). The Prophet (peace be upon him) said to Mu'adh (may Allah be pleased with him): 'Inform them that Allah has obligated upon them charity (sadaqah) to be taken from their rich and given to their poor.' In any case, in the hadith, the wealthy person is called 'ghani', and being 'ghani' is realized by abundance of wealth. But abundance has no well-known limit; rather, the states of people vary in this. Since there was no fixed limit for abundance (ghina), the Lawgiver (peace be upon him) fixed the cause of Zakat, i.e., ghina, with the amount of nisab. Hence, the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: He said, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'There is no charity (Zakat) on less than five awaq, there is no charity on less than five (heads of) camels, there is no charity on less than five wasq.' So because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) fixed the cause of Zakat with a quantity, the jurists made possession of the nisab amount a condition for Zakat being obligatory. One condition for the obligation of Zakat is hawlan al-hawl, i.e., it is necessary for one year to pass over the nisab property. The proof is that Zakat is obligatory on growing (productive) wealth, not on non-growing wealth. To ascertain growth and increase, a period was needed during which growth and increase of wealth would normally occur, and the Lawgiver fixed that period as one year. Hence the hadith: 'There is no Zakat on wealth until a year passes over it.' Therefore, since the Lawgiver prescribed a one-year period for growth, the jurists said that the passing of one year over the nisab property is necessary for the obligation of Zakat. The author of Al-Hidayah, while mentioning the legal wisdom (hikmah) of the condition of hawlan al-hawl, said that a one-year period enables growth and increase of wealth, because within a year a person can increase his wealth through trade etc., since the year consists of different seasons (winter, summer, spring, autumn), and it is most common that prices differ in these seasons; for example, one commodity becomes cheap in one season and expensive in another, so a person can profit from trade and increase his wealth. Although the basis of the obligation of Zakat is growth and increase, and that occurs within a year, the obligation of Zakat is made dependent on a one-year period, whether actual growth occurs or not. Now if someone objects: if a person buries his wealth in the ground, Zakat is still due on it even though there is no growth and increase? The answer is that in this case, although there is no actual growth, there is potential (taqdeer) growth, because it is the owner's foolishness that he entrusted his wealth to the earth while he had the ability to trade with it. So his ability (to grow it) is considered, and his foolishness is not considered. The issue remains: Is Zakat payment obligatory immediately (ala al-fawr) or with delay (ala al-tarakhi)? After the year passes, when Zakat becomes due for payment, is it obligatory immediately or with delay (i.e., is it wajib to pay it instantly or is delay permissible)? Regarding this, Imam al-Karkhi's view is that after the year is complete, it is wajib to pay immediately. Therefore, if one delays despite ability, he is sinful. The proof is that in 'give the Zakat' (Quran) and the hadith 'pay Zakat on your wealth,' the command (amr) is absolute, and the requirement of an absolute command is to perform the commanded act immediately. Therefore, after the year passes, paying Zakat immediately is wajib. If one delays paying Zakat despite the ability to pay, he will be sinful. The author of Al-Hidayah's argument in this has no strength (says the commentary). Because an absolute command does not require immediacy nor does it require delay. Rather, it merely requires that the commanded act be performed, whether immediately or delayed. Hence, for the obligated person, both delay and immediacy are permissible in fulfilling the command. Imam Muhammad also held that Zakat is wajib immediately. It is narrated from him that the testimony of one who delays Zakat without an excuse is not accepted. And he distinguished between delay of Zakat and delay of Hajj, saying that delaying Hajj after obligation does not make one sinful, but delaying Zakat does make one sinful. Because Zakat is the right of the poor (fuqara); it must be paid as soon as possible. Therefore, delaying their right (i.e., Zakat) makes one sinful. Hajj is the right of Allah, and Allah is independent (needless). So...
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from Ashraf al-Hidayah on the conditions for Zakat obligation and the ruling on its timing. It begins by addressing whether Zakat is due with delay (ala al-tarakhi) or immediately (ala al-fawr), referencing a previous discussion. Then it lists the conditions for Zakat being obligatory as stated by Imam al-Quduri: being free, sane, adult, Muslim, owning the nisab with complete ownership, and the passage of one year over the nisab. The commentary then provides proofs for the obligation of Zakat from the Quran, hadith, and consensus. It clarifies that in the matn (text), the term 'wajib' is used to mean 'fard' because Zakat is established by definitive evidence, but the word 'wajib' is used because some details are derived from zanni (probability) sources. The commentary then explains each condition in detail: freedom ensures complete ownership; sanity and adulthood exclude the insane and minors; Islam excludes disbelievers as Zakat is an act of worship; possession of nisab is fixed by hadith (five awaq of silver, five camels, five wasq of grains); and the yearly cycle (hawl) ensures potential growth. The passage also discusses the wisdom behind the hawl and addresses an objection about buried wealth. Finally, it debates whether Zakat is due immediately or with delay: Imam al-Karkhi and Imam Muhammad hold it is immediate, while the author of Al-Hidayah is claimed to have a weak argument; the commentary favors the view that absolute commands do not require immediacy, but for Zakat, because it is a right of the poor, delay without excuse is sinful. This distinction is made between Zakat and Hajj.

Key Terms
فرض (fard): A religious obligation proven by definitive (qat'i) evidence; denial is kufr.
واجب (wajib): A religious obligation proven by probable (zanni) evidence; denial is not kufr but omission is sinful.
نصاب (nisab): The minimum amount of wealth that triggers the obligation of Zakat. For silver: 200 dirhams (approx. 595 grams); for gold: 20 mithqal (approx. 85 grams); for livestock: 5 camels, 30 cows, etc.; for agricultural produce: 5 wasq (approx. 653 kg).
حولان حول (hawlan al-hawl): The passing of one lunar year over the nisab property.
ملک کامل (milk kamila): Complete ownership that includes both usufruct and the essence of the property, allowing full disposal.
علی الفور (ala al-fawr): Immediately, without delay.
علی التراخی (ala al-tarakhi): With delay, i.e., permissible to defer payment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on delaying Zakat payment after the year has passed without a valid excuse?
A) It is permissible to delay, no sin.
B) It is sinful because Zakat is a right of the poor that must be paid immediately.
C) It is obligatory to delay until a convenient time.
D) It is permissible only if one intends to pay later but becomes sinful if the wealth is destroyed.

Key Takeaway
Zakat is an immediate obligation as soon as the year passes, because it is the right of the poor, not merely a delayed command.

Nisab: The Minimum Threshold for Zakat
Explains the nisab condition with hadith proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the nisab amounts for different types of wealth and explain why the Lawgiver specified a threshold.

Core Idea
Zakat is only due on wealth that reaches the nisab amount specified by hadith.

Zakat is a pillar of Islam, but not all wealth is subject to it. The Prophet (peace be upon him) set minimum thresholds (nisab) to determine when zakat becomes obligatory. This lesson examines the hadith evidence and the Hanafi ruling on nisab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
Recognize that the passage addresses the cause of zakat (sabab) and its specification by amount.
2
Locate the primary dalil
Find the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri that sets thresholds for silver, camels, and agricultural produce.
The hadith is cited in the source arabic.
3
Derive the ruling
From the hadith, jurists deduced that ownership of nisab is a condition for zakat.
The passage explains that the Lawgiver specified ghina (wealthiness) with quantity.
4
Note the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school follows these nisab amounts, and the passage confirms this as the relied-upon position.

Source Text

كتاب الزكوة
شرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم ہیں ۔ پس چونکہ کثرتِ مال یعنی غنی کی کوئی حد مقرر نہیں تھی اس لئے صاحب شریعت صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے سبب زکوۃ یعنی غنی کو مقدار نصاب کے ساتھ مقدر کیا ہے، چنانچہ حدیث ابو سعید خدری ہے قَالَ قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم لَيْسَ فِيْمَا دُونَ حَمْسِ أَوَاقٍ صَدَقَةً وَ
لَيْسَ فِيْمَا دُونَ خَمْس دُودٍ صَدَقَةٌ وَلَيْسَ فِيْمَا دُونَ خَمْسَةَ اَوسق صَدَقَة " حضرت ابوسعید خدری نے کہا کہ رسول اللہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ پانچ اوقیہ سے کم میں زکوۃ نہیں اور پانچ راُس سے کم میں زکوۃ نہیں اور پانچ اوسق سے کم میں زکوۃ نہیں ہے، پس چونکہ رسول خدا صلى الله عليه وسلم نے سبب زکوۃ کو مقدار کے ساتھ مقدر کیا ہے اس لئے فقہاء کرام نے زکوۃ واجب ہونے کے لئے مقدار نصاب کا مالک ہونا شرط قرار دیا ہے۔ وجوب زکوۃ کی ایک شرط حولان حول ہے، یعنی مال نصاب پر سال گزرنا ضروری ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ زکوۃ مال نامی میں واجب ہوتی ہے نہ کہ غیر نامی میں، اور نمواور بڑھاوا دریافت کرنے کے لئے اتنی مدت کی ضرورت تھی جس میں نمو اور مال کا بڑھ جانا متفق ہو، اور شریعت نے اس مدت کو ایک سال کے ساتھ مقدر کیا ہے چنانچہ حدیث ہے لَا زَكوة فِي مَالِ حَتَّى يَحُولَ عَلَيْهِ الْحَوْلُ پس چونکہ نمو کے لئے شریعت نے ایک سال کی مدت مقرر کی ہے اس لئے فقہاء نے کہا کہ وجوب زکوۃ کے لئے مال نصاب پر ایک سال کا گذر نا ضروری ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے حولان حول کے شرط ہونے کی حکمت شرعی ذکر کرتے ہوئے فرمایا ہے کہ ایک سال کی مدت نمو اور مال بڑھ جانے پر قدرت دینے والی ہے یعنی ایک سال کے اندر آدمی تجارت وغیرہ کے ذریعہ مال کا بڑھا سکتا ہے کیونکہ سال مختلف فصلوں ( سردی گرمی ، ربیع اور خریف ) پر مشتمل ہوتا ہے اور اغلب یہی ہے کہ ان فصلوں میں نرخوں کا تفاوت ہوتا ہے مثلاً ایک چیز ایک فصل میں ارزاں اور دوسری فصل میں گراں ہو جاتی ہے ، پس اس طرح آدمی تجارت میں نفع حاصل کر کے اپنا مال بڑھا سکتا ہے۔ وجوب زکوۃ کا مدار اگر چہ نمؤ اور بڑھاوے پر ہے اور وہ ایک سال میں ہو جاتا ہے اس لئے وجوب زکوہ کا مدار ایک سال کی مدت کو قرار دیا گیا ہے خواہ اس میں حقیقتا نمو پایا جائے یا نہ پایا جائے۔ اب اگر کوئی یہ اعتراض کرے کہ کسی نے اگر اپنا مال زمین میں دفن کر دیا اس پر بھی زکوۃ ہے حالانکہ یہاں کوئی نمو اور بڑھاوا نہیں ہے، تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اس صورت میں حقیقتا اگر چہ نمونہیں لیکن تقدیر نمو ہے کیونکہ یہ مالک کی حماقت ہے کہ اس نے اپنا مال
زمین کے حوالہ کیا حالانکہ اس کو اپنے مال پر تجارت وغیرہ کی قدرت حاصل ہے پس اس کی قدرت معتبر ہوگی اور حماقت معتبر نہ ہوگی۔
Book of Zakat. Sharh Urdu Hidayah, Volume Three. Since there was no defined limit for abundant wealth (ghina), the Lawgiver (peace be upon him) specified the cause of zakat, i.e., ghina, with the amount of nisab. Thus, the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: he said the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'There is no sadaqah on less than five awaq, and there is no sadaqah on less than five head (of camels), and there is no sadaqah on less than five awsuq.' So since the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) specified the cause of zakat with an amount, the jurists made ownership of the nisab amount a condition for zakat being obligatory. One condition for the obligation of zakat is the passing of a year (hawalan al-hawl), i.e., it is necessary that a year passes over the nisab wealth. The proof is that zakat is obligatory on growing wealth (mal al-nami) not on non-growing wealth. And to ascertain growth (numu) and increase, a period was needed in which growth and increase of wealth typically occur, and the Lawgiver specified this period as one year. Thus the hadith: 'There is no zakat on wealth until a year passes over it.' Since the Lawgiver prescribed one year for growth, the jurists said that for zakat to be obligatory, the passing of one year over the nisab wealth is necessary. The author of Hidayah, mentioning the legal wisdom of making the passing of a year a condition, said that one year gives the ability for growth and increase, because within a year a person can increase his wealth through trade etc., since a year comprises different seasons (winter, summer, spring, autumn) and usually prices differ in these seasons; for example, one thing becomes cheap in one season and expensive in another. Thus a person can gain profit in trade and increase his wealth. Although the basis of zakat obligation is growth and increase, and that occurs in one year, the basis for obligation is set as one year, whether actual growth occurs or not. If someone objects: if a person buries his wealth in the ground, zakat is still due on it even though there is no growth, the answer is that in this case, although there is no actual growth, there is presumptive growth (taqdir al-numu), because it is the owner's foolishness to entrust his wealth to the earth while he has the ability to trade with it, so his ability is considered, not his foolishness.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling with proof on the two essential conditions for zakat obligation: nisab and haul. The author begins by explaining the wisdom behind setting a minimum threshold (nisab): the Lawgiver did not leave the definition of wealthiness vague but specified it with precise amounts from the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri. The hadith sets three thresholds for different categories: 5 awaq (200 dirhams) for silver, 5 head of camels for livestock, and 5 awsuq (approximately 653 kg) for agricultural produce. The author then moves to the second condition: the passing of a full lunar year (hawlan al-hawl). The proof is the hadith 'There is no zakat on wealth until a year passes over it.' The rationale is that zakat is linked to growth (nama'), and growth requires a period in which increase can naturally occur; the Lawgiver set this period as one year. The author addresses a potential objection: what if wealth is buried and does not grow? The answer is that the owner had the ability to trade (and thus earn growth) but chose not to; therefore, the potential for growth (taqdir al-numu) is considered, not the actual lack of growth. This follows the Hanafi principle that ability (qudrah) is the basis for obligation, not actual performance. The passage is taken from a commentary on al-Hidayah and represents the standard Hanafi position.

Key Terms
نصاب (nisab): The minimum amount of wealth that makes zakat obligatory. It is specified by hadith for different types of wealth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) 5 awaq (200 dirhams)
B) 10 awaq
C) 1 awaq
D) 20 dirhams

Key Takeaway
Zakat is only obligatory when wealth reaches the nisab amount specified by the Prophet.

Haul: The Passing of a Lunar Year for Zakat
Explains the haul condition with proof and rationale.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the rationale for the haul condition and apply it to cases involving potential growth.

Core Idea
A full lunar year must pass over nisab wealth for zakat to become due, because zakat is linked to growth.

In addition to the nisab, zakat requires that a lunar year passes over the wealth. The passage explains the wisdom behind this condition: it allows time for typical growth to occur. This lesson explores the hadith evidence and the Hanafi reasoning, including the concept of presumptive growth (taqdir al-numu) for buried wealth.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
The passage states 'hawalan al-hawl' as a condition for zakat obligation.
The source arabic uses حولان حول.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith 'La zakata fi malin hatta yahula 'alayhi al-hawl' (No zakat on wealth until a year passes).
This hadith is cited in the arabic.
3
Understand the rationale
Zakat is obligatory on growing wealth (mal al-nami). Growth takes time; the Lawgider set one year as the period in which growth typically occurs.
The passage explains that a year includes seasons with price fluctuations enabling trade profit.
4
Address the objection about buried wealth
Even if wealth is buried and does not grow, zakat is still due because the owner had the ability to trade (potential growth). This is called taqdir al-numu (presumptive growth).
The passage answers that the owner's ability is considered, not the actual lack of growth.

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling with proof on the two essential conditions for zakat obligation: nisab and haul. Key Terms
حولان حول (hawalan al-hawl): The condition that a full lunar year must pass over the nisab wealth for zakat to become obligatory.
نمؤ (numu): Actual or potential growth of wealth, which is the underlying basis for zakat obligation.

What is the legal wisdom (hikmah) given by the author of Hidayah for the haul condition?
A) To prevent wealth from being idle

Key Takeaway
Zakat is due on wealth that has reached nisab and has been in one's possession for a full lunar year, because zakat is tied to the potential for growth.

The Ruling on Immediate vs Delayed Payment of Zakat
Discusses whether zakat must be paid immediately or can be delayed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school permits delaying zakat and evaluate the opposing positions within and outside the school.

Core Idea
Zakat need not be paid immediately; the Hanafi position permits delay, and accidental loss before payment cancels the obligation.

This passage explores a key intra-Hanafi dispute: once the zakat year ends, must payment be immediate? The author presents multiple Hanafi views and then compares with three other schools. By understanding this dispute, you will grasp how Hanafi usul principles (like the nature of absolute commands) shape practical rulings.

Guided Path
1
State the relied-upon Hanafi position
Identify the mufta bihi view: delay (tarakhi) is permissible, and accidental loss of wealth before payment extinguishes the obligation.
This is the view preferred by later Hanafi authorities.
2
Identify the opposing Hanafi views
List the positions of Imam al-Karkhi and Imam Muhammad (faur required) and Imam Abu Yusuf (tarakhi but sin for Hajj delay).
Note the different usul principles invoked.
3
Analyze the proofs on each side
Examine the dalil: amr mutlaq (absolute command) does not imply faur according to Hanafi usul; the right of the poor is not time-bound.
Contrast with the Shafi'i usul that amr mutlaq implies faur.
4
Note the additional dispute on destruction
Understand the Hanafi argument that when the specific wealth perishes, the part due (1/40th) perishes too, so liability only arises with ta'addi.
Opposing schools consider it a debt that survives destruction.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: a person who delays and then loses his wealth accidentally owes nothing; in other schools, he would still owe.
This highlights the importance of ta'addi in Hanafi law.

زکوۃ ادا کر نافی الفور واجب ہے یا تراخی کے ساتھ رہی یہ بات کہ سال گزرنے کے بعد زکوۃ جب واجب الادا ہوئی تو علی الفور واجب ہے یا علی التراخی یعنی فی الفور ادا کرنا واجب ہے یا تراخی بھی جائز ہے؟ اس بارے میں امام کرخی کا قول یہ ہے کہ سال پورا ہونے کے بعد فی الفور ادا کرنا واجب ہے۔ چنانچہ قدرت کے باوجود تا خیر کی صورت میں گنہ گار ہوگا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ اتوا الزَّکوۃ اور حدیث ادوا زكوة اَمْوَالِكُمْ میں امر مطلق ہے اور مطلق امر کا مقتضی مامور بہ کو فی الفور بجالانا ہے۔ اس لئے سال گزرنے کے بعد فی الفور ز کوۃ ادا کرنا جب ہوگا۔ اگر امکانی قدرت کے باوجود زکوۃ ادا کرنے میں تاخیر کی تو گنہگار ہو گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ کی بیان کردہ اس دلیل میں کوئی جان نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ مطلق امر نہ علی الفور کا تقاضا کرتا ہے اور نہ علی التراخی کا ۔ بلکہ محض اس کا تقاضا کرتا ہے کہ مامور بہ کو ادا کر لیا جائے خواہ علی الفور ہو یا خواه علی التراخی یہ پس مکلف کے لئے امتثال امر میں تراخی اور فور دونوں جائز ہوں گے۔ حضرت امام محمد بھی علی الفور زکوۃ واجب ہونے کے قائل ہیں۔ چنانچہ ان سے مروی ہے کہ جس نے بلا عذر ز کوۃ کو مؤخر کیا اس کی شہادت قبول نہیں ہوگی۔ اور تاخیر زکوۃ اور تاخیر حج کے درمیان فرق کرتے ہوئے فرمایا کہ وجوب کے بعد تاخیر حج سے گنہ گار نہیں ہوگا۔ اور تاخیر زکوۃ سے گنہگار ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ زکوۃ فقراء کا حق جلد از جلد ادا کرنا چاہئے۔ اس لئے ان کے حق یعنی زکوۃ کو مؤخر کرنے میں گنہگار ہوگا۔ اور حج خلصتہ اللہ کا حق ہے اور اللہ کی ذات بے نیاز ہے۔ لہذا اس کو
مؤخر کرنے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔ پس مرنے سے قبل جب جی چاہے حج کرلے لیکن اگر بغیر حج کئے مر گیا حالانکہ اس پر حج فرض تھا تو بالیقین گنہگار ہوگا۔ امام ابو یوسف سے مروی ہے کہ تاخیر زکوۃ سے گنہگار نہیں ہوگا البتہ تاخیر حج سے گنہگار ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ زکوۃ غیر موقت ہے اور حج نماز کی طرح موقت ہے۔ پس زکوۃ تو کبھی بھی ادا کر سکتا ہے لیکن اگر حج نہ کیا تو اب اس کو ایک سال کا انتظار کرنا پڑے گا۔ اور ایک سال کا عرصہ اس قدر دراز ہے کہ نہ جانے کون مرے اور کون جیئے ( کون جیتا ہے تیری زلف کے سر ہونے تک ) اس لئے بلا عذر تا خیر حج کی وجہ سے گنہگار ہوگا۔
امام ابوبکر جصاص رازی کا قول ہے کہ سال گذرنے کے بعد زکوۃ کا مؤخر کرنا جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ تمام عمر اس کی ادا کا وقت ہے۔ یعنی اگر فی الفور ز کوۃ ادا نہ کی تو جب کبھی زندگی میں ادا کرے گا تو وہ ادا ہوگی قضاء نہ ہوگی۔ پس معلوم ہوا کہ زکوۃ کی ادائیگی کا وقت موت تک ہے اور جب ادا کا وقت موت تک ہے تو تاخیر کی وجہ سے گنہ گار نہ ہو گا۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ جب واجب الا داز کو ۃ دے دینے میں کوتاہی کی اور ٹال مٹول کرتا رہا، پھر پورا مال ہلاک ہو گیا تو وہ مقدار زکوۃ کا ضامن نہیں ہوتا۔ اگر زکوۃ فی الفور واجب ہوتی تو اس صورت میں ضامن ہوتا۔ پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ سال گذرنے کے بعد زکوۃ فی الفور واجب نہیں ہوتی بلکہ اس کو مؤخر کر دینا بھی جائز ہے۔ امام مالک، امام شافعی اور امام احمد نے فرمایا ہے کہ اس صورت میں مقدار زکوۃ کا ضامن ہوگا۔ جیسا کہ پورے مال کو ہلاک کر دینے کی صورت میں بالا تفاق ضامن ہوتا ہے۔ اس طرح ہلاک ہونے کی صورت میں بھی ضامن ہوگا۔ ان حضرات کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مالِ نصاب پر سال گذرنے سے زکوۃ مالک نصاب کے ذمہ میں دین ہوگئی ہے اور ہلاک ہونے کی وجہ سے دین ساقط نہیں ہوتا لہذا زکوۃ بھی ساقط نہ ہو گی۔ ہمارا جواب یہ ہے کہ مالک نصاب پر نصاب کا ایک جز یعنی چالیسواں حصہ واجب ہے۔ پس جب پورا مال نصاب ہلاک ہو گیا تو اس کے ایک جز کی بقاء کیسے ممکن ہوگی ۔ وہ بھی ہلاک ہو گیا۔ اس کے برخلاف اگر مالک نصاب نے پورے مالِ نصاب کو ہلاک کر دیا تو اس میں اس کی طرف سے تعدی پائی گئی۔ پس اس کی گوشمالی اور زجز و تو شیخ کرنے کے لئے اُسے زکوۃ کا ضامن قرار دیا گیا۔ اور چونکہ ہلاک ہونے کی صورت
میں مالک کی طرف سے کوئی تعدی نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے اس صورت میں زجر و توبیخ کی کوئی ضرورت نہ رہی۔
Is the payment of zakat obligatory immediately (faur) or can it be delayed (tarakhi)? This matter arises after the year passes and zakat becomes due. Regarding this, Imam al-Karkhi says that immediately after the year is complete, it is wajib to pay immediately, and delaying with capability results in sin. His proof is that the command 'Give zakat' (atū al-zakāt) and the hadith 'Pay zakat of your wealth' are absolute commands, and an absolute command requires immediate compliance. Therefore, one becomes sinful by delaying. However, the author of Hidayah mentions that this argument has no weight, because an absolute command requires neither immediacy nor delay; it merely requires performance, whether immediately or later. Both are permissible for the obligee. Imam Muhammad also holds that zakat is due immediately, such that if someone delays without excuse, his testimony is rejected. He differentiates between delaying zakat and delaying Hajj: delaying zakat causes sin because it is the right of the poor and should be paid promptly, whereas Hajj is a right of Allah, who is independent. Therefore, one may delay Hajj until before death, but if one dies without performing it while it was obligatory, he is undoubtedly sinful. Imam Abu Yusuf is reported to hold that delaying zakat does not cause sin, but delaying Hajj does, because zakat is not time-bound (ghayr muwaqqat) whereas Hajj is time-bound. One can pay zakat at any time, but if one misses Hajj, he must wait a whole year, which is a long time. So delaying Hajj without excuse is sinful. Imam Abu Bakr al-Jassas al-Razi holds that delaying zakat after the year is permissible because the entire lifetime is its time for payment. If he does not pay immediately, whenever he pays during his life, it will be ada' (fulfillment), not qada' (make-up). Therefore, the time for payment is until death, and delay does not cause sin. This is supported by the ruling that if after the year the wealth is destroyed before payment, the owner is not liable for the zakat amount. If zakat were due immediately, he would be liable. This proves that zakat is not immediately due. Imam Malik, Imam Shafi'i, and Imam Ahmad say that in this case he is liable for the zakat amount, just as he would be liable if he deliberately destroyed the wealth. Their proof is that once the year passes, zakat becomes a debt on the owner, and destruction does not cancel a debt. Our (Hanafi) response: what is obligatory on the owner is a part of the nisab, i.e., one-fortieth. When the entire nisab is destroyed, how can that part remain? It is also destroyed. In contrast, if the owner deliberately destroys the wealth, there is transgression (ta'addi), so he is made liable as a deterrent. But when the wealth is destroyed without his fault, there is no transgression, so no deterrent is needed.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage addresses a significant intra-Hanafi dispute: once the zakat year elapses, must the zakat be paid immediately (faur) or can it be delayed (tarakhi)? The author presents several positions. Imam al-Karkhi and Imam Muhammad hold that it is wajib to pay immediately, and delay without excuse incurs sin. Imam Abu Yusuf holds that delay is permissible without sin, but for Hajj it is not. Later Hanafis like Imam al-Jassas also side with permissibility. The author then brings in the position of the three other imams (Malik, Shafi'i, Ahmad) on the additional question: if the wealth is destroyed after the year but before payment, is the owner liable? The Hanafis say no, because zakat is a specified part of the wealth (1/40th), and when the wealth perishes, that part perishes with it. The other schools consider it a debt that survives destruction. The author refutes their argument by distinguishing between deliberate destruction (which incurs liability) and accidental destruction (which does not). The relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi) is that zakat can be delayed, and the owner is not liable if the wealth perishes without his negligence. This passage illustrates the Hanafi method of weighing proofs (amr mutlaq vs. considerations of rights of the poor) and the importance of ta'addi in liability.

Key Terms
الفور (al-faur): Immediate performance of an obligatory act as soon as it becomes due
التراخی (al-tarakhi): Delayed performance of an obligatory act, permissible within the time period
تعدی (ta'addi): Transgression or exceeding proper limits, e.g., deliberately destroying one's own wealth after zakat became due

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a person's zakatable wealth is accidentally destroyed after the year passes but before he pays?
A) He must still pay zakat from other wealth
B) He is not liable for the zakat
C) He must pay only if he had the money saved
D) He must pay double

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, zakat is not immediately due after the year; delay is permissible, and accidental loss cancels liability.

Zakat Not Obligatory on Minors and Insane Persons: Dispute with Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i on zakat for minors/insane

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakat for minors and insane persons, compare it with the Shafi'i view, and explain the reasoning based on the nature of zakat as 'ibadah.

Core Idea
Zakat is an act of worship requiring choice and intention, not a mere financial due.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses whether zakat is obligatory on the wealth of minors and the insane. Imam al-Shafi'i argued that zakat is a financial obligation analogous to kharaj or maintenance, and thus should apply regardless of legal capacity. The Hanafi school counters that zakat's essence is worship, which demands intentional choice. The distinction between financial dues (mu'nah) and acts of worship is central to the dispute.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Read the opening of the passage: 'Zakat is not obligatory upon the child and the insane.' Identify the ruling and note that it is contrary to al-Shafi'i.
The ruling is simple: no zakat on minors or insane.
2
Identify the Shafi'i proof
The passage quotes al-Shafi'i's argument: zakat is a financial imposition (gharamah maliyyah) and is analogized to other financial obligations like spousal maintenance, 'ushr, and kharaj. Understand the qiyas.
Shafi'i sees zakat as a right of property, not requiring intention.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi proof: zakat is an act of worship ('ibadah), so it requires choice (ikhtiyar) to actualize the meaning of divine testing (ibtilā'). Minors and insane lack intellect (aql), hence no choice. Then note the distinction from kharaj and 'ushr, where the financial aspect predominates.
The key distinction: 'ibadah vs. mu'nah.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The passage discusses partial recovery: if the insane recovers during part of the year, Abu Yusuf considers the majority of the year, while Abu Hanifa considers the year from recovery (like a child reaching puberty).
This affects the calculation of the zakat year.
5
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: in Hanafi, guardian does not pay zakat on behalf of minor/insane; in Shafi'i, guardian must pay if wealth reaches nisab. Also, note the mufta bihi position.
The ruling has direct financial implications.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کن لوگوں پر زکوۃ واجب نہیں، اقوال فقہاء
وَ لَيْسَ عَلَى الصَّبِيِّ وَالْمَجْنُون زَكوةً خِلافًا للشَّافِعِي فَإِنَّهُ يَقُولُ هِيَ غَرَامَةٌ مَالِيَّةٌ فَتُعْتَبَرُ بِسَائِرِ الْمُؤْنِ كَنفَقَةِ الزَّوْجَاتِ وَصَارَ كَالْعُشْرِ وَالْحَرَاجِ وَلَنَا أَنَّهَا عِبَادَةً فَلَا تَتَادَّى إِلَّا بِالْإِخْتِيَارِ تَحْقِيقًا لِمَعْنَى الْإِبْتَلَاءِ وَلَا اخْتِيَارَ لَهُمَا لِعَدَمِ الْعَقْلِ بِخَلافِ الْخَرَاجِ لِأَنَّهُ مَوْنَةُ الْأَرْضِ وَكَذَلِكَ الْغَالِبُ فِي الْعُشْرِ مَعْنَى الْمُؤْنَةِ وَمَعْنَى الْعِبَادَةِ تَابِعٌ وَلَوْ أَفَاقَ فِي بَعْضٍ السَّنَةِ فَهُوَ بِمَنْزِلَةِ إِفَاقَةٍ فِى بَعْضِ الشَّهْرِ فِى الصَّوْمِ وَعَنْ أَبِى يُوسُفَ أَنَّهُ يُعْتَبَرُ اَكْثَرَ الْحَوْلِ وَلَا فَرَقَ بَيْنَ الأَصْلِي وَالْعَارِضِي وَعَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ أَنَّهُ إِذَا بَلَغَ مَجْنُونَا يُعْتَبَرُ الْحَوْلُ مِنْ وَقْتِ الْافَاقَةِ بِمَنْزِلَةِ الصَّبِيِّ إِذَا بَلَغَ ترجمہ اور نابالغ اور مجنون پر زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہے۔ امام شافعی کا اختلاف ہے اس لئے کہ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ زکوۃ تو مال پر ایک لازمی حق ہے تو اس کو دوسری تمام مؤنتوں ( حقوق مالیہ پر قیاس کیا جائے گا۔ جیسے بیویوں کا نفقہ اور عشر اور خراج کے مانند ہو گیا اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ زکوۃ ایک عبادت ہے۔ پس یہ عبادت بغیر اختیار کے ادا نہ ہوگی۔ تا کہ ابتلاء کے معنی متحقق ہوں اور عقل معدوم ہونے کی وجہ سے ان دونوں کے لئے کوئی اختیار نہیں ہے۔ برخلاف خراج کے کیونکہ وہ زمین کی مؤنت ہے۔ اور اسی طرح عشر میں بھی مونت کے معنی
On whom zakat is not obligatory – statements of the jurists. And zakat is not obligatory upon the child (sabi) and the insane (majnun), contrary to al-Shafi'i, for he says: It is a financial imposition (gharamah maliyyah), so it is analogized to all other financial obligations like spousal maintenance, and it becomes like 'ushr and kharaj. Our proof is that it is an act of worship ('ibadah), so it is not performed except with choice (ikhtiyar) to actualize the meaning of test (ibtilā'), and they lack choice due to absence of intellect. Unlike kharaj, because it is a due on land. Similarly, in 'ushr the predominant meaning is that of a due (mu'nah), and the meaning of worship is subordinate. And if he (the insane) becomes rational during some part of the year, it is like the recovery during some part of the month in fasting. It is reported from Abu Yusuf that the majority of the year is considered (akthar al-hawl), and there is no distinction between permanent insanity and temporary. And from Abu Hanifa that if an insane person becomes mentally fit, the year is calculated from the time of recovery, like the child when he reaches puberty. Translation: And zakat is not obligatory upon the child and the insane. Imams Shafi'i disagrees because he says zakat is a necessary financial right, so it is analogized to all other financial obligations like spousal maintenance and becomes like 'ushr and kharaj. Our proof is that zakat is an act of worship; thus it will not be performed without choice, so that the meaning of test is realized, and they have no choice due to absence of intellect. Unlike kharaj because it is a due on land. Similarly, in 'ushr the meaning of due predominates, and the meaning of worship is subordinate.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling that zakat is not obligatory on children (sabi) and the insane (majnun), and refutes the Shafi'i position. The author quotes the Arabic text from al-Hidayah directly. Shafi'i analogizes zakat to other financial obligations like nafaqah and kharaj, arguing that since these are due regardless of legal capacity, so should zakat. The Hanafi response is that zakat is fundamentally an act of worship ('ibadah), which requires intention (niyyah) and choice (ikhtiyar) to fulfill the purpose of divine testing (ibtilā'). Minors and the insane lack the legal capacity of intellect (aql) and therefore cannot validly perform it. The author also distinguishes zakat from kharaj (land tax) and 'ushr (tithe on produce), stating that in kharaj the predominant aspect is mu'nah (financial due), and in 'ushr the worship aspect is subordinate. Therefore, zakat is not analogous. The passage also includes an intra-Hanafi discussion regarding a person who is insane for part of the year: Abu Yusuf says the majority of the year is considered, while Abu Hanifa says the year starts from the time of recovery, similar to a child reaching puberty. This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
صبی (sabi): A minor who has not reached puberty; such a person is not obligated to perform zakat.
مجنون (majnun): An insane person lacking intellect; like sabi, not obligated for zakat.
مؤنت (mu'nah): A financial due or burden that is incurred regardless of capacity, like kharaj; it does not require intention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is zakat not obligatory on a minor even if he possesses nisab wealth?
A) Because minors are not financially responsible
B) Because zakat is an act of worship requiring choice and intention, which minors lack
C) Because minors need the wealth for their growth
D) Because the Prophet exempted minors

Key Takeaway
Zakat is an act of worship; thus it is not obligatory on minors and the insane, who lack the capacity for intention and choice.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate
8 min
Zakat on Minors and Insane Persons: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on zakat obligation for minors and insane persons

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on zakat for minors and insane persons, explain the Hanafi proof from hadith and rational argument, and distinguish the Hanafi classification of zakat as worship ('ibadah) from the Shafi'i classification as financial right (gharamah).

Core Idea
Zakat is worship requiring intention; minors and insane lack capacity, so no zakat.

This passage presents a major inter-madhhab dispute: is zakat obligatory on the wealth of minors and insane persons? The Hanafi school says no, based on the hadith 'رفع القلم' and the nature of zakat as worship. The Shafi'i school says yes, relying on a hadith about the orphan's guardian and qiyas to maintenance obligations. Understanding this dispute requires grasping the Hanafi distinction between worship and maintenance, and its effect on legal capacity.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling of the Hanafi school: zakat is not wajib on the wealth of minors and insane persons, even if they possess nisab.
This is the mufta bihi position from Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Identify the Hanafi proof
The primary dalil is the hadith 'رفع القلم عن ثلاثة' (the pen is lifted from three). Also a rational proof: zakat is worship, and worship requires choice (ikhtiyar), which minors and insane lack.
The hadith is reported by Abu Dawud and al-Nasa'i.
3
State the Shafi'i position and proof
The Shafi'i school (along with Maliki and Hanbali) holds zakat is obligatory. Their proof includes the hadith: 'ألا من ولي يتيما له مال فليتجر فيه ولا يتركه حتى تأكله الصدقة' and qiyas on nafaqah and kharaj.
They classify zakat as a financial right (gharamah maliyah).
4
Analyse the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafis refute the Shafi'i hadith as weak (da'if) and interpret 'الصدقة' as nafaqah, not zakat. They reject the qiyas because zakat is worship, while nafaqah and kharaj are maintenance (mu'nah); they are different categories.
The distinction between ibadah and mu'nah is crucial.
5
Determine the practical difference
The thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafis do not take zakat from a minor's or insane person's wealth; Shafi'is require the guardian to pay it annually.
This affects estate planning and guardian duties.

Source Text

عاقل ہو ۔ حدیث کی مراد یہ ہے کہ مذکورہ تینوں آدمی احکام شرع کے مخاطب نہیں ہیں۔ پس جب نا بالغ بچہ اور مجنون حکم شرع کے مخاطب اور مکلف نہیں ہیں۔ تو ان پر زکوۃ کیونکر فرض ہوگی۔ رہی وہ حدیث جس کو امام Kitab al-Zakat. ... (long translation not fully included here for brevity) ... Summary: The passage discusses the obligation of zakat on the wealth of minors and insane persons. The Hanafi position is that it is not obligatory. The Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali positions are that it is obligatory. The Hanafi proof includes the hadith 'The pen is lifted from three...' and rational argument that zakat is an act of worship requiring choice. The Shafi'i proof includes the hadith about the orphan's guardian and qiyas on nafaqah and kharaj. The Hanafi response rebuts the Shafi'i hadith as weak and interprets it differently, and rejects the qiyas because zakat is worship while kharaj and 'ushr are maintenance.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute on whether zakat is obligatory on the wealth of minors (saghir) and insane persons (majnun). The Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani) holds that zakat is not obligatory on them because they are not legally responsible (mukallaf). The Shafi'i school (along with Maliki and Hanbali) holds that zakat is obligatory, and their guardian should pay it from their wealth. The Hanafi proof is the hadith: 'The pen is lifted from three: the sleeper until he wakes, the child until he reaches puberty, and the insane until he recovers.' This indicates that such persons are not addressed by the commands of Sharia, including zakat. A rational proof is added: zakat is an act of worship ('ibadah), and worship requires intention and choice (ikhtiyar), which minors and the insane lack. The Shafi'i counter-argument includes a hadith: 'Whoever becomes the guardian of an orphan who has wealth, let him trade with it and not leave it so that charity consumes it.' They interpret 'charity' as zakat. The Hanafi response: (1) This hadith is weak according to Imam al-Tirmidhi and Imam Ahmad; (2) Even if accepted, 'charity' here means nafaqah (maintenance) for the orphan, not zakat. The Shafi'i also makes qiyas: zakat is a financial obligation (gharamah maliyah), similar to nafaqah of wife and kharaj/'ushr on land, which are obligatory on minors and insane. The Hanafi rebuttal: Zakat is purely worship ('ibadah), while kharaj and 'ushr are maintenance (mu'nah) for the land. The dominant aspect of 'ushr is maintenance, not worship. Qiyas cannot be made between different categories. The author then explains the term mu'nah: that which causes the preservation of something, e.g., nafaqah preserves life and marriage. Kharaj and 'ushr preserve the land by funding the military and the poor, respectively. Thus, they are not analogous to zakat.

Key Terms
زكوة (zakāh): The obligatory charity on wealth, considered an act of worship by Hanafis.
نابالغ (nābāligh): A person who has not reached puberty; legally a minor.
مجنون (majnūn): An insane person lacking reason.
غرامت (gharāmah): Financial obligation; a right that becomes incumbent on a person.
مؤنت (mu'nah): Maintenance; something that causes preservation or continuation of a thing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is zakat not obligatory on the wealth of a minor or an insane person?
A) Because they do not own wealth
B) Because they are not legally responsible (mukallaf) and zakat is an act of worship requiring choice
C) Because their guardian is not allowed to pay zakat from their wealth
D) Because their wealth is not subject to any financial obligations

Key Takeaway
Zakat is not obligatory on minors and insane persons in the Hanafi school because they lack legal capacity and zakat is an act of worship requiring intention.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate
12 min
Why Zakat is Not Obligatory on Orphans and the Insane
Refuting Shafi'i proofs on zakat for orphans and insane

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on zakat for orphans and insane persons, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-arguments by critiquing their hadith and qiyas.

Core Idea
Zakat is 'ibadah, and 'ibadah requires intention; orphans and the insane lack intellect, so zakat is not obligatory.

In this passage, the Hanafi author systematically refutes the Shafi'i view that zakat must be paid on the property of orphans and insane individuals. The refutation proceeds in three stages: first, discrediting the Shafi'i hadith evidence; second, presenting a rational proof based on the nature of worship; and third, demolishing the analogy to kharaj and 'ushr. By the end, you'll understand why Hanafis treat zakat differently from financial impositions on land.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
State the ruling: zakat is not fard (obligatory) on children or insane persons. Note that this is a settled Hanafi position with no internal ikhtilaf.
The ruling applies to property owned by these individuals; guardians are not required to pay zakat on their behalf.
2
Examine the Shafi'i proof (hadith)
The Shafi'is cite a hadith: 'Trade with the orphan's property so that it is not consumed by sadaqah.' They interpret 'sadaqah' as zakat. Analyse why the Hanafis reject this.
The Hanafi response: the hadith is weak (declared by Tirmidhi and Ahmad), and even if authentic, 'sadaqah' here means nafaqah (maintenance), not zakat.
3
Analyse the Hanafi rational proof (dalil 'aqli)
Zakat is one of the five pillars; it is an 'ibadah (act of worship). 'Ibadah requires choice (ikhtiyar) and intention (niyyah). Since children and the insane have no intellect, they cannot have choice, so zakat cannot be performed on their behalf, hence it is not obligatory.
This proof rests on the Hanafi usul principle that 'ibadat require niyyah, which depends on a sound mind.
4
Understand the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i qiyas
The Shafi'is analogize zakat to kharaj and 'ushr, which are obligatory on land regardless of the owner's capacity. The Hanafi refutation distinguishes: zakat is purely 'ibadah, while kharaj/'ushr are mu'nat (cost/maintenance) of land. Mu'nat preserves the land by supporting the army and the poor, and is not an act of worship requiring intention.
The dominant element in kharaj/'ushr is mu'nat, not 'ibadah; thus the analogy is invalid.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Hanafis do not take zakat from the property of a child or insane person; Shafi'is require the guardian to pay it. This is a real difference in practice.

جواب تو یہ ہے کہ امام ترمذی نے اس کی سند کو ضعیف کہا ہے۔ اور امام احمد نے فرمایا کہ یہ صحیح حدیث نہیں ہے۔ پس امام احمد اور امام ترمذی کے کلام کرنے کے بعد یہ حدیث کس طرح قابل استدلال ہو سکتی ہے۔ اور اگر اس کو صحیح اور قابل استدلال مان بھی لیا جائے تو ہم کہتے ہیں کہ حَتَّى تَأكُلَهُ الصَّدَقَة میں صدقہ سے مراد نفقہ ہے۔ مطلب یہ ہے کہ مقیم کے متولی کو چاہئے کہ وہ یتیم کے مال میں تجارت کرے ورنہ خود یتیم کا نفقہ اور اگر اس کی بیوی ہو تو اس کا نفقہ اس پورے مال کو چند سالوں میں کھا ڈالے گا۔ یعنی جب اس مال سے یتیم کی ضروریات بھی پوری کی جائیں گی۔ اور بیوی ہو تو اس کا نفقہ بھی اس میں سے دیا جائے گا تو اس مال سے تجارت نہ کرنے کی صورت میں وہ مال رفتہ رفتہ سارا ختم ہو جائے گا۔ اس تشریح کے بعد یہ حدیث شافعی کا مستدل نہ ہوگی۔

ہماری طرف سے عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ زکوۃ ایک عبادت ہے۔ کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے بُنِيَ الْإِسْلَامُ عَلَى خَمْسِ الخ اور زکوۃ کے علاوہ باقی چار چیزیں یعنی شہادتین، نماز، روزہ، حج بالاتفاق عبادت ہیں۔ پس اسی طرح زکوۃ بھی عبادت ہے۔ اور جو چیز عبادت ہو وہ بغیر اختیار کے ادا نہیں ہوتی۔ اس لئے کہ عبادت نام ہے ابتلاء اور آزمائش کا اور آزمائش کے معنی بغیر اختیار کے حق نہیں ہو سکتے۔ پس ابتلاء اور آزمائش کے معنی ثابت کرنے کے لئے اختیار ضروری ہے اور ان دونوں کو چونکہ عقل و دانش نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے ان کے واسطے اختیار بھی نہ ہوگا۔ اور عبادت چونکہ بغیر اختیار کے ادا نہیں ہوتی۔ اس لئے ان دونوں کی طرف سے زکوۃ بھی ادا نہ ہو گی۔ اور جب ان کی طرف سے زکوۃ ادا نہیں ہو سکتی تو معلوم ہوا کہ ان پر زکوۃ فرض نہیں ہے۔

بخلاف الخراج سے امام شافعی کے قیاس کا جواب ہے جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ زکوۃ کو خراج وغیرہ پر قیاس کرنا درست نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے کہ زکوۃ محض ایک عبادت ہے اور خراج اور عشر زمین کی مؤنت ہے۔ خراج کے اندر تو مؤنت ہی کے معنی پائے جاتے ہیں۔ اور عشر کے اندر مؤنت کے معنی غالب اور عبادت کے معنی تابع ہیں۔ اور یہ امر مسلم ہے کہ غالب کا اعتبار ہوتا ہے۔ تابع کا اعتبار نہیں ہوتا۔ پس ثابت ہوا کہ عشر بھی خراج کی طرح مؤنت ہے۔ پس جب مقیس ( زکوۃ ) اور مقیس علیہ ( خراج عشر ) میں اس قدر فرق ہے کہ مقیس عبادت کے قبیل سے ہے۔ اور مقیس علیہ مؤنت کے قبیل سے ہے۔ تو اس فرق کے ہوتے ہوئے یہ قیاس کس طرح درست ہو گا۔ رہی یہ بات کہ مؤنت کس کو کہتے ہیں۔ اور خراج اور عشر زمین کی مؤنت کس طرح ہے۔ سو آپ کفایہ کے بیان کے مطابق ملاحظہ فرمائیے فرمایا ہے کہ مؤنت اس چیز کا نام ہے جو کسی شیء کی بقاء کا سبب ہو یعنی بقاء شیء کا نام مؤنت ہے۔ جیسے نفقہ زوجہ بقاء حیات اور بقاء نکاح کا سبب ہے۔ لہذا نفقہ بوجہ مؤنت کہلائے گا۔ ملاحظہ ہو کہ خراج اور عشر دونوں مالکوں کے قبضہ میں بقاء اراضی کا سبب ہیں۔ اس لئے کہ عشر کا مصرف فقراء ہیں۔ اور خراج کا مصرف مقاتلہ ( بکسر التاء ) یعنی لڑائی کرنے والی جماعت ہے۔ پس مقاتلہ ( لڑائی کرنے والی جماعت ) خراج کے مال سے جنگی تیاری کر کے حملہ آور کفار کو اہل اسلام سے دفع کریں گے۔ اور فقراء عشر کا مال کھا کر کفار کے مقابلہ میں مسلمانوں کی فتح اور نصرت کی دعا کریں گے۔ چنانچہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم کا ارشاد ہے إِنَّمَا تُنصَرُونَ بِضُعَفَائِكُم یعنی مسلمانو! تمہاری مدد کی جائے گی تمہارے کمزور لوگوں کے ذریعہ۔ اور بات ظاہر ہے کہ کمزور لوگوں کے ذریعہ مدد دعا ہی کے ساتھ کی جا سکتی ہے۔ چنانچہ علامہ ابن الہمام نے فتح القدیر میں یہ روایت ان الفاظ کے ساتھ ذکر کی ہے۔ إِنَّمَا تُنصَرُ هَذِهِ الْأُمَّةُ بِضُعَفَائِهَا بِدَعْوَاهُمْ - (الحديث) بہر حال جب مقاتلہ یعنی اسلامی فوج نے کفار کو مسلمانوں کے ملک سے دفع کیا اور فقراء نے دعاؤں کے ذریعہ ان کی مدد کی تو کیا اسلامی فوج اور فقراء سبب ہیں مسلمانوں کے ملک اور ان کی زمین کی بقاء کا اور ان دونوں یعنی اسلامی فوج اور فقراء کی بقاء کا سبب خراج اور عشر ہیں۔ اور چونکہ شیء کے سبب کا سبب اس شیء کا سبب ہوتا ہے اس لئے خراج اور عشر دونوں زمین کے مالک کے قبضہ میں زمین کی بقاء کا سبب ہوں گے اور جو چیز شیء کی بقاء کا سبب ہوتی ہے وہ مؤنت کہلاتی ہے۔ اس لئے خراج اور عشر دونوں زمین کی مؤنت کہلائیں گے۔
The answer is that Imam Tirmidhi declared its chain weak. And Imam Ahmad said that this hadith is not authentic. So after the statements of Imam Ahmad and Imam Tirmidhi, how can this hadith be used as evidence? And if it is accepted as authentic and usable, we say that in 'hatta ta'kulahu al-sadaqah', sadaqah means nafaqah (maintenance). The meaning is that the guardian of the resident should trade with the orphan's property, otherwise the orphan's own nafaqah—and if he has a wife, her nafaqah—will consume the entire property over several years. That is, when the orphan's needs are met from this property, and if there is a wife, her nafaqah is also given from it, then without trading, the property will gradually be completely consumed. With this explanation, this hadith will no longer be evidence for the Shafi'is.

Our rational proof is that zakat is an 'ibadah (act of worship). Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Islam is built on five [pillars]...' and besides zakat, the other four things—shahadatayn, salah, sawm, Hajj—are unanimously 'ibadah. So similarly, zakat is 'ibadah. And whatever is 'ibadah cannot be performed without choice (ikhtiyar). Because 'ibadah means test and trial, and the meaning of trial cannot be realized without choice. So to establish the meaning of test and trial, choice is necessary, and since these two (children and insane) do not have intellect, they will have no choice. And since 'ibadah is not performed without choice, zakat will not be performed on their behalf. And when zakat cannot be performed on their behalf, it is known that zakat is not fard upon them.

As for the qiyas (analogy) of Imam al-Shafi'i with kharaj, the answer is that it is not correct to analogize zakat to kharaj etc. Because zakat is purely an 'ibadah, while kharaj and 'ushr are mu'nat (cost/maintenance) of land. In kharaj, only the meaning of mu'nat is found. In 'ushr, the meaning of mu'nat is dominant and the meaning of 'ibadah is subordinate. And it is a settled matter that the dominant element is considered, not the subordinate. So it is established that 'ushr is also mu'nat like kharaj. Thus when the maqis (zakat) and maqis 'alayh (kharaj/'ushr) have this much difference—the maqis is of the category of 'ibadah and the maqis 'alayh is of the category of mu'nat—then with this difference, how can this qiyas be valid? As for what mu'nat means and how kharaj and 'ushr are mu'nat of land, please see according to the explanation of Kifayah. It says: mu'nat is the name for something that is the cause of the preservation of something, i.e., it is the preservation of something. For example, the nafaqah of the wife is the cause of the preservation of life and the preservation of marriage, therefore nafaqah is called mu'nat. Note that kharaj and 'ushr are both causes of the preservation of land in the possession of the owners. Because the recipients of 'ushr are the poor, and the recipients of kharaj are the muqatilah (fighters). So the muqatilah will prepare for war with the wealth of kharaj and repel the attacking disbelievers from the Muslims. And the poor will eat the wealth of 'ushr and pray for the victory and help of the Muslims against the disbelievers. Indeed, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'You are only helped by your weak ones.' It is obvious that help from the weak can only come through prayer. Indeed, Allamah Ibn al-Humam mentioned this narration in Fath al-Qadir with these words: 'This ummah is only helped by its weak ones through their prayers.' (Hadith) In any case, when the muqatilah (Islamic army) repelled the disbelievers from the Muslims' land and the poor helped them through prayers, then the Islamic army and the poor are the cause of the preservation of the Muslims' land. And the cause of the preservation of these two (the army and the poor) is kharaj and 'ushr. And since the cause of the cause of a thing is the cause of that thing, therefore kharaj and 'ushr will be the cause of the preservation of the land in the possession of the landowner. And whatever is the cause of the preservation of a thing is called mu'nat. Therefore, kharaj and 'ushr are both called mu'nat of the land.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and the Shafi'is regarding the obligation of zakat on the property of orphans and insane persons. The author first refutes the Shafi'i proof based on a hadith by showing its weakness according to Imam Tirmidhi and Imam Ahmad. Even if the hadith were accepted, its interpretation (that 'sadaqah' means 'nafaqah' not zakat) nullifies the Shafi'i argument. Then the author presents a rational proof (dalil 'aqli): zakat is an 'ibadah, and 'ibadah requires choice (ikhtiyar). Since children and the insane lack intellect, they cannot have choice, thus zakat is not obligatory on them. This is a fundamental Hanafi principle distinguishing between 'ibadat (which require intention) and mu'amalat (financial obligations). Finally, the author responds to the Shafi'i qiyas that compares zakat to kharaj and 'ushr. The Hanafi response differentiates between zakat as pure 'ibadah and kharaj/'ushr as mu'nat (cost/maintenance) for land. Mu'nat is defined as that which causes the preservation of something, and kharaj/'ushr preserve the land by supporting the army and the poor, whereas zakat is an act of worship for its own sake. Therefore, the analogy is invalid.

Key Terms
عبادت ('Ibadah): Act of worship that requires intention and submission; includes salah, sawm, zakat, etc.
اختیار (Ikhtiyar): Free choice and volition; a prerequisite for valid worship because worship is a test requiring conscious obedience.
مؤنت (Mu'nat): Cost or maintenance that ensures the preservation of something; e.g., kharaj and 'ushr preserve land.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the core reason Hanafis give for not requiring zakat on the property of a child or insane person?
A) The child or insane person does not own enough property.
B) Zakat is an 'ibadah that requires intention (niyyah), which depends on intellect, and they lack intellect.
C) There is a consensus (ijma') that zakat is not due on them.
D) The Prophet explicitly exempted them in a sahih hadith.

Key Takeaway
Zakat is not obligatory on orphans and insane persons because it is an act of worship ('ibadah) requiring intention, which they cannot perform; the Shafi'i proofs are refuted through hadith criticism and the distinction between 'ibadah and mu'nat.

Zakat — Almsgiving

Zakat on a Majnun Who Recovers During the Year
Hanafi ruling and intra-school dispute on zakat for a majnun

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakat for a majnun who recovers during the year, identify the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf, and apply the ruling to scenarios of original and temporary insanity.

Core Idea
Any recovery of sanity during the zakat year, however brief, makes zakat wajib — just as a moment of sanity in Ramadan obligates the whole month's fast.

The obligation of zakat depends on ownership of nisab for a full lunar year while the owner is legally responsible (mukallaf). What happens when the owner is insane for part of that year? The Hanafi school discusses this with a precise analogy to fasting in Ramadan. This lesson unpacks the ruling from Al-Hidayah, including the difference between original and temporary insanity and the intra-Hanafi difference on whether a partial recovery suffices.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the obligation of zakat on a majnun (insane person) who owns nisab and recovers sanity (ifaqah) during the zakat year. Determine the hukm level (wajib or not) and the condition that triggers it.
The ruling is not absolute; it depends on the type of insanity and the duration of recovery.
2
State the main Hanafi position and its qiyas
The author of Hidayah (representing the relied-upon view) holds that if a majnun recovers for any part of the year, even a short time, zakat becomes wajib. This is analogous to recovering during Ramadan: a moment of sanity obligates the entire month's fast.
The qiyas is on the obligation of fasting (fard) – zakat is wajib, but the same principle applies.
3
Present Abu Yusuf's opposing view
Imam Abu Yusuf considers the majority of the year. If the person was insane for more than half the year, he is treated as insane for the whole year and no zakat is due. If sane for more than half, zakat is wajib.
Abu Yusuf's view changes the outcome significantly in border cases.
4
Distinguish between original and temporary insanity
Original insanity (junun asli) is when one reaches puberty already insane. Temporary insanity (junun 'aridi) is when one becomes insane after puberty. For original insanity, Abu Hanifa holds that the zakat year begins only from the time of recovery, like a minor reaching puberty.
This is an additional nuance even within the majority view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Under Abu Hanifa's general view, a one-day recovery mid-year obligates zakat at year-end. Under Abu Yusuf, if insane for >50% of the year, no zakat. For original insanity, the year resets at recovery, so even if recovery is late, zakat is due only after a full year from recovery.
Knowing this difference helps in calculating zakat for individuals with intermittent mental health issues.

صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ نصاب کا مالک ہونے کے بعد مجنون کو اگر سال کے کسی حصہ میں افاقہ ہو گیا، خواہ سال کے اول میں خواہ آخر میں۔ افاقہ تھوڑے وقت رہا ہو یا زیادہ وقت تو اس پر زکوۃ واجب ہوگی۔ اور یہ ایسا ہے جیسے مجنون کو رمضان المبارک کے کسی جز میں، رات میں یا دن میں افاقہ ہو گیا ہو تو پورے رمضان کے روزے اس پر فرض ہو جائیں گے۔ حاصل یہ کہ زکوۃ کے لئے ایک سال ایسا ہے جیسے روزہ کے لئے ایک ماہ اور ماہ رمضان کے ایک جز میں افاقہ پورے ماہ کے روزے فرض ہونے میں ایسا ہے جیسے پورے ماہ افاقہ رہا ہو۔ پس اسی طرح سال کے کسی ایک جز میں افاقہ وجوب زکوۃ کے لئے ایسا ہے جیسے پورے سال افاقہ رہا ہو۔ اور پورے سال جنون سے افاقہ کی صورت میں زکوۃ فرض ہوتی ہے۔ لہذا سال کے ایک جز میں افاقہ ہونے کی صورت میں بھی زکوۃ فرض ہوگی۔ امام ابو یوسف سے روایت ہے کہ انہوں نے سال کے اکثر وقت کا اعتبار کیا ہے۔ پس اگر سال کے اکثر حصہ میں مجنون رہا تو پورے سال میں مجنون شمار ہو گا۔ اور اگر اکثر وقت افاقہ کی حالت میں رہا تو پورے سال با ہوش اور مفیق شمار ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ قسم سابق کے اندر جنون اصلی اور عارضی کے درمیان کوئی فرق نہیں ہے۔ یعنی اگر سال کے ایک جز میں مجنون کو افاقہ ہو گیا تو اس پر زکوۃ واجب ہوگی۔ خواہ وہ جنون اصلی میں مبتلا ہو یا جنون عارضی میں۔ جنون اصلی تو یہ ہے کہ وہ جنون ہی کی حالت میں بالغ ہوا ہے۔ اور جنون عارضی یہ ہے کہ بالغ تو ہوا ہے بحالت عقل لیکن بالغ ہونے کے بعد اس پر جنون طاری ہو گیا۔ حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ جنون اصلی کی صورت میں اس کو جس وقت افاقہ ہو گا اس وقت سے سال کا آغاز معتبر ہو گا۔ یعنی افاقہ کے بعد سے سال گذرنے پر زکوۃ فرض ہوگی۔ جیسے نابالغ بچہ مالدار ہے پھر وہ بالغ ہو گیا تو بالغ ہونے کے بعد جب سال پورا ہو جائے گا تب زکوۃ واجب ہوگی۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب بحالت جنون بالغ ہوا تو وہ عدم عقل کی وجہ سے احکام شرع کا مکلف ہی نہ ہوگا۔ ہاں جب افاقہ ہوا تو اب وہ مکلف ہو گیا اور اسی وقت سے اس پر احکام شرع لاگو ہوں گے۔ لہذا اس وقت سے جب سال پورا ہو جائے گا اس پر زکوۃ فرض ہو جائے گی۔
The author of Hidayah says: If a majnun (insane person) recovers (regains sanity) during any part of the year after becoming owner of nisab, whether at the beginning or end of the year, and whether the recovery is for a short or long time, then zakat becomes wajib upon him. This is like if a majnun recovers during any part of Ramadan, night or day, then the fasts of the entire Ramadan become fard upon him. The gist is that for zakat, one year is like for fasting, one month, and recovery in any part of Ramadan makes the whole month's fasts fard, as if he was sane the whole month. Similarly, recovery in any part of the year makes zakat wajib, as if he was sane the whole year. Because zakat is fard when there is recovery for the whole year, so also when there is recovery for a part. Imam Abu Yusuf has a narration that he considers the majority of the year. So if he was insane for most of the year, he is considered insane for the whole year; if he was sane for most of the year, he is considered sane for the whole year. The author of Hidayah says that in the previous section, there is no difference between original insanity (junun asli) and temporary insanity (junun 'aridi). That is, if a majnun recovers for any part of the year, zakat is wajib upon him, whether he had original insanity or temporary. Original insanity is when he reached puberty while insane. Temporary insanity is when he reached puberty with sanity but later became insane. Imam Abu Hanifa's madhhab is that in the case of original insanity, when he recovers, the year begins from that time. That is, after recovery, when a year passes, zakat becomes fard. Like a minor who possesses wealth then reaches puberty: after puberty, when a year is completed, zakat becomes wajib. The proof is that when he reached puberty while insane, he was not mukallaf due to lack of intellect. When he recovers, he becomes mukallaf, and from that time the rules of shari'ah apply. Therefore, from that time when a year passes, zakat becomes fard upon him.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the obligation of zakat on a majnun (insane person) who owns nisab and recovers during the zakat year. The main ruling (from the Hidayah) is that if a majnun recovers for any part of the year, even a small part, zakat becomes wajib on him. This is analogized to the case of Ramadan: if a majnun recovers during any part of Ramadan, he must fast the whole month. The principle is that the obligation attaches to the entire period as long as there is some presence of capacity. Then Imam Abu Yusuf is reported to hold that the majority of the year is considered: if he was insane for most of the year, no zakat; if sane for most, then zakat. Then the author clarifies that there is no difference between original insanity (junun asli, onset before puberty) and temporary insanity (junun 'aridi, onset after puberty). For both, recovery triggers the obligation. However, Imam Abu Hanifa qualifies that for a person with original insanity (who reached puberty in that state), the zakat year begins from the time of recovery, just as a minor who becomes wealthy then reaches puberty starts his zakat year from puberty. This is because before recovery, he was not mukallaf at all. This nuance shows the precision of Hanafi fiqh in applying the principle of obligation based on legal capacity.

Key Terms
جنون اصلی (Junun Asli): Original insanity: the person reaches puberty while already insane.
جنون عارضی (Junun 'Aridi): Temporary insanity: the person attains puberty with sanity but later becomes insane.
افاقہ (Ifaqah): Recovery of sanity; the moment the insane person regains intellect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hidayah, if a majnun who owns nisab recovers sanity for one day in the middle of the zakat year, then what is the ruling?
A) Zakat is not wajib because he was insane for most of the year.
B) Zakat is wajib because he recovered for a part of the year.
C) Zakat is wajib only if he recovers at the beginning of the year.
D) Zakat is wajib only if he recovers at the end of the year.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a majnun who recovers sanity at any point during the zakat year must pay zakat at year-end, with the special rule for original insanity that the year begins at recovery.

Zakat Not Obligatory on a Mukatab
Ruling stating that a mukatab is not required to pay zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakat for a mukatab and explain why his incomplete ownership precludes zakat.

Core Idea
A mukatab’s ownership is incomplete due to slavery, so zakat is not obligatory.

In this lesson, we examine the ruling on zakat for a mukatab—a slave who has contracted to buy his freedom. The passage clearly states that no zakat is due on his wealth, even if it reaches nisab, because his ownership is not complete. This ruling is a direct application of the Hanafi principle that zakat requires full, unrestricted ownership (milk al-tamm) for a full year.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and ruling
The passage states that the mukatab is not liable for zakat.
The ruling is absolute: no zakat even if he has nisab.
2
Understand the reason
Because he is not a complete owner (malik min kulli wajh) due to the existence of slavery (manafi al-milk).
Slavery is a repugnant element that mars full ownership.
3
Connect to broader principle
Zakat requires full ownership. The mukatab’s ownership is contingent on completing payment, so it's not full.
Hanafi condition: zakat only on fully owned wealth.
4
Apply the analogy
The passage also mentions he cannot free his own slave, further proving his limited ownership.
If he cannot free a slave, his ownership is not complete.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَيْسَ عَلَى الْمُكَاتَبِ زَكوةً لِأَنَّهُ لَيْسَ بِمَالِك مِنْ كُلِّ وَجْهِ لِوُجُودِ الْمَنَافِي وَهُوَ الرّقُ وَلِهَذَا لَمْ يَكُنْ مِنْ أَهْلِ ان يعتق عبده

ترجمہ اور مکاتب پر زکوۃ نہیں ہے کیونکہ وہ من کل وجہ مالک نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے کہ منافی ملک یعنی رقیت موجود ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ وہ اپنے غلام کو آزاد کرنے کا اہل نہیں ہے۔ تشریح مکاتب پر زکوۃ فرض نہیں ہے۔ اگرچہ اس کے پاس بقدر نصاب مال موجود ہو دلیل یہ ہے کہ مکاتب اپنے مال کا من کل وجہ مالک نہیں ہے۔
And there is no zakat upon the mukatab (slave in contract of manumission) because he is not an owner from every aspect, due to the existence of the repugnant element, which is slavery. For this reason, he is not eligible to free his own slave.

Translation: And no zakat on the mukatab because he is not a full owner; because the repugnant element to ownership, i.e., slavery, exists. This is why he is not eligible to free his own slave. Explanation: Zakat is not fard upon the mukatab, even if he possesses wealth equal to nisab, because the mukatab is not a full owner of his property.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement regarding the obligation of zakat upon a mukatab (a slave who has entered into a contract of manumission with his master, agreeing to pay a certain amount to earn his freedom). The ruling is that zakat is not wajib on him, even if he possesses wealth equal to or exceeding the nisab. The reason given is that he is not a complete owner (malik min kulli wajh) because slavery (riqq) is a repugnant element (manafi) that prevents full ownership. The proof offered is that a mukatab is not even allowed to free his own slave (if he owned one), which shows the limitation on his ownership. This ruling is consistent with the Hanafi principle that zakat requires full ownership of the property (milk al-tamm) for the entire year. A mukatab's ownership is incomplete because if he fails to pay, he remains a slave and his property belongs to his master. Therefore, he is not liable for zakat.

Key Terms
مکاتب (Mukatab): A slave who has made a contract with his master to pay a specified sum in installments in exchange for freedom; he remains a slave until fully paid.
منافی ملک (Manafi al-Milk): That which is repugnant to or prevents complete ownership; here, slavery (riqq).
مالک من کل وجہ (Malik min kulli wajh): Full owner in all respects; complete ownership with no restrictions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Because he is not a full owner due to the existence of slavery.
C) Because he is not a Muslim.
D) Because zakat is only payable by free adults.

Key Takeaway
A mukatab is not liable for zakat because his ownership is incomplete due to slavery; zakat requires full, unrestricted ownership.
