زکوۃ معروف ہو چکی اور یہ خطرہ بھی لاحق ہو گیا کہ سلاطین لوگوں کے مالوں پر ہوس کا ہاتھ پھیریں گے اس لئے مالکان مال کو نائب کر دیا کہ وہ اپنے مالوں کی زکوۃ خود ادا کریں ، پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ مال کا مالک کو ہ تیروں کو دینے میں امام مسلمین کا نائب ہے۔
Book of Zakat. Ashraf al-Hidaya Sharh Urdu Hidaya Volume Three. The author of Hidaya says: In the condition that the nisab of zakat remains, the debt of zakat prevents the obligation of zakat. Because paying the debt of zakat will reduce the nisab of zakat. The scenario is: A person owns two hundred dirhams and a year passes over them. But he did not pay zakat until a second year also passed. Then the zakat of the second year will not be obligatory. Because the obligation of the first year's zakat prevents the obligation of zakat in the second year. Because extracting the first year's zakat, i.e., five dirhams, reduces the nisab. And it is obvious that zakat is not obligatory on less than nisab. And the same ruling applies after complete destruction of wealth. That is, a person owned two hundred dirhams and a year passed over them. Then before giving zakat, he destroyed the entire nisab along with the zakat. Then he acquired two hundred dirhams and a year passed over them, then zakat on this acquired two hundred dirhams will not be obligatory because the obligation of the first nisab's zakat is a debt upon him. And the debt of zakat also prevents the obligation of zakat. This detail is according to the majority. Imam Zufar opposes in both cases, i.e., in the nisab where zakat became obligatory but was not paid until the second year passed, and in the nisab where zakat became obligatory but the entire nisab was destroyed, then he became owner of nisab and a year passed. The conclusion is that according to Imam Zufar, in both cases the debt of zakat does not prevent the obligation of zakat. Imam Zufar's proof is that the debt of zakat is a loan for which no one from the servants makes a claim. Thus it becomes like the debt of a vow and the debt of expiation. And a debt for which no one from the servants makes a claim does not prevent the obligation of zakat. Hence, the debt of zakat and the debt of destroyed property will both not prevent the obligation of zakat. Imam Abu Yusuf opposes us in the second case. That is, the debt of the first year's zakat prevents the obligation of zakat in the second year. But if after the passing of the year, he destroyed the entire nisab, then became owner of two hundred dirhams and a hawl passed, then the debt of zakat of the destroyed property will not prevent the obligation of zakat in the second year. The reason for the difference is that for the debt of destroyed property (mustahlak), i.e., after the passing of the hawl if he destroys the entire nisab, then there is no one from the servants to claim its zakat. In contrast, if the nisab is present and after the passing of the hawl he did not pay zakat, then the collector and the zakat receiver can claim its zakat. Since in this case there is a claimant from the servants, this debt of zakat prevents the obligation of zakat for the next year, and since the debt of destroyed property has no claimant from the servants, it will not prevent. The proof of the majority is that there is a claimant for the debt of zakat, and that claimant is the Imam of the Muslims for grazing animals, and for other trade wealth his deputy. But if it is said that the Imam does not have a deputy coming to ask for zakat of grazing animals nor for zakat of trade wealth, the answer is that the Imam of the Muslims himself gave permission to the owners. So the owners of wealth themselves are the deputies of the Imam. In this manner, the owner, in extracting zakat, is the owner of zakat, and in giving this zakat to the poor, he is the deputy of the Imam. And its origin is the saying of Allah Most High: "Take from their wealth charity" (at-Tawbah: 103). By this verse, the right to take zakat from every wealth is established for the Imam. This is why the Messenger of Allah (may Allah bless him and grant him peace) and his grandfather as-Siddiq al-Akbar and al-Faruq al-A'zam used to take zakat from animals, currency, and trade wealth and spend it in rightful avenues. But when the caliphate of Uthman began, he saw that zakat had become well-known among Muslims and also the danger arose that rulers would covet people's wealth, so he made the owners of wealth deputies that they themselves give zakat of their wealth. Thus it became established that the owner of wealth is the deputy of the Imam of the Muslims in giving zakat.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of unpaid zakat debt (dain al-zakat) on the obligation of zakat in subsequent years. The author of Hidayah, following Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, rules that the existence of an unpaid zakat debt from a previous year prevents the obligation of zakat for the following year, even if the nisab is still present. The reasoning is that the unpaid zakat is considered a debt (dain) on the owner, and since zakat is not obligatory on less than nisab, the debt effectively reduces the nisab. This applies both when the nisab remains intact and when it is destroyed after the hawl. Imam Zufar disagrees in both cases, arguing that zakat debt has no human claimant (unlike other debts), so it does not act as a barrier. Imam Abu Yusuf partially agrees with the majority: he holds that zakat debt prevents future obligation as long as the nisab is still present (since the imam or his deputy can claim it), but if the nisab has been destroyed, there is no claimant, so the debt does not prevent. The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) rebut Zufar and Abu Yusuf by proving that there is indeed a human claimant: the imam of the Muslims, who either collects personally or delegates the authority to the owners themselves. They cite the Quranic verse (al-Tawbah 103) and the practice of the Prophet and the early caliphs. Uthman's delegation to the owners is seen as making them deputies. Thus, the relied-upon position (al-mufta bihi) is that dain al-zakat is a valid impediment (mani') to future zakat obligation. This has practical implications: a person who has not paid zakat for several years cannot simply start paying from the current year; the past unpaid zakat remains a debt and affects the obligation until cleared.

Key Terms
دین زکوۃ (dain al-zakat): The unpaid obligation of zakat considered as a debt on the owner after the hawl has passed.
نصاب (nisab): The minimum amount of wealth that triggers the obligation of zakat.
حولان حول (hawalan al-hawl): The passing of one lunar year over the nisab.
مانع (mani'): A legal impediment that prevents the obligation or validity of an act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, if a person does not pay zakat for two years while the nisab remains, which years' zakat is wajib?
A) Both years are wajib
B) Only the first year is wajib; the second year is not due until the first is paid
C) Neither year is wajib
D) Only the second year is wajib

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, unpaid zakat debt (dain al-zakat) acts as a mani' (impediment) to future zakat obligation because it reduces the nisab and there is a human claimant (the imam or his deputy), a position upheld by the majority and relied upon for fatwa.

Zakat — Almsgiving

Exemption of Essential Items from Zakat: Primary Need and Non-Growth
Ruling with proof exempting items of primary need from zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rules for exemption from zakat based on primary need (hajat asliyyah) and non-growth (nami), and apply the distinction to tools of craftsmen.

Core Idea
Zakat is not due on items that serve a primary need and do not grow—this protects basic necessities from taxation.

The Hidayah lists specific items exempt from zakat: homes, clothes, furniture, riding animals, slaves for service, weapons, books for scholars, and tools of craftsmen. The exemption is based on two reasons: these items are occupied with primary need (they remove hardship) and they are not growing (nami). This lesson unpacks those reasons and shows how later Hanafi scholars applied them to distinguish between exempt consumables and zakatable trade goods.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories of exempt items
List the specific items mentioned in the text: residential homes, clothes, household furnishings, riding animals, slaves for service, weapons for use, books of knowledge for scholars, and tools of craftsmen.
These are all items of personal or professional use, not held for trade.
2
Extract the dual reason for exemption
The text gives two reasons: (1) they are occupied with primary need, and (2) they are not growth (nami). Both must be present to prevent zakat.
Primary need is defined as that which removes human destruction and hardship.
3
Define 'primary need' (hajat asliyyah)
From the commentary: primary need removes destruction or hardship, whether actual (e.g., hunger) or estimated (e.g., potential need).
This is a broad concept covering all essential necessities.
4
Define 'non-growth' (nami)
The commentary explains that growth can be intrinsic (like gold and silver) or through trade (like trade goods). The exempt items are neither.
If an item is held for trade, it becomes nami and potentially zakatable.
5
Apply to tools of craftsmen with the consumable distinction
The commentary adds a nuance: if raw materials are consumed and do not remain in the final product (e.g., soap for washing), they are exempt. But if they remain and add value (e.g., dye for fabric), they become trade goods and are zakatable if they reach nisab.
This illustrates the practical application of the nami condition.

Source Text

رہائشی مکان ، استعمال کے کپڑے، گھر کے استعمال کا سامان ، سواری کے جانور ، خدمت کے غلام، استعمال کے ہتھیار، علماء کی کتابیں اور پیشہ وروں کے اوزاروں میں زکوۃ نہیں ہے
وَلَيْسَ فِي دُوَرِ السُّكْنى وَثِيَابُ الْبَدَنِ وَآثَاتُ الْمَنَازِلِ وَدَوَابُ الرُّكُوبِ وَعَبِيدُ الْخِدْمَةِ وَ سَلَاحُ الْإِسْتِعْمَالِ زَكَوةً لأنَّهَا مَشْعُولَة بِالْحَاجَةِ الْأَصْلِيَّةِ وَلَيْسَتْ بِنَامِيَةٍ أَيْضًا وَعَلَى هَذَا كتُبُ الْعِلْمِ لِأهْلِهَا وَالاتُ الْمُحترفين لما قلنا ترجمہ اور زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہے رہنے کے گھروں میں ، بدن کے کپڑوں میں گھر کے اثاثہ میں سواری کے جانوروں میں، خدمت کے غلاموں میں ، استعمال کے ہتھیاروں میں۔ کیونکہ یہ چیزیں اصلی حاجت میں مشغول ہیں ۔ اور یہ چیزیں نامی بھی نہیں ہیں اور اسی حکم پر علم کی کتابیں اہل علم کے واسطے ہیں اور اسی حکم پر اہل حرفہ کے آلات ہیں ۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ متن میں مذکورہ چیزوں کے اندر زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ چیزیں اصلی حاجت میں مشغول ہیں۔ اصلی حاجت اس کو کہتے ہیں کہ جس سے انسانی ہلاکت اور تکلیف دور ہو۔ خواہ حقیقیہ خواہ تقدیر ا۔ اور یہ چیزیں نامی بھی نہیں ہیں۔ حاصل یہ کہ حاجت اصلی کے ساتھ مشغول ہونا اور نامی نہ ہوتا ان میں سے ہر ایک وجوب زکوۃ سے مانع ہے۔ پس جب یہاں دونوں باتیں ہیں تو بدرجہ اولی زکوۃ واجب نہ ہوگی۔ ان چیزوں کا اصلی حاجت کے ساتھ مشغول ہونا تو ظاہر ہے اور نامی نہ ہونا اس لئے ہے کہ نمو یا تو خلقی ( پیدائشی ) ہوتا ہے۔ جیسے سونے اور چاندی میں یا تجارت سے ہوتا ہے جیسے مال تجارت میں اور اس جگہ دونوں باتیں نہیں ہیں۔ اس لئے ہم نے کہا کہ مذکورہ چیزیں نامی نہیں ہیں۔ اسی طرح اگر اہل علم کے واسطے علم کی کتابیں ہوں تو ان میں زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہے۔ عبارت میں اہل علم کی قیدا اتفاقی ہے کیونکہ اگر کسی جاہل کے پاس کتابیں ہوں اور تجارت کے لئے نہ ہوں تو ان میں بھی زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہے۔ یہی حکم اہل حرفہ کے آلات کا ہے۔ جیسے حلوائی کی دیگیں، بڑھتی اور گھڑی ساز کے آلات وغیرہ ان میں زکو نہیں ہے۔ بعض حضرات نے کہا ہے کہ آلات حرفہ میں سے وہ چیزیں جن کا اثر بنائی ہوئی چیزوں پر باقی نہیں رہتا۔ جیسے صابن اثنان دھوبی نے خریدا، اور نان بائی نے روٹیوں کے لئے نمک اور لکڑی خریدی تو ان چیزوں میں زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہوگی۔ اور اگر بنائی ہوئی چیزوں میں اثر باقی رہتا ہے جیسے انگریز نے کسم ، زعفران اور رنگ خریدا تا کہ اجرت لے کر لوگوں کے کپڑے رنگے ۔ اور اس پر سال گذر گیا تو ان چیزوں میں زکوۃ واجب ہوگی۔ بشر طیکہ یہ چیزیں نصاب کی مقدار کو پہنچ گئی ہوں ۔
There is no zakat on residential homes, clothes of the body, household furnishings, riding animals, slaves for service, weapons for use. Because they are occupied with primary need and are also not growth (nami). And similarly, books of knowledge for scholars and tools of craftsmen follow the same ruling. Translation: And zakat is not obligatory on residential homes, clothes of the body, household furnishings, riding animals, slaves for service, weapons for use. Because these things are occupied with primary need. And these things are also not growth. And similarly, books of knowledge for scholars and tools of craftsmen follow the same ruling. Explanation: The issue is that zakat is not obligatory on the items mentioned in the text. Because these things are occupied with primary need. Primary need is defined as that which removes human destruction and hardship, whether actual or estimative. And these things are also not growth. The conclusion is that being occupied with primary need and not being growth, each of these prevents the obligation of zakat. So when both are present, zakat is even more not obligatory. That these things are occupied with primary need is obvious. And their not being growth is because growth is either natural (intrinsic) like in gold and silver, or through trade like in trade goods, and here both are absent. Therefore we say that the mentioned items are not growth. Similarly, if there are books of knowledge for a scholar, there is no zakat on them. The condition "for scholars" in the text is incidental, because if an ignorant person has books and they are not for trade, there is also no zakat. The same ruling applies to tools of craftsmen, like the pots of a confectioner, the tools of a carpenter and a watchmaker, etc., there is no zakat on them. Some esteemed scholars have said: Among tools of craftsmen, items whose effect does not remain on the manufactured goods, like the soap and ashes a washerman buys, and the salt and wood a baker buys for breads, there is no zakat on these things. But if the effect remains on the manufactured goods, like a dyer buys sumac, saffron, and dye to dye people's clothes for wages, and a year passes over them, then zakat is obligatory on these things, provided they reach the quantity of nisab.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This is a ruling statement with proof regarding items that are exempt from zakat. The text lists residential homes, clothes, household items, riding animals, slaves for service, weapons for use, books of knowledge for scholars, and tools of craftsmen. Two reasons (illah) are given for exemption: (1) These items are occupied with primary need (hajat asliyyah) – meaning they are essential for human survival and well-being, removing destruction and hardship. (2) They are not growth (nami) – they do not naturally increase nor are they held for trade. Both conditions must be present to prevent zakat. The commentary clarifies that the condition 'for scholars' is incidental; even an unlearned person's books not for trade are exempt. For tools of craftsmen, there is a further distinction: if the raw material is consumed and does not remain in the final product (like soap for washing), it is not zakatable; but if it remains and increases value (like dye for coloring), it becomes trade goods and is zakatable if it reaches nisab. This illustrates the Hanafi principle that zakat is only on growing wealth (mal nami).

Key Terms
حاجت اصلیہ (hajat asliyyah): Primary need that removes human destruction and hardship, whether actual or estimated.
نامی (nami): Growing or increasing, either intrinsically (like gold) or through trade.
آلات حرفہ (alat al-hirfah): Tools of a craft or profession used for livelihood.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hidayah, which of the following is a reason for exemption of residential homes from zakat?
A) They are not owned by the resident
B) They are not growth (nami)
C) They are too expensive
D) They are rented out

Key Takeaway
Items of primary need that do not naturally grow or appreciate are exempt from zakat, but when such items are acquired for trade, they become zakatable.

Zakat on Debt After Denial and Confession
Ruling with proof and ikhtilaf on zakat obligation for past years when debtor denies and later confesses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakat for past years when a debtor denies and later confesses, and explain why the Hanafi school differs from Imam Zufar and al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
No zakat on hidden wealth (mal al-simar) — lack of access prevents obligation even after the debt is proven.

When a debt is denied for years, the creditor has no effective access to the wealth. According to the Hanafi school, zakat is not due for those past years, even if the debt is later proven. This principle is based on the category of mal al-simar (hidden wealth). However, Imam Zufar and Imam al-Shafi'i disagree, arguing that the cause of zakat existed. This lesson unpacks the dispute, the proofs, and the practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify the exact ruling: for a debt denied for years and later proven by evidence, zakat is not wajib for the past years.
The ruling applies to the past period; zakat is due only for the year of recovery.
2
Identify the opponents and their position
Imam Zufar (within Hanafi) and Imam al-Shafi'i hold that zakat is due for all past years once the debt is proven.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
3
Analyze the opposing proof
Their argument: the sabab (cause) of zakat – ownership of nisab for a year – was present; loss of physical possession does not negate obligation, analogized to the wealth of a traveler (ibn al-sabil).
Identify the key analogy.
4
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi school relies on the statement of Ali (ra): 'No zakat on mal al-simar (hidden wealth).' The debt, while denied, is inaccessible; possession (yad) is not established.
The Hanafi response distinguishes the traveler case: there, the wealth is still effectively in his possession via representatives.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: if a creditor recovers after 3 years of denial, Hanafi says pay zakat only for 1 year (recovery year); opponent says pay for all 3 past years.
This difference affects the amount of zakat owed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جس شخص کا دوسرے پر قرض ہو اور مدیون نے کئی برس کے قرضہ کا انکار کر دیا پھر اس پر بینہ قائم ہو گیا گذرے ہوئے ایام کی زکوۃ کا حکم
وَمَنْ لَهُ عَلَى آخَر دَيْن فَجَحَدَهُ سِنِينَ ثم قَامَتْ بِهِ بَيْنَةُ لَمْ يُرَكِهِ لِمَا مَضَى مَعْنَاهُ صَارَتْ لَهُ بَيْنَةٌ بِأَنْ أَفَرَّ عِندَ النَّاسِ وَهِيَ مَسْأَلَةُ المَالِ الصِّمَارِ وَفِيهِ خِلافُ رُفُو وَ الشَّافِعِى وَمِنْ جُمْلَتِهِ المَالُ المَفقود والابق والضال وَالْمَغْضُوبُ إِذَا لَمْ يَكُنْ عَلَيْهِ بَيْنَةٌ وَالْمَالُ السَّاقِط فِي الْبَحْرِ وَالْمَدْفُونُ فِي الْمَفَازَةِ إِذَا نَسِيَ مَكَانَهُ وَالَّذِي اَخَذَهُ السّلْطَانِ مُصَادِرَةً وَوُجُوبِ صَدَقَةِ الْفِطْرِ بِسَبَبِ الأَيْقِ وَالصَّالِ وَالْمَعْصُوبِ عَلَى هَذَا الخِلَافِ لَهُمَا أَنَّ لسَّبَبَ قَدْ تَحَقَّقَ وَفَوَاتُ الْيَدِ غَيْرُ مُحِلُّ بِالْوُجُوبِ كَمَالِ اِبْنِ السَّبِيلِ وَلَنَا قَوْلُ عَلَى لَا زَكَوةَ فِي مَالِ النِّمَارِ
The ruling regarding the person who has a debt on another, and the debtor denied the debt for several years, then a witness (bayyinah) is established against him: zakat is not required from him for the past period. Meaning that a witness became available for him, such that he confessed among people. This is the issue of mal al-simar (hidden wealth). In this, there is difference of opinion with Zufar and al-Shafi'i. Included in this category are lost wealth, runaway slaves, stray animals, usurped property when there is no witness over it, wealth that falls into the sea, wealth buried in the desert when its location is forgotten, wealth taken by the ruler through confiscation, and the obligation of sadaqat al-fitr due to slaves, and [illegible]. According to this difference, their argument is that the cause (sabab) has been actualized, and loss of possession does not vitiate the obligation, like the wealth of the wayfarer (ibn al-sabil). And our proof is the statement of Ali: 'There is no zakat on hidden wealth (mal al-simar).'
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage deals with a scenario where a creditor has a debt on another person, and the debtor denies it for years. Later, a witness (bayyinah) is established, but the ruling is that the creditor does not have to pay zakat for the past years on that debt. The reason is that until the debt is acknowledged or proven, the creditor had no effective access (yad) to the wealth; it was not in his possession. This is known as the issue of mal al-simar (hidden or inaccessible wealth). The text mentions that this is disputed by Imam Zufar and Imam al-Shafi'i. They argue that the cause of zakat (possession of nisab for a year) was present in principle, and loss of physical possession (fawat al-yad) should not negate the obligation, similar to the wealth of a traveler (ibn al-sabil) who may be absent but still owes zakat. However, the Hanafi school relies on the statement of Ali (may Allah be pleased with him): 'There is no zakat on hidden wealth (mal al-simar).' This hadith establishes that if the wealth is not effectively in one's control, zakat is not due for the past period. The commentary then lists analogous cases: lost property, runaway slaves, stray animals, usurped property without evidence, wealth fallen into the sea, buried and forgotten wealth, and goods confiscated by a ruler. All these fall under the same principle. The passage also notes that this difference applies to sadaqat al-fitr due to slaves? (The text is unclear). The relied-upon Hanafi position is that zakat is not obligatory for past years on such inaccessible debts.

Key Terms
مال الصمار (mal al-simar): Hidden or inaccessible wealth, such as a debt that is denied or lost property without proof.
بینہ (bayyinah): Legal proof or testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a debtor denies a debt for three years and then a witness is established, when must the creditor pay zakat on that debt?
A) For all three past years
B) Only for the current year after recovery
C) For the first year only
D) Zakat is never obligatory on debts

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school exempts zakat for past years on a debt that was denied, based on the principle of mal al-simar and the hadith of Ali.

Zakat Exemptions for Items of Basic Need and Professional Tools
Ruling on zakat exemption for essential items and professional tools

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which items are exempt from zakat due to basic need and non-growth, and apply the distinction for professional tools.

Core Idea
Items of basic need and tools of trade are exempt from zakat because they are not growth assets.

Not every asset you own attracts zakat. The Hanafi school exempts items that are essential for daily living and do not naturally grow. This lesson unpacks the categories and the reasoning behind the exemption, including a critical distinction for craftsmen's tools.

Guided Path
1
List the exempt categories
Identify the six categories mentioned: residential homes, clothing, household furnishings, riding animals, servants, and weapons for use.
These are all mawquf bi al-hajah al-asliyyah (occupied by basic need).
2
Understand the twin conditions
Note that two conditions must be present for exemption: (1) the item is needed for basic survival or dignity, and (2) it is not a growth asset (namiyah).
Gold and silver are namiyah, so they are not exempt even if needed.
3
Extend the rule to books and professional tools
The same reasoning applies to scholars' books and craftsmen's tools—they are not growth assets and are needed for livelihood.
The phrase 'for their people' is explanatory, not restrictive.
4
Distinguish consumable vs. non-consumable tools
Items that are consumed in the work (e.g., soap for a laundress) are exempt, but items that retain their effect in the product (e.g., dye for a dyer) are zakatable if they reach nisab and a year passes.
This nuance is often overlooked.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَيْسَ فِي دُوَرِ السُّكْنى وَثِيَابُ الْبَدَنِ وَآثَاتُ الْمَنَازِلِ وَدَوَابُ الرُّكُوبِ وَعَبِيدُ الْخِدْمَةِ وَ سَلَاحُ الْإِسْتِعْمَالِ زَكَوةً لأنَّهَا مَشْعُولَة بِالْحَاجَةِ الْأَصْلِيَّةِ وَلَيْسَتْ بِنَامِيَةٍ أَيْضًا وَعَلَى هَذَا كتُبُ الْعِلْمِ لِأهْلِهَا وَالاتُ الْمُحترفين لما قلنا
There is no zakat on residential homes, body garments, household furnishings, riding animals, servants for service, weapons for use—because they are occupied with basic need and are not growth assets. And upon this rule are books of knowledge for their people and tools of professionals, due to what we said.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage states a clear ruling: zakat is not wajib on items that meet one's basic needs (حاجة أصلية) and are not growth assets (نامية). These include the six categories listed in the matn: residential homes, clothing, household goods, riding animals, servants, and weapons for personal use. The reason is twofold: (1) these items are consumed by the basic need (human survival and prevention of hardship) and (2) they do not naturally grow (نمو نہیں) like gold, silver, or trade goods. The same rule extends to scholars' books and craftsmen's tools—e.g., a cook's pots, a carpenter's tools, or a watchmaker's instruments. The commentator notes that the condition 'for their people' is incidental; even an ignorant person's books (if not for trade) are exempt. However, there is a distinction for craftsmen: items that are consumed in the process (e.g., soap for a laundress, salt for a baker) are exempt, but items that retain their effect in the finished product (e.g., dye for a dyer) are zakatable if they reach nisab and a year passes. This is a standard Hanafi ruling from the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
حاجة أصلية (hājah aṣliyyah): Basic need that prevents human destruction or severe hardship, whether actual or by estimation.
نامية (nāmiyah): Growth asset—either naturally (like gold/silver) or through trade (like trade goods).
آلات المحترفين (ālāt al-muḥtarifīn): Tools of professionals/craftsmen used in their trade.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is NOT exempt from zakat?
A) A scholar's personal library of academic books
B) A carpenter's tools used for his trade
C) Dye purchased by a dyer for coloring customers' clothes, kept for a year
D) A riding horse for personal transport

Key Takeaway
Zakat is not due on items that are mawquf bi al-hajah al-asliyyah and ghayr namiyah; but trade tools that retain effect in the product are zakatable.

Zakat on Denied Debt and Missing Property (Mal al-Dhimar)
Ruling on zakat for missing property and denied debts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakat for mal al-dhimar and explain why the owner's power to dispose (qudrat al-tasarruf) is decisive.

Core Idea
Zakat is not due on property the owner cannot access or dispose of—mal al-dhimar is exempt.

This lesson examines a key Hanafi ruling on zakat for property that is missing or unattainable (mal al-dhimar). The passage clarifies that even if a denied debt is later proven, no zakat is owed for past years because the owner lacked the power to dispose—a condition the Hanafi school considers essential for zakat liability. We will explore the proof from the saying of Ali (radi Allahu anhu), the opposing views of Zufar and al-Shafi'i, and the intra-Hanafi differences on bankrupt debtors.

Guided Path
1
Define mal al-dhimar
Identify the types of property the passage lists as mal al-dhimar: denied debt without proof, lost property, absconding slave, stolen goods without evidence, property fallen into sea, buried property with forgotten location, and confiscated property.
The common feature is that recovery is not hoped for and the owner has no actual possession.
2
State the Hanafi ruling and its proof
The Hanafi school rules that no zakat is due on mal al-dhimar for past years. The proof is the saying of Ali (radi Allahu anhu): 'No zakat on mal al-dhimar.' Additionally, the school reasons that zakat requires growth (nama'), and growth requires the power to dispose (qudrat al-tasarruf), which is absent.
Note that the proof is a qawl sahabi, considered authoritative in Hanafi usul.
3
Understand the opposing view
Imam Zufar and Imam al-Shafi'i argue that zakat is due because the cause (sabab) of zakat—ownership of nisab—exists. Loss of possession does not negate obligation, analogous to a traveler's property which is zakatable because he can appoint a deputy.
Their dalil is based on qiyas, considered valid by them.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school rebuts by distinguishing the traveler's case: the traveler can dispose through his deputy (niyabah), whereas the owner of mal al-dhimar cannot authorize anyone because the property is out of reach. Hence, the analogy fails.
This distinction hinges on the concept of qudrat al-tasarruf.
5
Examine the intra-Hanafi difference on bankrupt debtor
For a debt owed by an acknowledging bankrupt debtor, Abu Hanifah holds zakat is due because the judge's declaration of bankruptcy (taflis) is invalid. Muhammad says no zakat because bankruptcy is realized. Abu Yusuf compromises: he agrees with Muhammad on the realization but with Abu Hanifah on the ruling, out of consideration for the poor.
This shows the internal flexibility of the school.

وَمَنْ لَهُ عَلَى آخَر دَيْن فَجَحَدَهُ سِنِينَ ثم قَامَتْ بِهِ بَيْنَةُ لَمْ يُرَكِهِ لِمَا مَضَى مَعْنَاهُ صَارَتْ لَهُ بَيْنَةٌ بِأَنْ أَفَرَّ عِندَ النَّاسِ وَهِيَ مَسْأَلَةُ المَالِ الصِّمَارِ وَفِيهِ خِلافُ رُفُو وَ الشَّافِعِى وَمِنْ جُمْلَتِهِ المَالُ المَفقود والابق والضال وَالْمَغْضُوبُ إِذَا لَمْ يَكُنْ عَلَيْهِ بَيْنَةٌ وَالْمَالُ السَّاقِط فِي الْبَحْرِ وَالْمَدْفُونُ فِي الْمَفَازَةِ إِذَا نَسِيَ مَكَانَهُ وَالَّذِي اَخَذَهُ السّلْطَانِ مُصَادِرَةً وَوُجُوبِ صَدَقَةِ الْفِطْرِ بِسَبَبِ الأَيْقِ وَالصَّالِ وَالْمَعْصُوبِ عَلَى هَذَا الخِلَافِ لَهُمَا أَنَّ لسَّبَبَ قَدْ تَحَقَّقَ وَفَوَاتُ الْيَدِ غَيْرُ مُحِلُّ بِالْوُجُوبِ كَمَالِ اِبْنِ السَّبِيلِ وَلَنَا قَوْلُ عَلَى لَا زَكَوةَ فِي مَالِ النِّمَارِ وَلأنَّ السَّبَب هُوَ المَالُ النَّامِيُّ  َولَانِمَاء إِلَّا بِالْقُدْرَةِ عَلَى التَّصَرُّفِ وَلَا قَدَرَةَ عَلَيْهِ وَابْنُ السَّبِيلُ يَقْدِرُ بَنَائِبِهِ وَالْمَدْفُونُ بِالْبَيْتِ نِصَابُ لِتَيْسِيرِ الوُصُولِ إِلَيْهِ وَفِي الْمَدْفُونِ فِي الْاَرْضِ اَوَ الْكَرَمِ اِخْتِلَافُ الْمَشَائِخِ وَلَوْ كَانَ الدَّيْنُ عَلَى مُقِرٌ مَلِنِى أَوْ مُعْسِر تَجِبُ الزَّكَوةُ لِإِمْكَانِ الْوُصُولِ إِلَيْهِ اِبْتِدَاءً أَوْ بِوَاسِطَةِ التَّحصيل وَكَذَا لَوْ كَانَ عَلَى جَاحِدٍ وَعَلَيْهِ بَيِّنَة أَو عَلِمَ بِهِ القاضِي لِمَا قَلْنَا وَلَوْ كَانَ عَلَى مُقِرٌ مُفْلِسٍ فَهُوَ نِصَابٌ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ لِأَنَّ تَفْلِيسَ الْقَاضِي لَا يَصِحُ عِنْدَهُ وَعِندَ مُحَمَّدٍ لَا يَجِبُ لَتَحَقَّقِ الْإِفُلَاسِ عِنْدَهُ بِالتَّفْلِيسِ وَاَبُوْ يُوسُفَ مَعَ مُحَمَّدٍ فِي تَحقَّقِ الْإِفْلَاسِ وَمَعَ أَبي حَنِيفَة فِى حُكْمِ الزَّكَوةِ رِعَايَةً لِجَانِبِ الْفُقَرَاءِ
And whoever has a debt upon another and he denies it for years, then a proof (bayyinah) is established against him, he will not give zakat for the past. Its meaning: he has a proof in that he confessed before people. This is the issue of mal al-dhimar. And there is a difference of opinion with Zufar and al-Shafi'i. And from its category: lost property, an absconding slave, a stray, a usurped property if there is no proof against him, property fallen into the sea, property buried in the desert if he forgot its place, and that which the Sultan took by confiscation. And the obligation of sadaqat al-fitr due to an absconding slave, a stray, and a usurped one is upon this difference. Their proof: the cause (sabab) has been realized, and loss of possession does not nullify obligation, like the property of a traveler (ibn al-sabil). And our proof: the saying of Ali: 'No zakat on mal al-dhimar.' And because the cause is growing property, and there is no growth except with power to dispose, and he has no power. And the traveler can dispose through his deputy. And property buried in the house is zakatable nisab because access is easy. And in property buried in the ground or garden, there is a difference among the mashayikh. And if the debt is upon an acknowledging wealthy or poor debtor, zakat is obligatory because access is possible initially or through collection. Similarly, if it is upon a denier and there is a proof against him or the judge knows of it, due to what we said. And if it is upon an acknowledging bankrupt debtor, then it is nisab according to Abu Hanifah, because the judge's declaration of bankruptcy is not valid in his view. And according to Muhammad, it is not obligatory because bankruptcy is realized in his view by the judge's declaration. And Abu Yusuf is with Muhammad in realization of bankruptcy, and with Abu Hanifah in the ruling of zakat, out of consideration for the poor.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on zakat for debts that have been denied for years and then proven, and extends to all forms of 'mal al-dhimar'—property that is missing and unlikely to be recovered. The ruling: zakat is not wajib for past years because the owner lacked power to dispose (qudrat al-tasarruf). This is a Hanafi position opposed by Imam Zufar and Imam al-Shafi'i, who argue that the cause (sabab) of zakat—ownership of nisab—exists, and loss of possession does not negate obligation, citing the analogy of a traveler's property (which is zakatable because he can appoint a deputy). The Hanafi rebuttal: the cause is growing property, and growth requires power to dispose; mal al-dhimar lacks such power. The traveler differs because he can dispose through a deputy. The passage then lists examples: lost property, absconding slaves, stolen goods without witnesses, property fallen into the sea, buried property if place forgotten, confiscated property. The same dispute applies to sadaqat al-fitr for such slaves. Further details: debt from a solvent or poor acknowledger is zakatable because access is possible. Debt from a denier with proof or judicial knowledge is zakatable. For a bankrupt acknowledger, Abu Hanifah says zakat is due because the judge's declaration of bankruptcy is invalid (his view: tahjir is not effective), while Muhammad says no zakat because bankruptcy is realized. Abu Yusuf holds a middle view: with Muhammad on realization but with Abu Hanifah on the ruling (zakat wajib) to favor the poor. This is an intra-Hanafi dispute noted in the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
مال ضمار (māl al-ḍimār): Property that is missing and its recovery is not hoped for; the owner owns the corpus but has no actual possession (yad).
قدرة التصرف (qudrat al-taṣarruf): Legal capacity to dispose of property, either directly or through a deputy.
تفليس (taflīs): Judge's declaration that a debtor is bankrupt, restricting his disposal of property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on zakat for a debt that has been denied for years and then proven?
A) Zakat is due for all past years because the cause existed
B) Zakat is not due for past years because it is mal al-dhimar
C) Zakat is due only for the current year
D) Zakat is due if the debtor was wealthy at the time

Key Takeaway
Zakat on missing property (mal al-dhimar) is not wajib due to the lack of power to dispose, distinguishing it from property that can be accessed.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate
10 min
The Ruling on Zakat for Mal al-Dhimar (Lost/Inaccessible Wealth)
Defines mal al-dhimar, provides examples, states the Hanafi ruling with proofs, and presents inter- and intra-madhhab disputes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define mal al-dhimar, state the Hanafi ruling that zakat is not wajib on it, explain the proofs (qawl sahabi and rational), and distinguish the intra-Hanafi positions on debt from a bankrupt debtor.

Core Idea
Mal al-dhimar is exempt from zakat because growth requires disposal power, and the traveler analogy fails.

This lesson unpacks mal al-dhimar — lost or inaccessible wealth with no hope of recovery. The Hanafi school exempts it from zakat for past years, even if later recovered. We examine the proofs from Imam Ali and Hasan al-Basri, the rational argument based on the condition of nama' (growth), and the rebuttal of the opposing view by Imam Zufar and Imam al-Shafi'i. The lesson also addresses the intra-Hanafi disagreement on debts owed by a bankrupt debtor.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition and examples
Read the definition of mal al-dhimar and the eight examples given in the commentary. Note that the corpus is owned but the owner has no disposal power.
The Arabic term 'dhimar' implies concealment and absence of hope.
2
State the Hanafi ruling and its proofs
The Hanafi ruling is that no zakat is due on mal al-dhimar for past years. The proofs are the saying of Imam Ali 'La zakata fi mal al-dhimar' and the report from Hasan al-Basri, plus rational reasoning: growth (nama') requires the ability to dispose, which is absent.
The proof is a qawl sahabi, which is zanni al-thubut but qati al-dalala.
3
Analyze the opposing view and its analogy
Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i argue that the cause of zakat (ownership of nisab) is present, and loss of possession does not negate obligation, analogizing to a traveler's wealth.
They consider the analogy valid because both involve absence of physical possession.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafi response distinguishes: a traveler can appoint a deputy to dispose, so nama' is possible. Mal al-dhimar completely lacks disposal power, so the analogy fails.
This distinction is critical: the traveler has a deputy (na'ib), while mal al-dhimar has none.
5
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on bankrupt debtor
For a debt owed by a bankrupt (muqirr mufallis), Abu Hanifa holds zakat is due because the judge's declaration of bankruptcy is invalid. Muhammad holds it is not due because bankruptcy is established by the judge. Abu Yusuf agrees with Muhammad on establishment but with Abu Hanifa on the ruling, out of consideration for the poor.
This affects the mufta bihi: many later scholars follow Abu Hanifa's view.

ولأنَّ السَّبَب هُوَ المَالُ النَّامِيُّ وَلَا نَمَاءَ إِلَّا بِالْقُدْرَةِ عَلَى التَّصَرُّفِ وَلَا قَدْرَةَ عَلَيْهِ وَابْنُ السَّبِيلِ يَقْدِرُ بِنَائِبِهِ وَالْمَدْفُونُ بِالْبَيْتِ نِصَابٌ لِتَيْسِيرِ الْوُصُولِ إِلَيْهِ وَفِي الْمَدْفُونِ فِي الْأَرْضِ أَوِ الْكَرْمِ اخْتِلَافُ الْمَشَائِخِ وَلَوْ كَانَ الدَّيْنُ عَلَى مُقِرٍّ مَلِيٍّ أَوْ مُعْسِرٍ تَجِبُ الزَّكَاةُ لِإِمْكَانِ نِصَابٌ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ لِأَنَّ تَفْلِيسَ الْقَاضِي لَا يَصِحُّ عِنْدَهُ وَعِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ لَا يَجِبُ لِتَحَقُّقِ الْإِفْلَاسِ عِنْدَهُ بِالتَّفْلِيسِ وَأَبُو يُوسُفَ مَعَ مُحَمَّدٍ فِي تَحَقُّقِ الْإِفْلَاسِ وَمَعَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ فِي حُكْمِ الزَّكَاةِ رِعَايَةً لِجَانِبِ الْفُقَرَاءِ. ترجمہ: اور جس کا دوسرے پر قرضہ ہے اور اس نے کئی برس قرضہ کا انکار کیا پھر اس پر بینہ قائم ہو گیا تو گذرے ایام کی زکوۃ نہ دے گا۔ اس کلام کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ اس کے گواہ ہو گئے بایں طور کہ مدیون نے لوگوں کے سامنے قرضہ کا اقرار کر لیا اور یہ مال ضمار کا مسئلہ ہے اور مالِ ضمار میں امام زفر اور امام شافعی کا اختلاف ہے اور منجملہ مال ضمار کے وہ مال ہے جو مفقود ہو گیا اور وہ غلام جو بھاگ گیا اور وہ جانور اور غلام جو بہک کر گم ہو گیا اور وہ مال جس کو کسی نے غصب کر لیا بشرطیکہ غاصب پر گواہ نہ ہوں اور وہ مال جو سمندر میں گر پڑا اور وہ مال جس کو جنگل میں دفن کیا جبکہ اس کی جگہ بھول گیا ہو اور وہ مال جس کو سلطان نے مالک سے جدا کر لیا ہو، اور بھاگے ہوئے غلام اور بھٹکے ہوئے غلام اور غصب کئے غلام کی طرف سے صدقۃ الفطر واجب ہونا اسی اختلاف پر ہے۔ امام زفر اور شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ صدقۃ الفطر کا سبب تو متحقق ہے اور رہا قبضہ کا فوت ہونا تو وہ وجوب کے لئے محل نہیں ہے جیسے مسافر کا مال۔ اور ہماری دلیل حضرت علی کا قول ہے کہ مال ضمار میں زکوۃ نہیں ہے اور اس لئے کہ سبب زکوۃ تو وہ مال ہے جو نامی ہو اور نمونہیں ہے مگر جبکہ تصرف کی قدرت ہو اور مالِ ضمار پر تصرف کی قدرت نہیں ہے اور مسافر کو اپنے نائب کے ذریعہ تصرف کی قدرت حاصل ہے اور جو مال کمرہ میں دفن ہو وہ نصاب زکوۃ ہے کیونکہ اس تک پہنچنا آسان ہے اور جو مال زمین یا باغ میں دفن ہو تو اس میں مشائخ کا اختلاف ہے اور اگر قرضہ کسی قرضدار مقر پر ہو خواہ وہ مالدار ہو یا تنگدست ہو تو زکوۃ واجب ہوگی کیونکہ اس کا قرضہ وصول کر لینا ممکن ہے یا تو ابتداء میں یا بواسطہ تحصیل کے۔ اور یوں ہی اگر قرضہ کسی منکر پر ہو اور اس پر گواہ موجود ہوں یا قاضی کو اس قرضہ کا علم ہو اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے بیان کی، اور قرضہ کسی مدیون مقر مفلس پر ہو تو یہ بھی ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک نصاب زکوۃ ہے کیونکہ قاضی کا اس کو مفلس کرنا ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک صحیح نہیں ہے اور امام محمد کے نزدیک ایسے قرضہ کی زکوۃ واجب نہ ہوگی کیونکہ امام محمد کے نزدیک قاضی کے مفلس کرنے سے افلاس متحقق ہو جاتا ہے اور امام ابو یوسف افلاس متحقق ہونے میں امام محمد کے ساتھ ہیں اور زکوۃ واجب ہونے میں ابو حنیفہ کے ساتھ میں فقراء کی رعایت کے پیش نظر۔ تشریح: اب تک ان لوگوں کا ذکر تھا جن پر زکوۃ واجب ہوتی ہے اور جن پر زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہوتی، اب یہاں سے ان اموال کا بیان ہے جن میں زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہوتی۔ اس مال کا نام جس میں زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہوتی مال ضمار ہے، ضمار کی اصل اضمار ہے اور اضمار کے لغوی معنی غائب کرنا اور چھپانا ہے۔ کہا جاتا ہے اضمر فی قلبه اس نے اپنے دل میں چھپا لیا۔ اور فقہاء کی اصطلاح میں مال ضمار وہ مال ہوتا ہے جو غائب ہو اور اس کے ملنے کی امید نہ ہو اور اگر اس کے ملنے کی امید ہو تو وہ مال ضمار نہیں کہلائے گا۔ بعض نے کہا ہے کہ مال ضمار وہ مال ہے جس کا رقبہ تو موجود ہو مگر مالک اس سے نفع اٹھانے پر قادر نہ ہو کیونکہ مال ضمار میں رقبہ تو مالک کا مملوک ہوتا ہے مگر ید مملوک نہیں ہوتا۔ مال ضمار کی صورتیں: مصنف نے مال ضمار کی متعدد صورتیں ذکر کی ہیں (۱) ایک شخص کا دوسرے پر قرضہ ہے۔ قرضدار چند سال تک اس قرضہ کا انکار کرتا رہا اور قرض خواہ اس عرصہ گواہوں سے محروم رہا، چند سال گذرنے کے بعد گواہ میسر آئے اس طور پر کہ قرضدار نے لوگوں کے سامنے قرضہ کا اقرار کر لیا تو یہ لوگ قرض خواہ کے اقراری گواہ ہو گئے۔ یعنی یہ لوگ اس پر گواہ ہو گئے کہ قرضدار نے ہمارے سامنے قرضہ کا اقرار کیا ہے پس ان گواہوں کے قائم ہونے سے پہلے یہ قرضہ مالِ ضمار تھا اور گواہوں کے قائم ہونے کے بعد مال ضمار نہ رہا کیونکہ جب تک گواہ موجود نہ تھے تو اس قرضہ کے وصول ہونے کی کوئی امید نہ تھی لیکن جب گواہ دستیاب ہو گئے تو بذریعہ عدالت قاضی اس قرضہ کو وصول ہونا ممکن اور پر امید ہو گیا، (۲) گم شدہ مال، (۳) بھاگا ہوا غلام، (۴) وہ جانور اور غلام جو بہک کر گم ہو گیا، (۵) وہ مال جس کو کسی نے غصب کر لیا مگر مالک کے پاس غاصب کے خلاف گواہ نہ ہوں، (۶) وہ مال جو سمندر میں گر گیا ہو، (۷) وہ مال جس کو جنگل میں دفن کیا اور اس کی جگہ بھول گیا، (۸) وہ مال جس کو بادشاہ نے مالک سے جدا کر لیا ہو۔ اب سوال یہ ہے کہ مال ضمار جو چند سال تک مالک کے پاس سے غائب رہا اور اس عرصہ میں اس کے ملنے کی امید بھی نہ تھی پھر چند سال کے بعد یہ مال مل گیا تو ان گذشتہ چند سالوں کی زکوۃ واجب ہوگی یا نہیں ؟ سو اس بارے میں احناف کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ سنین گذشتہ کی زکوۃ واجب نہ ہوگی، اور امام زفر اور امام شافعی کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ زکوۃ واجب ہوگی۔ یہی اختلاف بھاگے ہوئے غلام، بھٹکے ہوئے غلام اور غصب کئے ہوئے غلام کی طرف سے صدقۃ الفطر واجب ہونے میں ہے چنانچہ ہمارے نزدیک مولیٰ پر ان کی طرف سے صدقۃ الفطر واجب نہ ہوگا۔ اور امام زفر اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک صدقۃ الفطر ان کی طرف سے واجب ہے۔ امام زفر اور امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مال ضمار میں زکوۃ واجب ہونے کا سبب یعنی نصاب نامی کا مالک ہونا موجود ہے اور جب وجوب زکوۃ کا سبب موجود ہے تو مال ضمار میں زکوۃ بھی واجب ہوگی۔ زیادہ سے زیادہ یہ کہا جا سکتا ہے کہ مالِ ضمار پر مالک کا قبضہ فوت ہے۔ سو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ قبضہ کا فوت ہونا وجوب زکوۃ کے لئے محل نہیں ہے۔ جیسے مسافر کا مال کہ حالت سفر میں اس کے قبضہ میں نہیں حالانکہ بالاتفاق اس پر صدقۃ الفطر بھی واجب ہے اور زکوۃ بھی واجب ہے۔ ہماری دلیل حضرت علی کا قول لا زكوة في مال ضمار ہے۔ یہی مضمون حسن بصری سے اس طرح منقول ہے: إذا حضر الوقت الذي يؤدي فيه الرجل زكوته أدى عن كل مال و عن كل دين إلا ما كان ضمارا لا يرجوه۔ یعنی جب وہ وقت آ جائے جس میں آدمی اپنی زکوۃ ادا کرے گا تو ہر مال اور ہر دین کی زکوۃ ادا کرے مگر اس مال کی جو ضمار ہو اور اس کی امید نہ ہو۔ ان دونوں قولوں سے ثابت ہوا کہ مال ضمار میں زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ امام شافعی اور امام زفر کا یہ کہنا کہ وجوب زکوۃ کا سبب پایا گیا ہمیں تسلیم نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ زکوۃ واجب ہونے کا سبب مطلقاً مال کا مالک ہونا نہیں ہے بلکہ مال نامی کا مالک ہونا وجوب زکوۃ کا سبب ہے۔ اور مال ضمار کے اندر یہ سبب غیر متحقق ہے کیونکہ نماء اس وقت پایا جائے گا جبکہ تصرف کی قدرت ہو اور مالِ ضمار پر تصرف کی قدرت نہیں ہے۔ پس جب تصرف کی قدرت نہیں تو اس میں نماء بھی متحقق نہ ہوگا۔ اور جب نماء نہیں پایا گیا تو مال ضمار مال نامی بھی نہ ہوگا اور جب مال ضمار نامی نہیں تو اس میں زکوۃ بھی واجب نہ ہوگی۔ و ابن السبيل يقدر بنائبه سے امام زفر اور امام شافعی کے قیاس کا جواب ہے۔ حاصل جواب یہ ہے کہ مال ضمار کو مسافر کے مال پر قیاس کرنا غلط ہے کیونکہ مسافر کو اپنے نائب کے ذریعے تصرف کی قدرت ہے جبکہ مال ضمار میں ایسی قدرت نہیں۔
And because the cause is growing wealth, and there is no growth except with the power to dispose, and there is no power over it, while the wayfarer has power through his deputy. And wealth buried in the house is nisab due to ease of access, and regarding wealth buried in the ground or vineyard there is disagreement among the mashayikh. If the debt is upon an acknowledged solvent or insolvent person, zakat is wajib due to possibility of access initially or through collection. Similarly if it is upon a denier and there is evidence against him or the judge knows about it, for what we said. If it is upon an acknowledged bankrupt, then it is nisab according to Abu Hanifa because the judge's declaration of bankruptcy is not valid in his view. According to Muhammad, it is not wajib because bankruptcy is established in his view by the judge's declaration. Abu Yusuf is with Muhammad regarding establishment of bankruptcy and with Abu Hanifa regarding the ruling of zakat out of consideration for the poor. Translation: And the one who has a debt on another and he denied the debt for several years, then evidence was established against him, he will not give zakat for the past years. This statement means that he had witnesses that the debtor admitted the debt in front of people, and this is the issue of mal al-dhimar. There is disagreement of Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i regarding mal al-dhimar. Among mal al-dhimar is lost property, a runaway slave, an animal or slave that strayed and got lost, property that was usurped provided there are no witnesses against the usurper, property that fell into the sea, property buried in a forest and its location forgotten, and property that the sultan separated from its owner. And the obligation of sadaqat al-fitr for a runaway slave, stray slave, and usurped slave depends on this same disagreement. The proof of Imam Zufar and Shafi'i is that the cause of sadaqat al-fitr is present, and the loss of possession is not a ground for obligation, like the wealth of a traveler. And our proof is the saying of Ali that there is no zakat on mal al-dhimar, and because the cause of zakat is wealth that is growing, and there is no growth except with power to dispose, and there is no power over mal al-dhimar. The traveler has power through his deputy. Wealth buried in a room is nisab because it is easy to access, and wealth buried in ground or garden has disagreement among the mashayikh. If the debt is upon an acknowledged debtor whether wealthy or insolvent, zakat is wajib because recovery is possible either initially or through collection. Similarly if the debt is upon a denier and there are witnesses against him or the judge knows about it, for the reason we stated. If the debt is upon an acknowledged bankrupt debtor, then this is also nisab according to Abu Hanifa because the judge's declaration of bankruptcy is not valid in his view. According to Imam Muhammad, zakat on such a debt is not wajib because bankruptcy is established by the judge's declaration. Imam Abu Yusuf is with Muhammad regarding establishment of bankruptcy and with Abu Hanifa regarding the ruling of zakat out of consideration for the poor. Commentary: Up to now the mention was of those upon whom zakat is wajib and those upon whom it is not. Now from here is the explanation of those properties on which zakat is not wajib. The name of this property on which zakat is not wajib is mal al-dhimar. The origin of dhimar is idhmar, and idhmar lexically means to hide and conceal. It is said 'adhmara fi qalbihi' meaning he hid it in his heart. In the terminology of jurists, mal al-dhimar is property that is absent and there is no hope of recovering it. If there is hope of recovery, it is not called mal al-dhimar. Some have said that mal al-dhimar is property whose corpus exists but the owner is not able to benefit from it because in mal al-dhimar the corpus is owned by the owner but the hand (control) is not owned. Examples of mal al-dhimar: The author mentioned multiple forms: (1) One person has a debt on another. The debtor denied the debt for several years and the creditor was without witnesses. After several years witnesses became available such that the debtor admitted the debt in front of people, so these people became witnesses of admission for the creditor. That is, they testified that the debtor admitted the debt in front of them. So before these witnesses, this debt was mal al-dhimar, and after witnesses it ceased to be mal al-dhimar because as long as there were no witnesses, there was no hope of recovering the debt, but when witnesses became available, through the court the judge could recover it, making it possible and hopeful. (2) Lost property. (3) Runaway slave. (4) Animal or slave that strayed and got lost. (5) Property usurped but the owner has no witnesses against the usurper. (6) Property that fell into the sea. (7) Property buried in a forest and its location forgotten. (8) Property that the king separated from its owner. Now the question is: if mal al-dhimar remained absent for several years with no hope of recovery, then after several years it is recovered, is zakat wajib for those past years or not? The madhhab of the Hanafis is that zakat for the past years is not wajib, while Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i's madhhab is that zakat is wajib. This same disagreement applies to sadaqat al-fitr for a runaway slave, stray slave, and usurped slave: according to us, the master is not obliged to pay sadaqat al-fitr on their behalf, while according to Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i, it is wajib. The proof of Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i is that the cause of zakat being wajib on mal al-dhimar is present, because one owns the nisab of growing property, and when the cause of obligation is present, then zakat is also wajib on mal al-dhimar. At most it can be said that possession of mal al-dhimar is lost. So the response is that loss of possession is not a ground for obligation, like the wealth of a traveler where it is not in his possession during travel, yet by agreement sadaqat al-fitr is wajib on him and zakat is also wajib. Our proof is the saying of Ali: 'La zakata fi mal al-dhimar' (No zakat on lost property). And this meaning is also transmitted from Hasan al-Basri: 'When the time comes for a man to pay his zakat, he pays zakat on every property and every debt except what is dhimar that he does not hope to recover.' That is, when the time comes for a person to pay his zakat, he pays zakat on every property and every debt except that property which is dhimar and he has no hope of it. From these two sayings it is established that zakat is not wajib on mal al-dhimar. The second proof is that we do not accept the claim of Imam Shafi'i and Imam Zufar that the cause of zakat obligation is present. Because the cause of zakat being wajib is not absolutely owning property, but owning growing property is the cause. And in mal al-dhimar this cause is unfulfilled because growth occurs only when there is power to dispose, and there is no power to dispose over mal al-dhimar. So when there is no power to dispose, growth is not realized. And when growth is not present, mal al-dhimar is not growing property. And when mal al-dhimar is not growing, then zakat is not wajib on it. And the phrase 'wa ibn al-sabil yaqdiru bina'ibihi' is a response to the analogy of Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i. The conclusion is that qiyas of mal al-dhimar to the wealth of a traveler is incorrect because the traveler has power to dispose through his deputy, whereas such power does not exist in mal al-dhimar.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage is a complete exposition of the concept of mal al-dhimar (lost/inaccessible wealth) and the ruling of zakat upon it in the Hanafi school. The author begins by presenting the Arabic matn from the Hidayah, which states the principle: the cause of zakat is growing wealth, and growth requires the ability to dispose; since mal al-dhimar lacks this ability, zakat is not due. The matn then addresses specific cases: debts owed by an acknowledged debtor (solvent or insolvent) are subject to zakat because recovery is possible, as is a debt denied by the debtor if there is evidence or the judge's knowledge. However, a debt owed by a bankrupt debtor (declared bankrupt by the judge) creates an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa holds zakat is due because the judge's declaration of bankruptcy is invalid in his view, while Muhammad holds it is not due because bankruptcy is established by the judge's declaration. Abu Yusuf agrees with Muhammad on the establishment of bankruptcy but with Abu Hanifa on the ruling of zakat, out of consideration for the poor. Following the matn, the Urdu commentary (sharh) elaborates: it defines mal al-dhimar linguistically and terminologically, provides eight examples, and then presents the core dispute between the Hanafis (including Imam Zufar and Shafi'i). The Hanafi position is that no zakat is due on mal al-dhimar for past years when it is later recovered, based on the saying of Imam Ali ('La zakata fi mal al-dhimar') and the report from Hasan al-Basri, as well as rational reasoning: the cause of zakat is growing wealth, and growth requires the power to dispose, which is absent in mal al-dhimar. The opposing view (Zufar and Shafi'i) argues that the cause (ownership of nisab) is present, and loss of possession does not negate obligation, analogous to a traveler's wealth. The Hanafi response distinguishes: a traveler has a deputy with disposal power, whereas mal al-dhimar lacks any such power, so the analogy fails. This passage thus covers rulings with their proofs, multiple levels of dispute (inter-madhhab and intra-Hanafi), and the practical implications for zakat and sadaqat al-fitr on slaves.

Key Terms
مال ضمار (mal al-dhimar): Wealth that is absent and whose recovery is not hoped for; the corpus is owned but the owner has no disposal power (no yad).
نماء (nama'): Growth or potential for growth; a condition for zakat obligation according to the Hanafis.
مقر مفلس (muqirr mufalis): A debtor who acknowledges the debt but is declared bankrupt by the judge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, is zakat wajib on mal al-dhimar (lost/inaccessible wealth) for the years it was lost, if the property is later recovered?
A) Yes, because the cause of zakat (ownership of nisab) was present.
B) No, because the condition of growth (nama') requires the ability to dispose, which is absent in mal al-dhimar.
C) Yes, as an analogy to a traveler's wealth.
D) No, only if the loss was due to the owner's negligence.

Key Takeaway
Mal al-dhimar, wealth with no hope of recovery, is exempt from zakat for past years because the condition of growth (nama') requires actual disposal power, which is absent.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate
8 min
Zakat on Mal al-Dhimār: The Ḥanafī Position and Its Proofs
Dispute on zakat obligation for lost property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Ḥanafī ruling on zakat for mal al-dhimār and explain the two proofs (naqlī and ʿaqlī) that support it.

Core Idea
Zakat is not due on hopeless property because growth requires the power to dispose, which is absent.

This lesson examines a well-known dispute between the Ḥanafī school and Imām Zufar and Imām Shāfiʿī regarding zakat on property whose recovery is hopeless, such as a debt without witnesses. The Ḥanafīs argue that such property lacks the essential condition of being growing (māl nāmī) because the owner cannot transact with it. We will explore the textual evidence from ʿAlī and Ḥasan al-Baṣrī, as well as the rational argument concerning growth and power of disposal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key issue and the two positions
The issue is whether zakat is due for past years when mal al-dhimār is later recovered. State the Ḥanafī position (no zakat) and the opposing position (zakat is obligatory).
The same difference applies to Ṣadaqat al-Fiṭr for runaway slaves.
2
Examine the opposing proof (Imām Zufar and Shāfiʿī)
Their dalīl: ownership of a growing nisāb exists, and loss of possession does not remove obligation, analogizing to a traveler’s property.
3
Analyze the Ḥanafī naqlī proof
The sayings of ʿAlī (raḍiyallāhu ʿanhu) and Ḥasan al-Baṣrī explicitly exempt dhimār property. Determine the epistemological weight (zannī).
لا زكوة في ما ضمر and the statement from Ḥasan.
4
Analyze the Ḥanafī ʿaqlī proof
Growth (namāʾ) requires power of disposal; mal al-dhimār lacks such power, so it is not māl nāmī, hence no zakat.
5
Refute the opposing analogy
The traveler analogy is invalid because a traveler has power through a deputy, whereas mal al-dhimār does not.
‘wa ibn al-sabīl yuqaddaru bi-nāʾibihi’

کرے مگر اس مال کی جو ضمار ہو اور اس کی امید نہ ہو۔ ان دونوں قولوں سے ثابت ہوا کہ مال ضمار میں زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ امام شافعی اور امام زفر کا یہ کہنا کہ وجوب زکوۃ کا سبب پایا گیا ہمیں تسلیم نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ زکوۃ واجب ہونے کا سبب مطلقاً مال کا مالک ہونا نہیں ہے بلکہ مال نامی کا مالک ہونا وجوب زکوۃ کا سبب ہے۔ اور مال ضمار کے اندر یہ سبب غیر متحقق ہے کیونکہ نماء اس وقت پایا جائے گا جبکہ تصرف کی قدرت ہو اور مالِ ضمار پر تصرف کی قدرت نہیں ہے۔ پس جب تصرف کی قدرت نہیں تو اس میں نما بھی متحقق نہ ہوگا۔ اور جب نما نہیں پایا گیا تو مال مضمار مال نامی بھی نہ ہوگا اور جب مال ضمار نامی نہیں تو اس میں زکوۃ بھی واجب نہ ہوگی۔ و ابن السبيل يقدر بنائبہ سے امام زفر اور امام شافعی کے قیاس کا جواب ہے۔ حاصل جواب یہ ہے کہ مالِ معمار کو مسافر کے مال پر قیاس فاسد ہے۔ اس لئے کہ مال ضمار پر تصرف کی قدرت نہ بذات خود ہے اور نہ بذریعہ نائب کے۔ اور مسافر کو اپنے اس مال پر جو اس کے وطن میں ہے تصرف کی قدرت اگر چہ بذات خود نہیں لیکن بذریعہ نائب قدرت تصرف حاصل ہے۔ چنانچہ مسافر نے اگر اپنے مال میں سے کچھ بیچا تو جائز ہے کیونکہ مسافر اپنے نائب کے ذریعہ تسلیم مبیع پر قادر ہے۔ پس معلوم ہوا کہ مسافر کا مال ، مال نامی ہے اور مال ضمار نامی نہیں ہے۔ ایسی صورت میں امام زفر اور امام شافعی نغور کریں کہ اس عظیم فرق کے ہوتے ہوئے قیاس کس طرح درست ہو گا۔
[The debtor] kept denying the debt, and the creditor remained deprived of witnesses during this period. After several years, witnesses became available in such a way that the debtor confessed the debt in front of people, so these people became witnesses of confession for the creditor. That is, these people became witnesses that the debtor confessed the debt in front of us. So before these witnesses were established, this debt was mal al-dhimār, and after the witnesses were established, it was no longer mal al-dhimār, because as long as witnesses were not present, there was no hope of recovering this debt. But when witnesses became available, recovery through the court of the qāḍī became possible and hopeful. (2) Lost property, (3) A runaway slave, (4) An animal or slave that went astray and got lost, (5) Property that someone usurped but the owner has no witnesses against the usurper, (6) Property that fell into the sea, (7) Property buried in a jungle and its location forgotten, (8) Property that a king separated from its owner. Now the question is: If mal al-dhimār remained absent from the owner for several years and there was no hope of its recovery during that period, then after several years this property is found — is zakat due for those past years or not? In this regard, the madhhab of the Ḥanafīs is that zakat for the past years is not obligatory, and the madhhab of Imam Zufar and Imam Shāfiʿī is that zakat is obligatory. The same difference applies to the obligation of Ṣadaqat al-Fiṭr on behalf of a runaway slave, a stray slave, and a usurped slave. According to us, Ṣadaqat al-Fiṭr is not obligatory on the master on their behalf. According to Imam Zufar and Imam Shāfiʿī, Ṣadaqat al-Fiṭr is obligatory on their behalf. The proof of Imam Zufar and Imam Shāfiʿī is that the cause of zakat being obligatory in mal al-dhimār — i.e., ownership of a growing nisāb — exists, and when the cause of obligation exists, zakat will also be obligatory in mal al-dhimār. At most, it can be said that the owner's possession of mal al-dhimār is lost. The answer to this is that the loss of possession is not an obstacle to the obligation of zakat, like the property of a traveler which is not in his possession during travel, yet by consensus Ṣadaqat al-Fiṭr and zakat are obligatory on it. Our proof is the saying of ʿAlī: 'Lā zakāta fī mā ḍammara.' The same meaning is transmitted from Ḥasan al-Baṣrī: 'Idhā ḥaḍara al-waqtu alladhī yuʾaddī fīhi al-rajulu zakātahu addā ʿan kulli mālin wa ʿan kulli daynin illā mā kāna ḍimāran lā yarjūhu' — meaning when the time comes for a man to pay his zakat, he pays zakat on every property and every debt except the property that is dhimār and for which he has no hope. From both these sayings, it is established that zakat is not obligatory on mal al-dhimār. The second proof is that we do not accept the claim of Imam Shāfiʿī and Imam Zufar that the cause of zakat obligation exists. Because the cause of zakat obligation is not absolute ownership of property, but ownership of growing property (māl nāmī) is the cause. And in mal al-dhimār, this cause is not realized because growth (namāʾ) occurs only when there is power of disposal, and there is no power of disposal over mal al-dhimār. So when there is no power of disposal, growth is also not realized. And when growth is not found, mal al-dhimār is not growing property, and when it is not growing, zakat is not obligatory on it. The phrase 'wa ibn al-sabīl yuqaddaru bi-nāʾibihi' is the answer to the qiyās of Imam Zufar and Imam Shāfiʿī. The conclusion is that analogizing mal al-dhimār to the property of a traveler is invalid. Because over mal al-dhimār there is no power of disposal either personally or through a deputy. As for the traveler, although he does not have personal power of disposal over his property that is in his homeland, he does have power of disposal through a deputy. Thus, if the traveler sells something from his property, it is valid because he is able to deliver the sold item through his deputy. So it is known that the traveler's property is growing property, and mal al-dhimār is not growing property. In such a situation, how can the analogy be correct when this great difference exists?
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the obligation of zakat on mal al-dhimār (property whose recovery is hopeless). The text first defines mal al-dhimār with examples: a debt that cannot be recovered due to lack of witnesses, lost property, runaway slaves, usurped property without witnesses, property lost at sea, buried property whose location is forgotten, and property confiscated by a tyrant. The key issue: if such property is later recovered, is zakat due for the past years? The Ḥanafī position (Abū Ḥanīfa, Abū Yūsuf, Muḥammad) is that no zakat is due for the past years, while Imam Zufar and Imam Shāfiʿī hold it is obligatory. The same difference applies to Ṣadaqat al-Fiṭr for runaway slaves, etc. Imām Zufar and Shāfiʿī argue that the cause of zakat (ownership of a growing nisāb) exists, and loss of possession does not prevent obligation, analogizing to a traveler's property. The Ḥanafī response: first, they cite the saying of ʿAlī (raḍiyallāhu ʿanhu) 'Lā zakāta fī mā ḍammara' and a statement of Ḥasan al-Baṣrī that zakat is due on all property except that which is dhimār and hopeless. Second, they argue that the cause of zakat is not mere ownership but ownership of growing property, and growth requires power of disposal. Since mal al-dhimār lacks power of disposal (neither personally nor through a deputy), it is not growing property, and thus zakat is not due. The analogy to a traveler is rejected because a traveler has power of disposal through a deputy, whereas mal al-dhimār does not. Thus, the Ḥanafī position is supported by both textual evidence and rational argument.

Key Terms
مال ضمار (māl al-ḍimār): Property whose recovery is hopeless, such as a debt without witnesses, lost property, etc.
مال نامی (māl nāmī): Property that is capable of growth or increase, and over which the owner has power of disposal.
نماء (namāʾ): The potential for increase or profit, which requires the owner's power to dispose of the property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Ḥanafī school, what is the reason zakat is not due on mal al-dhimār?
A) The property is not owned by the person.
B) The property is less than nisāb.
C) The property lacks the potential for growth because the owner has no power of disposal.
D) The property is exempted by consensus.

Key Takeaway
Zakat is not due on mal al-dhimār because it lacks the potential for growth due to the absence of power of disposal.

Zakat on Buried Wealth: Room vs Land
Ruling on zakat for buried wealth with internal ikhtilāf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi ruling on zakat for wealth buried in a room versus in land and explain the internal dispute among the mashāyikh.

Core Idea
The obligation of zakat on buried wealth hinges on ease of access: a room makes it due, land is disputed.

This lesson examines a nuanced ruling from the Hidāyah regarding zakat on buried wealth. The text distinguishes between wealth buried in a fully possessed room, where zakat is clearly wajib, and wealth buried in a garden or land where the exact spot is forgotten, leading to a difference of opinion among later Hanafi scholars (mashāyikh). We will explore the reasoning behind each position and its reliance on the concept of mal al-ḍimār.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage presents two cases: (1) wealth buried in a room, and (2) wealth buried in owned land or a garden with forgotten location.
The room scenario is the base ruling from Hidāyah; the land scenario is an extension with scholarly dispute.
2
Understand the room scenario reasoning
The room is entirely in the owner's possession, making access easy. Thus the wealth is not mal al-ḍimār, and zakat is obligatory.
Key concept: mal al-ḍimār is wealth whose access is difficult or uncertain.
3
Analyze the land scenario dispute
Some mashāyikh argue that digging the entire land is possible, so power of disposal exists and zakat is due. Others argue that such digging constitutes hardship (ḥaraj), which the Sharīʿah removes, so zakat is not due.
Both arguments are based on the same principle but differ on the assessment of difficulty.
4
Note the absence of tarjīḥ
The text records the ikhtilāf without specifying which view is muftā bihī. This reflects the ongoing development of the school.
Later fatwa works may resolve this, but the passage leaves it open.
5
Apply the ruling to practice
In daily life, if you have wealth buried in a place you fully control (like a safe in your home), zakat is due. If buried in a large area with forgotten location, consult a scholar or follow the cautious view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کمرہ میں مدفون مال پر زکوۃ کا حکم : صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ جو مال کسی حجرہ میں مدفون ہو تو وہ نصاب زکوۃ ہے۔ یعنی اس مال میں زکوۃ واجب ہوگی۔ کیونکہ وہ حجرہ جمیع اجزاء کے ساتھ اس کے قبضہ میں ہے۔ اس لئے اس مال تک رسائی آسان ہے اور جب اس مال تک رسائی آسان ہے اور اس کا حاصل کرنا ممکن ہے تو یہ مال ، مال ضمار میں داخل نہ ہوگا۔ اور جب مال ضمار میں داخل نہیں تو اس میں زکوۃ بھی واجب ہوگی۔ اور اگر مال مملوکہ زمین یا باغ میں مدفون ہوا اور اس کی جگہ بھول گیا تو اس میں اختلاف مشائخ ہے۔ بعض نے کہا اس مال میں زکوۃ واجب ہے کیونکہ پوری نے مین کھود کر اس کو نکالنا ممکن ہے۔ اس لئے اس پر تصرف کی قدرت بھی حاصل ہے اور جب تصرف کی قدرت حاصل ہے تو یہ مال مضمار نہ ہو گا۔ اور بعض مشائخ نے کہا ہے کہ اس مال کی زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ پوری زمین کو کھود نا اگر چه مسعد رنہیں لیکن دشوار ضرور ہے، اور شریعت میں حرج کو دور کیا گیا ہے۔ اس لئے اس مال میں زکوۃ واجب نہ ہوگی۔
Ruling on wealth buried in a room: The author of Hidāyah says that wealth buried in a room is a zakatable nisāb. That is, zakat is obligatory on it. Because the room is in his possession in its entirety. Therefore access to this wealth is easy, and when it is easy to access and possible to obtain it, this wealth is not included in mal al-dhimār. And when it is not included in mal al-dhimār, zakat is obligatory on it. And if the wealth is buried in owned land or a garden and its location is forgotten, then there is a dispute among the mashāyikh. Some said zakat is obligatory on this wealth because it is possible to dig the whole land and extract it. Therefore, there is power of disposal over it, and when there is power of disposal, it will not be mal al-dhimār. And some mashāyikh said that zakat is not obligatory on this wealth because digging the entire land, although possible, is certainly difficult, and the Sharīʿah removes hardship. Therefore, zakat is not obligatory on this wealth.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on zakat for buried wealth and includes an internal ikhtilāf among later Ḥanafī scholars (mashāyikh). The text begins by stating the rule from the Hidāyah: wealth buried in one's room (ḥujrah) is subject to zakat because the owner has full possession of the room, making access easy. Hence, it is not mal al-dhimār. The difficulty arises when wealth is buried in owned land or a garden and its exact location is forgotten. The mashāyikh differ: some consider it still accessible through exhaustive digging, so power of disposal exists and zakat is due. Others consider the difficulty as constituting hardship (ḥaraj), and since the Sharīʿah removes hardship, they rule that zakat is not due. The text does not specify which view is muftā bihi, but it reflects the later development of the school.

Key Terms
مدفون (madfūn): Wealth that is buried, either in a room or in land.
حجرہ (ḥujrah): A room or chamber that is fully under the owner's possession.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling on zakat for wealth buried in a room?
A) Zakat is not obligatory because it is hidden.
B) Zakat is obligatory because the room is in the owner's possession and access is easy.
C) It is disputed among scholars.
D) Zakat is wajib only if the wealth exceeds nisāb for three years.

Key Takeaway
The obligation of zakat on buried wealth depends on whether the owner has easy access; wealth in a room is due, while wealth in land involves a difference of opinion among Hanafi scholars.
