Zakat on Debt: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Taflīs
Intra-Hanafi dispute on zakat after taflīs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on zakat of debt after the qāḍī's declaration of insolvency (taflīs) and identify the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Taflīs splits the Hanafi school: Abū Ḥanīfa sees it as invalid; the Sahibayn see it as effective.

The obligation of zakat on a debt depends on the possibility of recovery. When the debtor acknowledges the debt, recovery is possible even if he is poor, so zakat is wajib. But what happens when a judge declares the debtor insolvent? The Hanafi imams differ sharply on this point. This lesson walks through the base ruling and the internal disagreement.

Guided Path
1
State the base ruling on acknowledged debt
Identify the rule from Hidāyah: if the debtor acknowledges the debt, zakat is wajib regardless of his wealth or poverty.
The key concept is qudrat ḥukman (legal power), which prevents the debt from being mal al-dhimār.
2
Identify the point of disagreement
The dispute arises after the qāḍī formally declares the debtor insolvent (taflīs). Does this change the zakat obligation?
3
Follow Abū Ḥanīfa's reasoning
Abū Ḥanīfa holds that the qāḍī's taflīs is invalid. Since recovery is still possible through the debtor's earnings, zakat remains wajib.
He considers the debt still hopeful, like before the declaration.
4
Follow Muḥammad's reasoning
Muḥammad holds that taflīs is valid and effectively renders the debt like destroyed or denied property, so no zakat is due.
Abū Yūsuf agrees with Muḥammad on this point.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: after taflīs, Abū Ḥanīfa says the creditor must still pay zakat on the debt; Muḥammad says he does not until the debtor becomes wealthy again.
The mufta bihi is not stated here, but later practice often follows the Sahibayn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قرضدار مالدار ہو یا تنگدست لیکن قرضہ کا اقرار کرے، زکوۃ کا حکم : صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ اگر قرضہ کسی ایسے آدمی پر ہو جو اس قرضہ کا اقرار کرتا ہے خواہ یہ قرضدار مالدار ہو یا تنگدست ہو تو اس مال دین کی زکوۃ واجب ہے۔ کیونکہ اس قرضہ کا وصول کر لینا ممکن ہے۔ قرضدار اگر مالدار ہو تو ابتداء وصول کیا جا سکتا ہے۔ اور اگر تنگدست ہو تو بواسطہ تحصیل کے وصول کیا جاسکتا ہے۔ یعنی اس کی کمائی سے بحکم قاضی یا باہمی رضامندی سے حاصل کر لے۔ ایسے قرضہ پر مالک کو اگر چہ حقیقۂ قدرت نہیں لیکن حکما قدرت حاصل ہے۔ اور جب مالک کو قدرت حاصل ہے اگر چہ حکما ہی ہے تو اس کو مالِ ضمار نہیں کہا جائے گا۔ اور اگر قرضہ کسی منکر پر ہو لیکن قرض خواہ کے پاس اس کے خلاف گواہ موجود ہیں یا قاضی کو اس قرضہ کا ذاتی طور پر علم ہے تو بھی زکوۃ واجب ہے۔ کیونکہ اس قرضہ کا وصول کرنا ممکن ہے۔ اس لئے کہ گواہوں کی گواہی سے مالک مال کے حق میں قاضی فیصلہ کر دے گا یا قاضی اپنے علم کے موافق اس کے حق میں حکم کر دے گا۔ اور اگر قرضدار، قرضہ کا اقرار کرتا ہے مگر قاضی نے اس کے مفلس ہونے کا حکم دے دیا اور اعلان کر دیا تو یہ قرضہ کا مال بھی امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک نصاب زکوۃ ہے۔ یعنی اس کے اندر بھی زکوۃ واجب ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ قاضی کا اس کو مفلس کرنا یعنی اس کے مفلس ہونے کا حکم دینا اور اعلان کرنا صحیح نہیں ہے۔ پس جب قاضی کا اس کو مفلس کرنا صحیح نہیں تو مفلس کرنا اور نہ کرنا دونوں برابر ہیں۔ اور تفلیس نہ کرنے کی صورت میں بالاتفاق زکوۃ واجب ہوتی ہے۔ کیونکہ اس سے کمائی کرا کے قرضہ کا وصول کرنا ممکن ہے۔ پس اسی طرح تفلیس کے بعد بھی زکوۃ واجب ہو گی۔ اور امام محمد کے نزدیک مدیون کو قاضی کے مفلس کرنے کے بعد اس پر زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ امام محمد کے نزد یک قاضی کے مفلس کرنے کے بعد افلاس متحقق ہو جاتا ہے۔ اور جب قاضی کا مفلس کرنا امام محمد کے نزدیک صحیح ہے تو یہ قرضہ ، قرض خواہ کے حق میں بمنزلہ ہلاک شدہ مال کے ہو گیا۔ اور اس قرضہ کے مانند ہو گیا جس کا انکار کر دیا گیا ہو۔ اور ہلاک شدہ مال اور انکار کئے ہوئے مال میں زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہوتی۔ لہذا تفلیس قاضی کے بعد مدیون کے ذمہ جو دین ہے اس میں زکوۃ واجب نہ ہوگی۔ رہے امام ابو یوسف تو وہ تفلیس قاضی سے افلاس متحقق ہونے میں امام محمد کے ساتھ ہیں۔ چنانچہ قرضدار کے مالدرا ہونے تک قرض خواہ کا مطالبہ ساقط ہو جائے
Ruling on zakat when the debtor is wealthy or poor but acknowledges the debt: The author of Hidāyah said that if the debt is upon a person who acknowledges the debt, whether the debtor is wealthy or poor, then zakat on this debt is wajib. Because it is possible to recover this debt. If the debtor is wealthy, it can be recovered immediately. If he is poor, it can be recovered through acquisition, i.e., from his earnings by order of the qāḍī or by mutual consent. Although the owner does not have actual power over such a debt, he has power in a legal sense. And when the owner has power, albeit legally, it will not be called mal al-dhimār. And if the debt is upon a denier, but the creditor has witnesses against him, or the qāḍī has personal knowledge of the debt, then also zakat is wajib. Because it is possible to recover this debt. Because through the testimony of witnesses, the qāḍī will decide in favor of the owner of the wealth, or the qāḍī will rule in his favor according to his own knowledge. And if the debtor acknowledges the debt, but the qāḍī has declared him insolvent and announced it, then according to Imam Abū Ḥanīfa, this debt is also a zakatable nisāb. That is, zakat will be obligatory on it. Because the qāḍī's declaration of his insolvency — i.e., giving a ruling and announcement of his insolvency — is not valid. So when the qāḍī's declaration of insolvency is not valid, then declaring insolvent and not declaring are equal. And in the case of no declaration of insolvency, zakat is wajib by consensus. Because it is possible to recover the debt by making him earn. So similarly, after a declaration of insolvency, zakat will also be wajib. According to Imam Muḥammad, after the qāḍī declares the debtor insolvent, zakat is not wajib on it. Because according to Imam Muḥammad, insolvency is realized after the qāḍī's declaration. And when the qāḍī's declaration is valid according to Imam Muḥammad, then this debt becomes like destroyed property for the creditor. And it becomes like a debt that has been denied. And on destroyed property and denied debt, zakat is not wajib. Therefore, after the qāḍī's declaration of insolvency, zakat on the debt owed by the insolvent is not wajib. As for Imam Abū Yūsuf, he agrees with Imam Muḥammad that insolvency is realized by the qāḍī's declaration. Consequently, the creditor's claim is dropped until the debtor becomes wealthy.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Ḥanafī dispute regarding zakat on debts. The base ruling from the Hidāyah is that if a debtor acknowledges the debt, regardless of his financial status, zakat is due on the receivable because recovery is possible either immediately (if wealthy) or through forced acquisition (if poor). Even legal (ḥukman) power suffices to exclude it from mal al-dhimār. The same applies if the debtor denies but the creditor has witnesses or the qāḍī has personal knowledge. The dispute arises when the qāḍī formally declares the debtor insolvent (taflīs). Imam Abū Ḥanīfa holds that such a declaration is invalid, so the debt retains its status and zakat remains wajib. Imam Muḥammad holds that the qāḍī's declaration is valid and effectively makes the debt like destroyed or denied property, so no zakat is due. Imam Abū Yūsuf agrees with Muḥammad on the validity of taflīs, so he also holds zakat is not due after declaration. The muftā bihi position is not stated here, but the dispute is clear. The text ends with the consequence that the creditor's claim is suspended until the debtor becomes wealthy again.

Key Terms
تفلیس (taflīs): The qāḍī's formal declaration of a debtor's insolvency, preventing creditors from claiming until the debtor has wealth.
قدرت حکما (qudrat ḥukman): Legal power or capacity to dispose of property, even if actual physical access is lacking.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abū Ḥanīfa, why is zakat still wajib on a debt after the qāḍī declares the debtor insolvent?
A) Because the debtor is still required to pay zakat on his own wealth.
B) Because the qāḍī's declaration of insolvency is invalid.
C) Because the creditor has a legal right to claim the debt at any time.
D) Because the debt is considered destroyed property.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school is split on zakat after taflīs: Abū Ḥanīfa maintains the debt remains zakatable; the Sahibayn hold it becomes like destroyed property until the debtor regains wealth.

Zakat on Accessible Wealth: Buried Treasure and Traveler's Goods
Refutes a false analogy and states zakat rules for buried wealth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakat for buried wealth and distinguish between accessible and inaccessible wealth using the concept of mal ḍamār.

Core Idea
Zakat is due on wealth you can access, even through an agent; inaccessibility or extreme hardship may exempt it.

In this passage, the commentator refutes a flawed analogy that would exempt a traveler's wealth from zakat, then clarifies the rulings for wealth buried in a room versus land. The key distinction turns on whether the owner has effective power of disposal, either directly or through an agent. We will walk through the refutation and the two opinions on land-buried wealth so you can apply the principle of mal ḍamār correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the false analogy
What analogy did Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i make, and why is it considered corrupt? Trace the reasoning that compares traveler's wealth to lost wealth.
The false qiyās relies on lack of physical possession, but overlooks agency.
2
Understand the distinction: mal ḍamār vs mal nāmi
Define both terms as used in the passage. Lost wealth (ḍamār) has no access at all; growing wealth (nāmi) is productive or accessible. Traveler's wealth is nāmi because the owner can appoint an agent to sell and deliver.
The agent provides power of disposal, even if the owner is absent.
3
Apply the principle to wealth buried in a room
Why does the author of al-Hidayah rule zakat wajib for wealth buried in a room? Because the owner possesses the entire room and can easily access the treasure.
Easy access means it is not ḍamār.
4
Examine the ikhtilaf on wealth buried in land
When wealth is buried in a large garden and its exact spot is forgotten, some mashāyikh say zakat is wajib because digging the whole land is possible; others say not wajib because it is excessively difficult. Note the basis for each view.
The principle of hardship (rafʿ al-ḥaraj) is invoked to exempt if digging is extremely burdensome.
5
Summarize the resulting rulings
Consolidate: traveler's wealth → zakat wajib (accessible via agent). Buried in room → zakat wajib. Buried in land → two valid opinions within the Hanafi school.
No single muftā bihi is given; both views are recorded.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قیاس فاسد ہے۔ اس لئے کہ مال ضمار پر تصرف کی قدرت نہ بذات خود ہے اور نہ بذریعہ نائب کے۔ اور مسافر کو اپنے اس مال پر جو اس کے وطن میں ہے تصرف کی قدرت اگر چہ بذات خود نہیں لیکن بذریعہ نائب قدرت تصرف حاصل ہے۔ چنانچہ مسافر نے اگر اپنے مال میں سے کچھ بیچا تو جائز ہے کیونکہ مسافر اپنے نائب کے ذریعہ تسلیم مبیع پر قادر ہے۔ پس معلوم ہوا کہ مسافر کا مال ، مال نامی ہے اور مال ضمار نامی نہیں ہے۔ ایسی صورت میں امام زفر اور امام شافعی نظور کریں کہ اس عظیم فرق کے ہوتے ہوئے قیاس کس طرح درست ہو گا۔ کمرہ میں مدفون مال پر زکوۃ کا حکم : صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ جو مال کسی حجرہ میں مدفون ہو تو وہ نصاب زکوۃ ہے۔ یعنی اس مال میں زکوۃ واجب ہوگی۔ کیونکہ وہ حجرہ جمیع اجزاء کے ساتھ اس کے قبضہ میں ہے۔ اس لئے اس مال تک رسائی آسان ہے اور جب اس مال تک رسائی آسان ہے اور اس کا حاصل کرنا ممکن ہے تو یہ مال ، مال ضمار میں داخل نہ ہوگا۔ اور جب مال ضمار میں داخل نہیں تو اس میں زکوۃ بھی واجب ہوگی۔ اور اگر مال مملوکہ زمین یا باغ میں مدفون ہوا اور اس کی جگہ بھول گیا تو اس میں اختلاف مشائخ ہے۔ بعض نے کہا اس مال میں زکوۃ واجب ہے کیونکہ پوری زمین کو کھود کر اس کو نکالنا ممکن ہے۔ اس لئے اس پر تصرف کی قدرت بھی حاصل ہے اور جب تصرف کی قدرت حاصل ہے تو یہ مال مضمار نہ ہو گا۔ اور بعض مشائخ نے کہا ہے کہ اس مال کی زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ پوری زمین کو کھود نا اگر چه ممکن ہے لیکن دشوار ضرور ہے، اور شریعت میں حرج کو دور کیا گیا ہے۔ اس لئے اس مال میں زکوۃ واجب نہ ہوگی۔
The analogy is corrupt. Because on lost wealth (mal damar) there is no power of disposal by oneself nor through an agent. But a traveler has power of disposal over his wealth that is in his homeland, though not by himself, yet through an agent he has the power of disposal. So if a traveler sells some of his wealth, it is valid, because the traveler is able to deliver the sold item through his agent. Thus it became known that the traveler's wealth is 'growing wealth' (mal nami) and is not called 'lost wealth' (mal damar). In such a case, Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i should consider: despite this great difference, how can the analogy be correct? The ruling on buried wealth in a room: The author of Al-Hidayah says that wealth buried in a room reaches the niṣāb for zakat, meaning zakat is obligatory on that wealth. Because that room is in his possession in all its parts. Therefore access to that wealth is easy, and when access is easy and obtaining it is possible, this wealth does not fall under lost wealth. And when it does not fall under lost wealth, then zakat becomes obligatory. And if the wealth is buried in owned land or a garden and its location is forgotten, then there is a difference of opinion among the mashāyikh. Some said zakat is obligatory on that wealth because it is possible to dig the entire land and extract it. Therefore he has power of disposal over it, and when he has power of disposal, it is not lost wealth. And some mashāyikh said that zakat on this wealth is not obligatory, because although digging the entire land is possible, it is certainly difficult, and hardship is removed in the Shari'ah. Therefore zakat is not obligatory on this wealth.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage begins by refuting a false analogy (qiyas fāsid) that compares a traveler's wealth to lost wealth. The commentator clarifies the distinction: lost wealth (mal ḍamār) is completely inaccessible, whereas a traveler has access through an agent. Hence the traveler's wealth is called 'growing wealth' (mal nāmi) and zakat is due on it. Then the commentary addresses buried wealth. If it is buried in a room the owner controls, it is like any accessible property; zakat is wajib. If buried in land or a garden and forgotten, the mashāyikh differ: some consider digging possible (though burdensome) and thus zakat is due; others regard the hardship as significant enough to exempt it, based on the principle of removing hardship (raf' al-ḥaraj) in the Shari'ah. The passage does not give a single muftā bihi ruling, but presents both views.

Key Terms
مال ضمار (mal ḍamār): Lost wealth over which one has no power of disposal either directly or through an agent.
مال نامی (mal nāmi): Growing wealth that is productive or accessible, upon which zakat is obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is zakat wajib on wealth buried in a room but not necessarily on wealth buried in a large land when the location is forgotten?
A) Because a room is smaller and easier to dig.
B) Because the owner has full possession of the room, making access easy; for land, excavation may be too burdensome, leading to ikhtilaf.
C) Because land is not owned by the individual.
D) Because zakat is only on visible wealth.

Key Takeaway
Zakat is due on wealth you can access, even indirectly; extreme difficulty may exempt, as seen in the ikhtilaf on land-buried wealth.

Zakat on Debts: The Default Ruling When Collection is Possible
Ruling statement with proof for zakat on debts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakat for acknowledged debts and identify the condition that makes zakat wajib.

Core Idea
Zakat on a debt is wajib as long as collection is possible — even if only through legal means.

This passage from Al-Hidayah establishes the foundational Hanafi position: any debt that can be collected, whether immediately or through legal recourse, is subject to zakat. The key is the concept of 'legal power' (qudrat ḥukman) — even if you cannot physically collect, if the law gives you a route, the debt is not lost.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act under discussion is a debt owed to you. The ruling is that zakat is wajib on that debt.
This is the default ruling.
2
Identify the condition for obligation
The condition is that collection (tahṣīl) of the debt must be possible. The passage mentions two scenarios: debtor acknowledges (rich or poor) or denier with witnesses.
3
Distinguish between actual and legal power
Actual power (qudrat ḥaqīqiyya) means you can collect immediately. Legal power (qudrat ḥukman) means you can collect through the qadi. Both make zakat wajib.
This is the key legal principle.
4
Apply to the denier case
Even if the debtor denies, but you have witnesses or the qadi knows, zakat is wajib because collection is possible through the court.
This extends the ruling beyond acknowledged debts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قرضدار مالدار ہو یا تنگدست لیکن قرضہ کا اقرار کرے، زکوۃ کا حکم : صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ اگر قرضہ کسی ایسے آدمی پر ہو جو اس قرضہ کا اقرار کرتا ہے خواہ یہ قرضدار مالدار ہو یا تنگدست ہو تو اس مال دین کی زکوۃ واجب ہے۔ کیونکہ اس قرضہ کا وصول کر لینا ممکن ہے۔ قرضدار اگر مالدار ہو تو ابتداء وصول کیا جا سکتا ہے۔ اور اگر تنگدست ہو تو بواسطہ تحصیل کے وصول کیا جاسکتا ہے۔ یعنی اس کی کمائی سے بحکم قاضی یا باہمی رضامندی سے حاصل کر لے۔ ایسے قرضہ پر مالک کو اگر چہ حقیقۂ قدرت نہیں لیکن حکما قدرت حاصل ہے۔ اور جب مالک کو قدرت حاصل ہے اگر چہ حکما ہی ہے تو اس کو مالِ ضمار نہیں کہا جائے گا۔ اور اگر قرضہ کسی منکر پر ہو لیکن قرض خواہ کے پاس اس کے خلاف گواہ موجود ہیں یا قاضی کو اس قرضہ کا ذاتی طور پر علم ہے تو بھی زکوۃ واجب ہے۔ کیونکہ اس قرضہ کا وصول کرنا ممکن ہے۔ اس لئے کہ گواہوں کی گواہی سے مالک مال کے حق میں قاضی فیصلہ کر دے گا یا قاضی اپنے علم کے موافق اس کے حق میں حکم کر دے گا۔ اور اگر قرضدار، قرضہ کا اقرار کرتا ہے مگر قاضی نے اس کے مفلس ہونے کا حکم دے دیا اور اعلان کر دیا تو یہ قرضہ کا مال بھی امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک نصاب زکوۃ ہے۔ یعنی اس کے اندر بھی زکوۃ واجب ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ قاضی کا اس کو مفلس کرنا یعنی اس کے مفلس ہونے کا حکم دینا اور اعلان کرنا صحیح نہیں ہے۔ پس جب قاضی کا اس کو مفلس کرنا صحیح نہیں تو مفلس کرنا اور نہ کرنا دونوں برابر ہیں۔ اور تفلیس نہ کرنے کی صورت میں بالاتفاق زکوۃ واجب ہوتی ہے۔ کیونکہ اس سے کمائی کرا کے قرضہ کا وصول کرنا ممکن ہے۔ پس اسی طرح تفلیس کے بعد بھی زکوۃ واجب ہو گی۔ اور امام محمد کے نزدیک مدیون کو قاضی کے مفلس کرنے کے بعد اس پر زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ امام محمد کے نزد یک قاضی کے مفلس کرنے کے بعد افلاس متحقق ہو جاتا ہے۔ اور جب قاضی کا مفلس کرنا امام محمد کے نزدیک صحیح ہے تو یہ قرضہ ، قرض خواہ کے حق میں بمنزلہ ہلاک شدہ مال کے ہو گیا۔ اور اس قرضہ کے مانند ہو گیا جس کا انکار کر دیا گیا ہو۔ اور ہلاک شدہ مال اور انکار کئے ہوئے مال میں زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہوتی۔ لہذا تفلیس قاضی کے بعد مدیون کے ذمہ جو دین ہے اس میں زکوۃ واجب نہ ہوگی۔ رہے امام ابو یوسف تو وہ تفلیس قاضی سے افلاس متحقق ہونے میں امام محمد کے ساتھ ہیں۔ چنانچہ قرضدار کے مالدرا ہونے تک قرض خواہ کا مطالبہ ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ اس کو مطالبہ کرنے کا حق نہ ہوگا۔ الا یہ کہ قرضدار مال دار ہو جائے۔ اور زکوۃ واجب ہونے میں امام ابو حنیفہ کے ساتھ ہیں۔ چنانچہ قرض خواہ کو جب یہ قرضہ وصول ہو جائے گا تو شیخین کے نزدیک سنین ماضیہ کی زکوۃ قرض خواہ پر واجب ہوگی ۔ امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک زکوۃ واجب کرنے میں فقراء کی رعایت پیش نظر ہے۔
The ruling on zakat for a debtor whether wealthy or poor, but who acknowledges the debt: The author of Al-Hidayah said that if the debt is owed by a person who acknowledges that debt, whether the debtor is wealthy or poor, then zakat on that debt is obligatory. Because it is possible to collect that debt. If the debtor is wealthy, it can be collected immediately. If he is poor, it can be collected by means of earning; i.e., he can obtain it from his earnings by order of the qadi or by mutual consent. In such a debt, the owner (creditor) does not have actual power, but he has power in the eyes of the law (ḥukman). And when the owner has power, even if it is only legal, this debt will not be called lost wealth. And if the debt is owed by a denier, but the creditor has witnesses against him, or the qadi personally knows about this debt, then also zakat is obligatory. Because it is possible to collect this debt. For the qadi will decide in favor of the owner of the wealth based on the witnesses' testimony, or the qadi will rule in his favor according to his own knowledge. And if the debtor acknowledges the debt, but the qadi has declared him bankrupt and announced it, then this debt is also, in the view of Imam Abu Hanifa, subject to zakat, i.e., zakat will be obligatory on it. Because the qadi's declaring him bankrupt—i.e., his ruling and announcement of bankruptcy—is not valid. So when the qadi's bankruptcy declaration is not valid, then bankruptcy and non-bankruptcy are equal. And in the case of no bankruptcy, by consensus zakat is obligatory, because it is possible to make him earn and collect the debt. So similarly after the bankruptcy declaration, zakat will be obligatory. And in the view of Imam Muhammad, after the qadi declares the debtor bankrupt, zakat on him is not obligatory. Because according to Imam Muhammad, after the qadi declares bankruptcy, the insolvency is established. And when the qadi's bankruptcy is valid according to Imam Muhammad, then this debt, from the creditor's perspective, becomes like lost property. And it becomes like a debt that was denied. And on lost property and a denied debt, zakat is not obligatory. Therefore, after the qadi's bankruptcy declaration, zakat is not obligatory on the debt owed by the debtor. As for Imam Abu Yusuf, he agrees with Imam Muhammad that insolvency is established by the qadi's bankruptcy declaration. So until the debtor becomes wealthy, the creditor's claim is suspended. He will not have the right to demand payment unless the debtor becomes wealthy. But in the obligation of zakat, he agrees with Imam Abu Hanifa. So when the creditor collects this debt, according to the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), zakat for past years will be obligatory on the creditor. According to Imam Abu Yusuf, in making zakat obligatory, consideration for the poor is taken into account.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on zakat on debts. It begins with the default ruling: a debt acknowledged by the debtor, whether he is wealthy or poor, is subject to zakat because collection is possible either immediately or through legal means. Even if the debtor denies, if witnesses exist or the qadi knows, collection is possible, so zakat is due. Then it delves into an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding a debtor declared bankrupt by a qadi. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the qadi's bankruptcy declaration is invalid, so the debt remains potentially collectable, hence zakat is still wajib. Imam Muhammad holds that the bankruptcy is valid, making the debt like lost property, thus no zakat. Imam Abu Yusuf agrees with Muhammad on the validity of bankruptcy (the right to demand is suspended) but agrees with Abu Hanifa on zakat obligation when eventually collected; he also notes that the purpose of zakat is to consider the poor. The passage does not explicitly state the muftā bihi, but later Hanafi practice tends to follow the view of Imam Muhammad (no zakat during ongoing insolvency), though the text presents the positions.

Key Terms
قدرت حکما (qudrat ḥukman): Legal power; the creditor's ability to collect through judicial means, even if not physically able.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the condition that makes zakat on a debt wajib?
A) The debtor must be wealthy.
B) The debt must be acknowledged by the debtor.
C) Collection must be possible, either immediately or through legal means.
D) The creditor must have the money in hand.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi default ruling: zakat on a debt is wajib as long as the creditor has a legal means to collect it, even if actual receipt is delayed.

The Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf: Zakat After a Qadi's Bankruptcy Declaration
Intra-Hanafi dispute on zakat after bankruptcy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the three Hanafi positions on zakat for debts after a qadi's bankruptcy declaration and identify the key point of disagreement.

Core Idea
Imam Abu Hanifa holds zakat wajib even after bankruptcy; Imam Muhammad says no; Imam Abu Yusuf splits the difference.

When a qadi declares a debtor bankrupt (taflīs), does the creditor still owe zakat on that debt? This passage from Al-Hidayah presents the reasoning of the three great Hanafi imams. Understanding this ikhtilaf is crucial for issuing correct fatwas in cases of insolvency.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The debtor acknowledges the debt but the qadi declares him bankrupt and announces it. This triggers the ikhtilaf.
2
State Imam Abu Hanifa's view
He holds zakat is wajib because the qadi's bankruptcy declaration is invalid. Therefore, the debt remains potentially collectable.
Key point: Abu Hanifa does not recognize the legal effect of taflīs.
3
State Imam Muhammad's view
He holds zakat is not wajib because the qadi's declaration is valid, making the debt like lost property (māl hālik).
Key point: Muhammad recognizes the legal effect, so the debt is treated as if destroyed.
4
State Imam Abu Yusuf's view
He agrees with Muhammad that bankruptcy is valid (claim suspended) but agrees with Abu Hanifa that zakat is wajib when eventually collected.
His rationale: consideration for the poor (fiqh al-fuqarā').

قرضدار مالدار ہو یا تنگدست لیکن قرضہ کا اقرار کرے، زکوۃ کا حکم : صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ اگر قرضہ کسی ایسے آدمی پر ہو جو اس قرضہ کا اقرار کرتا ہے خواہ یہ قرضدار مالدار ہو یا تنگدست ہو تو اس مال دین کی زکوۃ واجب ہے۔ کیونکہ اس قرضہ کا وصول کر لینا ممکن ہے۔ قرضدار اگر مالدار ہو تو ابتداء وصول کیا جا سکتا ہے۔ اور اگر تنگدست ہو تو بواسطہ تحصیل کے وصول کیا جاسکتا ہے۔ یعنی اس کی کمائی سے بحکم قاضی یا باہمی رضامندی سے حاصل کر لے۔ ایسے قرضہ پر مالک کو اگر چہ حقیقۂ قدرت نہیں لیکن حکما قدرت حاصل ہے۔ اور جب مالک کو قدرت حاصل ہے اگر چہ حکما ہی ہے تو اس کو مالِ ضمار نہیں کہا جائے گا۔ اور اگر قرضہ کسی منکر پر ہو لیکن قرض خواہ کے پاس اس کے خلاف گواہ موجود ہیں یا قاضی کو اس قرضہ کا ذاتی طور پر علم ہے تو بھی زکوۃ واجب ہے۔ کیونکہ اس قرضہ کا وصول کرنا ممکن ہے۔ اس لئے کہ گواہوں کی گواہی سے مالک مال کے حق میں قاضی فیصلہ کر دے گا یا قاضی اپنے علم کے موافق اس کے حق میں حکم کر دے گا۔ اور اگر قرضدار، قرضہ کا اقرار کرتا ہے مگر قاضی نے اس کے مفلس ہونے کا حکم دے دیا اور اعلان کر دیا تو یہ قرضہ کا مال بھی امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک نصاب زکوۃ ہے۔ یعنی اس کے اندر بھی زکوۃ واجب ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ قاضی کا اس کو مفلس کرنا یعنی اس کے مفلس ہونے کا حکم دینا اور اعلان کرنا صحیح نہیں ہے۔ پس جب قاضی کا اس کو مفلس کرنا صحیح نہیں تو مفلس کرنا اور نہ کرنا دونوں برابر ہیں۔ اور تفلیس نہ کرنے کی صورت میں بالاتفاق زکوۃ واجب ہوتی ہے۔ کیونکہ اس سے کمائی کرا کے قرضہ کا وصول کرنا ممکن ہے۔ پس اسی طرح تفلیس کے بعد بھی زکوۃ واجب ہو گی۔ اور امام محمد کے نزدیک مدیون کو قاضی کے مفلس کرنے کے بعد اس پر زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ امام محمد کے نزد یک قاضی کے مفلس کرنے کے بعد افلاس متحقق ہو جاتا ہے۔ اور جب قاضی کا مفلس کرنا امام محمد کے نزدیک صحیح ہے تو یہ قرضہ ، قرض خواہ کے حق میں بمنزلہ ہلاک شدہ مال کے ہو گیا۔ اور اس قرضہ کے مانند ہو گیا جس کا انکار کر دیا گیا ہو۔ اور ہلاک شدہ مال اور انکار کئے ہوئے مال میں زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہوتی۔ لہذا تفلیس قاضی کے بعد مدیون کے ذمہ جو دین ہے اس میں زکوۃ واجب نہ ہوگی۔ رہے امام ابو یوسف تو وہ تفلیس قاضی سے افلاس متحقق ہونے میں امام محمد کے ساتھ ہیں۔ چنانچہ قرضدار کے مالدرا ہونے تک قرض خواہ کا مطالبہ ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ اس کو مطالبہ کرنے کا حق نہ ہوگا۔ الا یہ کہ قرضدار مال دار ہو جائے۔ اور زکوۃ واجب ہونے میں امام ابو حنیفہ کے ساتھ ہیں۔ چنانچہ قرض خواہ کو جب یہ قرضہ وصول ہو جائے گا تو شیخین کے نزدیک سنین ماضیہ کی زکوۃ قرض خواہ پر واجب ہوگی ۔ امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک زکوۃ واجب کرنے میں فقراء کی رعایت پیش نظر ہے۔
The ruling on zakat for a debtor whether wealthy or poor, but who acknowledges the debt: The author of Al-Hidayah said that if the debt is owed by a person who acknowledges that debt, whether the debtor is wealthy or poor, then zakat on that debt is obligatory. Because it is possible to collect that debt. If the debtor is wealthy, it can be collected immediately. If he is poor, it can be collected by means of earning; i.e., he can obtain it from his earnings by order of the qadi or by mutual consent. In such a debt, the owner (creditor) does not have actual power, but he has power in the eyes of the law (ḥukman). And when the owner has power, even if it is only legal, this debt will not be called lost wealth. And if the debt is owed by a denier, but the creditor has witnesses against him, or the qadi personally knows about this debt, then also zakat is obligatory. Because it is possible to collect this debt. For the qadi will decide in favor of the owner of the wealth based on the witnesses' testimony, or the qadi will rule in his favor according to his own knowledge. And if the debtor acknowledges the debt, but the qadi has declared him bankrupt and announced it, then this debt is also, in the view of Imam Abu Hanifa, subject to zakat, i.e., zakat will be obligatory on it. Because the qadi's declaring him bankrupt—i.e., his ruling and announcement of bankruptcy—is not valid. So when the qadi's bankruptcy declaration is not valid, then bankruptcy and non-bankruptcy are equal. And in the case of no bankruptcy, by consensus zakat is obligatory, because it is possible to make him earn and collect the debt. So similarly after the bankruptcy declaration, zakat will be obligatory. And in the view of Imam Muhammad, after the qadi declares the debtor bankrupt, zakat on him is not obligatory. Because according to Imam Muhammad, after the qadi declares bankruptcy, the insolvency is established. And when the qadi's bankruptcy is valid according to Imam Muhammad, then this debt, from the creditor's perspective, becomes like lost property. And it becomes like a debt that was denied. And on lost property and a denied debt, zakat is not obligatory. Therefore, after the qadi's bankruptcy declaration, zakat is not obligatory on the debt owed by the debtor. As for Imam Abu Yusuf, he agrees with Imam Muhammad that insolvency is established by the qadi's bankruptcy declaration. So until the debtor becomes wealthy, the creditor's claim is suspended. He will not have the right to demand payment unless the debtor becomes wealthy. But in the obligation of zakat, he agrees with Imam Abu Hanifa. So when the creditor collects this debt, according to the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), zakat for past years will be obligatory on the creditor. According to Imam Abu Yusuf, in making zakat obligatory, consideration for the poor is taken into account.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on zakat on debts. It begins with the default ruling: a debt acknowledged by the debtor, whether he is wealthy or poor, is subject to zakat because collection is possible either immediately or through legal means. Even if the debtor denies, if witnesses exist or the qadi knows, collection is possible, so zakat is due. Then it delves into an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding a debtor declared bankrupt by a qadi. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the qadi's bankruptcy declaration is invalid, so the debt remains potentially collectable, hence zakat is still wajib. Imam Muhammad holds that the bankruptcy is valid, making the debt like lost property, thus no zakat. Imam Abu Yusuf agrees with Muhammad on the validity of bankruptcy (the right to demand is suspended) but agrees with Abu Hanifa on zakat obligation when eventually collected; he also notes that the purpose of zakat is to consider the poor. The passage does not explicitly state the muftā bihi, but later Hanafi practice tends to follow the view of Imam Muhammad (no zakat during ongoing insolvency), though the text presents the positions.

Key Terms
تفلیس (taflīs): The qadi's ruling declaring a debtor bankrupt, which legally restricts his property and suspends creditors' claims.
قدرت حکما (qudrat ḥukman): Legal power; the creditor's ability to collect through judicial means, even if not physically able.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the key point of disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad regarding zakat after a qadi's bankruptcy declaration?
A) Whether the debt is collectable from the debtor's future earnings.
B) Whether the qadi's bankruptcy declaration is valid.
C) Whether the creditor must seek the qadi's permission to collect.
D) Whether zakat is due on lost property such as a denied debt.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has three distinct views on zakat after bankruptcy; the mufti must be aware of all three and the preferred practice.

Zakat — Almsgiving

Intention and Zakat: The Asymmetric Effect of Abandonment vs. Action
Ruling on zakat when intention changes from trade to service.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi distinction between abandonment (tark) and positive action (fi'l) to determine zakat obligations when a trade asset's purpose changes.

Core Idea
Abandonment of trade is mere intention; reinstating trade requires action.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a key question: can a change of intention alone affect the zakat status of a trade asset? The answer reveals a fundamental distinction in Hanafi fiqh between positive actions (which require action plus intention) and abandonments (which require only intention). Understanding this asymmetry is crucial for correctly applying zakat rules to assets that shift between trade and personal use.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial status
The asset (slave-girl) was purchased with the intention of trade. This makes it a trade good subject to zakat when it reaches niṣāb and a year passes.
Ownership plus trade intention is the key.
2
First change: intention for service
The owner intends to use her for service, i.e., abandons trade. According to Hanafi, abandonment (tark) is a non-action, so mere intention suffices to remove the asset from trade. Zakat is nullified.
Tark is realized by niyyah alone.
3
Second change: intention for trade again
If the owner later intends to return her to trade without selling, mere intention is insufficient because reinstating trade is a positive action. The asset remains a personal asset until a trade action (selling) occurs.
Fi'l requires action plus intention.
4
Recognize the underlying principle
The rule is based on the distinction: for actions of the limbs, intention alone is not enough; for abandonments, intention alone is sufficient. This is supported by the travel analogy: a traveler becomes resident by mere intention (abandoning travel), but a resident needs actual travel to become a traveler.
The analogy reinforces the principle.
5
Apply to modern cases
Any asset purchased for resale: if the owner decides to use it personally, zakat stops immediately by intention. If later he wants to sell it, no zakat until actual sale takes place.
The same rule applies.

باندی تجارت کی نیت سے خریدی پھر خدمت کی نیت کر لی تو زکوۃ باطل ہے
وَمَنِ اشْتَرى جَارِيَةِ لِلتِّجَارَةِ وَنَوَاهَا لِلْخِدْمَةِ بَطَلَتْ عَنْهَا الزَّكوةُ لِاِتِّصَالِ النّيةِ بِالْعَمَلِ وَهُوَ تَرَكُ التِّجَارَةِ وَإِنْ نَوَاهَا لِلتِّجَارَةِ بَعْدَ ذَالِكَ لَمْ تَكُنْ لِلتِّجَارَةِ حَتَّى بَيْعَهَا فَيَكُونُ فِى ثَمَنِهَا زَكوةً لأَنَّ النِّيَّةَ لَمْ تَتَّصِلُ بِالْعَمَلِ إِذْ هُوَ لَمْ يَتَّجِرُ فَلَمْ تُعْتَبَرُ وَلِهَذَا يَصِيرُ الْمُسَافِرُ مُقِيِّمًا بِمُجَرَّدِ البَيَةِ وَلَا يَصِيرُ الْمُقِيمُ مُسَافِرُ بِالنّيةِ إِلَّا بِالسَّفَرِ
ترجمہ اور جس شخص نے تجارت کے لئے ایک باندی خریدی اور خدمت کے لئے اس کی نیت کر لی تو اس باندی سے زکوۃ باطل ہو گئی ۔ کیونکہ نیت عمل کے ساتھ متصل ہو گئی اور وہ ترک تجارت ہے اور اگر اس کے بعد تجارت کے لئے نیت کر لی تو وہ باندی تجارت کے واسطے نہ ہوگی یہاں تک کہ اس باندی کو فروخت کرے۔ پس اس باندی کے شمن میں زکوۃ ہے۔ اس لئے کہ نیت کسی عمل کے ساتھ متصل نہیں ہوئی۔ کیونکہ اس نے تجارت کا کوئی فعل نہیں کیا تو نیت معتبر نہ ہوئی یہی وجہ ہے کہ مسافر محض نیت سے مقیم ہو جاتا ہے اور مقیم محض نیت سے مسافر نہ ہوگا مگر سفر کے ساتھ ۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی شخص نے تجارت کے ارادے سے ایک باندی خریدی پھر یہ ارادہ کر لیا کہ اس سے خدمت لوں گا اور اس کو تجارت سے خارج کرنے کی نیت کر لی تو اس باندی سے زکوۃ باطل ہو گئی یعنی اس باندی کی مالیت میں زکوۃ واجب نہ ہوگی۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ جو چیز اعمال جوارح سے ہے وہ محض نیت سے متحقق نہیں ہوتی بلکہ نیت کا عمل کے ساتھ متصل ہونا ضروری ہے۔ اور جو چیز ترک کے قبیل سے ہے اس میں محض نیت کا ہونا کافی ہے۔ پس چونکہ اس شخص نے تجارت کی نیت سے باندی خریدی اور پھر اس سے خدمت لینے کی نیت کر لی یعنی ترک تجارت کی نیت کی تو محض ہے سے یہ باندی تجارت سے خارج ہو جائے گی۔ اور جب تجارت سے خارج ہو گئی تو اس سے زکوۃ بھی باطل ہو گئی۔
صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا ہے کہ نیت عمل کے ساتھ متصل ہوگئی اور وہ عمل ترک تجارت ہے حالانکہ ترک تجارت عمل نہیں ہے بلکہ ترک عمل ہے۔ اور اگر تجارت کی نیت سے باندی خریدی پھر اس سے خدمت لینے کی نیت کی پھر اس کے بعد تجارت کی نیت کی ، تو وہ باندی تجارت کے واسطے نہ ہو گی ۔ یہاں تک کہ اس باندی کو فروخت کرے۔ پس اگر اس کو فروخت کر دیا تو اس باندی کے ثمن میں زکوۃ واجب ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ جب تک اس نے باندی کو فروخت نہیں کیا تو نیت عمل تجارت کے ساتھ متصل نہ ہوئی اور جونیت عمل کے ساتھ متصل نہ ہو وہ معتبر نہیں ہوتی۔ اس لئے محض نیت کرنے سے وہ باندی تجارت کے واسطے نہ ہوگی ۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ مسافر محض نیست اقامت سے مقیم ہو جائے گا۔ اس لئے کہ اقامت نام ہے ترک سفر کا اور ترک میں محض نیت کافی ہو جاتی ہے۔ لیکن مقیم محض نیت سفر سے مسافر نہیں ہو گا۔ ہاں اگر اس نے نیت کے ساتھ سفر شروع کر دیا تو مسافر ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ سفر جوارح کا عمل ہے اور جو عمل جوارح کا ہو وہ محض نیست تحق نہیں ہوتا بلکہ نیت کے ساتھ عمل کا پایا جانا بھی ضروری ہے اس لئے جب تک سفر شروع نہ کرے گا محض سفر کی نیت سے مسافر نہ ہوگا۔
If a person buys a slave-girl for trade and then intends her for service, zakat on her is nullified.
And whoever buys a slave-girl for trade and intends her for service, zakat on her is nullified because the intention is connected to an action, and that action is abandoning trade. And if after that he intends her for trade, she will not be regarded as for trade until he sells her; then zakat will be due on her price, because the intention was not connected to an action since he did not trade, so it is not considered. And for this reason, a traveler becomes a resident merely by the intention of residence, and a resident does not become a traveler by intention alone without traveling.
Translation: And whoever bought a slave-girl for trade and then intended her for service, zakat on that slave-girl is nullified. Because the intention became connected to an action, and that action is abandoning trade. And if after that he intends her for trade, she will not be for trade until he sells her. Then zakat is due on her price, because the intention was not connected to any action, since he did not perform a trade action, so the intention is not considered. For this reason, a traveler becomes a resident merely by the intention of residence, and a resident does not become a traveler by intention alone except with travel.
Explanation: The issue is that if a person bought a slave-girl with the intention of trade, then intended to take service from her and removed her from trade, zakat on her is nullified, i.e., zakat on her value is not wajib. The proof is that what belongs to actions of the limbs is not realized by mere intention; rather, intention must be connected to action. And what belongs to the category of abandonment (tark), mere intention is sufficient. So since he bought the slave-girl with the intention of trade and then intended to take service from her, i.e., intended to abandon trade, then by mere intention she exits trade. And when she exits trade, zakat on her is also nullified. The author of Al-Hidayah said that intention became connected to an action, and that action is abandoning trade, although abandoning trade is not an action but rather abandonment of action. And if he bought a slave-girl for trade, then intended to take service, then afterwards intended for trade, she will not become for trade until he sells her. If he sells her, then zakat becomes due on her price. Because until he sells her, the intention is not connected to the action of trade, and an intention not connected to action is not considered. Therefore, by mere intention, she does not become for trade. The author of Al-Hidayah stated that a traveler becomes resident by mere intention of residence, because residence is the abandonment of travel, and in abandonment mere intention is sufficient. But a resident does not become a traveler by mere intention of travel; yes, if he starts travel with intention, then he becomes a traveler. Because travel is an action of the limbs, and what is an action of the limbs is not realized by mere intention; rather, the presence of action along with intention is also necessary. Therefore, as long as he does not start travel, he will not become a traveler by mere intention.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on zakat for a slave-girl purchased with the intention of trade (for resale) and then changed to personal use (service). The key principle is: when an intention (niyyah) involves an action of the limbs (like selling or traveling), a mere change of intention is not sufficient to effect a legal change; the action must accompany the intention. However, when the change involves abandoning an action (like stopping trade), mere intention suffices because abandonment is a non-action. So: initially buying for trade makes the slave-girl a trade good subject to zakat. Then intending to use her for service is an abandonment of trade, which happens by mere intention, so she becomes a personal asset and zakat ceases. Later, if the owner wishes to return her to trade, mere intention is not enough; he must actually trade (sell her), because that requires a positive action. Only then does zakat become due on the sale price. The passage also draws an analogy: a traveler becomes a resident by mere intention of residence (since residency is abandoning travel), but a resident becomes a traveler only by actually traveling (a physical action). This analogy reinforces the rule.

Key Terms
نیت (niyyah): Intention; in this context, the intention to trade or to use personally.
ترک تجارت (tark al-tijārah): Abandonment of trade; a passive act that is realized by mere intention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, which of the following correctly states when a trade asset becomes subject to zakat after being converted to personal use?
A) As soon as the owner again intends trade.
B) Only when the asset is actually sold.
C) When a year passes after the new intention.
D) When the asset is offered for sale.

Key Takeaway
Intention alone can remove an asset from trade (tark), but reinstating trade requires a positive action (selling).

Effect of Changing Intention on Trade Asset for Zakah
Ruling on the effect of intention change on zakah for a trade asset, with qiyas proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that zakah on a trade asset is cancelled by mere intention to abandon trade, and explain the distinction between intention for omissions versus acts of commission.

Core Idea
Zakah on a trade asset is cancelled by mere intention to abandon trade, because omission is realized by intention alone.

This lesson examines a ruling from al-Hidayah about the role of intention (niyyah) in determining the zakah status of a trade asset. The key insight is the Hanafi distinction between acts of commission (a'maal jawarih) and acts of omission (tark). Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying the principles of niyyah in zakah and beyond.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is buying a slave-girl for trade, then intending her for service. The ruling: zakah is cancelled immediately upon the new intention.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is qiyas on the case of a traveler becoming a resident by mere intention to stay (tark of travel).
The analogy is explicit in the text.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The common element (illa) is that both cases involve an omission (tark): abandoning trade and abandoning travel. In Hanafi usul, omission is realized by intention alone.
This is a unique Hanafi principle.
4
Note the reverse scenario
If the owner later intends trade again, the asset does not become a trade asset until actual sale, because trading is a positive act requiring action.
This highlights the asymmetry between omission and commission.
5
Evaluate the thamarah
The practical consequence is that a person can instantly change the zakah status of an asset by mere intention when abandoning trade, but cannot re-enter trade status without a physical act.
This prevents manipulation and aligns with the nature of omission.

فرمایا ہے کہ مسافر محض نیست اقامت سے مقیم ہو جائے گا۔ اس لئے کہ اقامت نام ہے ترک سفر کا اور ترک میں محض نیت کافی ہو جاتی ہے۔ لیکن مقیم محض نیت سفر سے مسافر نہیں ہو گا۔ ہاں اگر اس نے نیت کے ساتھ سفر شروع کر دیا تو مسافر ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ سفر جوارح کا عمل ہے اور جو عمل جوارح کا ہو وہ محض نیست تحق نہیں ہوتا بلکہ نیت کے ساتھ عمل کا پایا جانا بھی ضروری ہے اس لئے جب تک سفر شروع نہ کرے گا محض سفر کی نیت سے مسافر نہ ہوگا۔
And whoever bought a slave-girl for trade and intended her for service, the zakah is cancelled due to the intention being connected to the action, which is abandoning trade. And if after that he intended her for trade, she is not for trade until he sells her, so there is zakah in her price because the intention was not connected to an action, since he did not trade, so it is not considered. And for this reason, a traveler becomes a resident by mere intention, but a resident does not become a traveler by intention except with travel.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage states a ruling about a slave-girl bought for trade. If the owner then intends to use her for service (thus abandoning the trade intention), the zakah obligation on her value is cancelled immediately because the intention to abandon trade is itself considered an act of omission (tark) which is realized by mere intention. However, if after that he again intends her for trade, she does not become a trade asset until he actually sells her, because the new trade intention must be connected to an action (the sale). The commentary explains the underlying legal principle: Intentions for acts of commission (like traveling, trading) require connection to the physical act; intentions for omission (like staying, abandoning trade) are effective by mere intention. This is illustrated by the analogy of a traveler: he becomes a resident by merely intending to stay (tark of travel), but a resident does not become a traveler by mere intention; he must actually start traveling. The author (Sahib al-Hidayah) notes that although abandoning trade is not a positive act, the intention is deemed connected to the omission, so the ruling is consistent.

Key Terms
نِيَّة (niyyah): Intention in the heart that determines the legal nature of an action or omission.
تَرْك (tark): Abandonment or omission of an action; considered a legal act that can be realized by intention alone.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man buys a slave-girl for service, then intends to sell her for profit. According to the Hanafi school, when does she become a trade asset?
A) Immediately upon the new intention
B) Only after he actually tries to sell her or offers for sale
C) After one year of intention
D) Never

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, an intention to abandon trade (an omission) is effective immediately, while an intention to engage in trade (an act of commission) requires a physical action to take effect.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Trade Intention on Non-Purchase Acquisitions
Dispute on trade intention after non-purchase acquisition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on whether trade intention after acquiring property through gift, bequest, marriage, khul', or settlement makes it trade property, and identify the practical consequence for zakah.

Core Idea
Intention alone does not make an asset trade property; it must be connected to a trading action.

The Hanafi school agrees that buying with trade intention creates trade property. But what about assets acquired without purchase—like gifts or inheritances? The school splits: Abu Yusuf treats acceptance as an action linking intention to the asset, while Muhammad requires the action itself to be trading. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and its effect on zakah.

Guided Path
1
1. State the agreed rule for purchase
When one buys something intending trade, the intention is directly connected to the buying action (a trade act), so the asset becomes trade property. This is uncontested.
The key is the connection between intention and a trade-related action.
2
2. Explain why inheritance is different
Inheritance involves no action from the heir; the property simply transfers to ownership. Thus, a later trade intention cannot connect to any action, so the asset remains non-trade property.
The absence of action is decisive.
3
3. List the contested acquisition modes
Gift, bequest, marriage dower, khul' (divorce for compensation), and settlement for blood money all require the recipient's acceptance (qabul), which is an action. The dispute centers on whether this action suffices to link the trade intention.
These modes involve an action by the acquirer (acceptance).
4
4. Present Abu Yusuf's view and reasoning
Abu Yusuf holds that acceptance is an action, so the trade intention is connected to it, making the asset trade property. The intention accompanies the action of taking ownership.
He interprets 'action' broadly.
5
5. Present Muhammad's view and reasoning
Muhammad argues that acceptance is not a trading action; it is merely the act of receiving. Since the intention is not connected to a trade-related action, the asset does not become trade property.
He requires the action itself to be of trade. A reverse narration is also reported.

نزدیک یہ چیز تجارت کے لئے نہ ہو گی ۔ کیونکہ نیت عمل تجارت کے ساتھ متصل نہیں ہوئی۔ اس لئے کہ یہ عقود یعنی ہیں، وصیت و غیر تجارت نہیں ہیں۔ بعض حضرات نے کہا ہے کہ اختلاف بر عکس ہے یعنی مذکورہ صورتوں میں امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک نیت تجارت کے باوجود وہ چیز تجارت کے واسطے نہ ہوگی۔ اور امام محمد کے نزدیک تجارت کے لئے ہو جائے گی۔
And if he bought something and intended it for trade, it is for trade because the intention is connected to the action, contrary to when he inherits and intends for trade, because there is no action from him. Or if he owned something through gift, bequest, marriage, khulu', or settlement for blood money, and he intended it for trade, it becomes for trade according to Abu Yusuf because it accompanies an action, but according to Muhammad it does not become for trade because the intention is not connected to the action of trade. And it is said that the dispute is the opposite.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage addresses the effect of trade intention on assets acquired without a purchase transaction. It begins by stating the rule for purchase: buying with trade intention makes the item a trade asset because the intention is immediately connected to the action of buying. In contrast, if one inherits something and then forms a trade intention, the item does not become a trade asset because inheritance involves no action from the heir. The text then discusses other modes of acquisition (gift, bequest, marriage dower, khulu', settlement for blood money). According to Imam Abu Yusuf, these acquisitions do involve an action from the recipient (acceptance), so the trade intention is connected to that action, making the asset trade property. According to Imam Muhammad, however, the intention is not connected to a trade-related action because these contracts are not themselves trading actions; therefore the asset does not become trade property. The commentary notes a reverse narration of the dispute. The practical consequence for zakah: if the asset is considered trade property, zakah is due on its value when the year passes; otherwise, no zakah unless it reaches nisab as non-trade wealth.

Key Terms
وِرَاثَة (wirathah): Acquisition of property from deceased without any action by the heir.
هِبَة (hibah): Gift; a contract requiring acceptance (qabul) considered an action.
خُلْع (khul'): Divorce in exchange for compensation; the husband acquires the consideration by acceptance.
قَبُول (qabul): Acceptance of a contract; the act of taking ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because gifts are not subject to zakah
B) Because the intention to trade is not connected to a trading action
C) Because the recipient's acceptance is not a valid action
D) Because gifts must be kept for one year before trading

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes purchase from inheritance regarding trade intention; for other acquisitions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad dispute whether acceptance connects intention, affecting zakah obligations.

Intention and Acquisition: Abu Yusuf vs. Muhammad on Trade Goods
Intra-Hanafi dispute on effect of intention on property acquired through non-trade means

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on when property becomes trade goods by intention, and apply the principle of ittisal al-niyyah bi al-‘amal to new scenarios.

Core Idea
Intention alone does not make property trade goods unless connected to a trade-related action or acquisition.

In this lesson, we examine an intra-Hanafi dispute on a key zakat question: when does property become trade goods ('urud al-tijarah) subject to zakat? The agreed principle is that intention must be connected to an action. The disagreement arises over which actions qualify. By understanding the reasoning of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, you will learn to apply the principle to various acquisition methods and see the practical impact on zakat obligations.

Guided Path
1
State the agreed rulings
Identify that purchase with intention creates trade goods, while inheritance with intention does not. Note the reason: purchase is an action connected to intention; inheritance is passive.
2
Understand the key principle
The principle of ittisal al-niyyah bi al-‘amal (connection of intention to action) is central. Without an action from the owner, intention alone is ineffective.
This principle is specific to Hanafi fiqh.
3
List the disputed acquisitions
Gift, bequest, marriage, khul', and settlement for blood-money are the methods where the Sahibayn differ.
These involve the recipient's acceptance but not trade.
4
Compare the two positions
Abu Yusuf says the act of acceptance (qabul) is sufficient to connect the intention, making property trade goods. Muhammad says the action must be trade-related; these contracts are not trade, so intention is not connected.
A reverse narration is also mentioned.
5
Apply Sahib 'Inayah's categorization
Classify acquisitions into: (a) without action (inheritance) – no intention effect by consensus; (b) with financial exchange (purchase) – intention effective; (c) with non-financial exchange or no exchange – disputed.
This helps summarize the ruling structure.

Source Text

تجارت کی نیت سے کوئی چیز خریدی وہ تجارت کے لئے ہی ہوگی ، اسی طرح اگر کسی کو میراث میں کوئی چیز ملی اس نے تجارت کی نیت کی اس کا کیا حکم ہے
وَانٍ اشْتَرى شَيْئًا وَنَوَاهُ لِلتِّجَارَةِ كَانَ لِلتِّجَارَةِ لِاِتِّصَالَ الَّتِيةِ بِالْعَمَلِ بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا وَرِثَ وَنَوَى لِلتِّجَارَةِ لِأَنَّهُ لَا عَمَلَ مِنْهُ وَلَوْ مَلَكَهُ بِالْهَبَةِ وَبِالْوَصِيَّةِ  أَوِ النِّكَاح أَوِ الْخُلع أَو الصُّلْحِ عَنِ الْقَوْدِ وَنَوَاهُ لِلتِّجَارَةِ كَانَ للتِّجَارَةِ عِند أبى يُوسُفَ لِافْتِرَانَهَا بِالْعَمَلِ وَعِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ لَا يَصِيرُ لِلتِّجَارَةِ لأنَّهَا لَمْ تَقَارِنُ عَمَلُ التِّجَارَةِ وَ قِيلَ الْاِخْتِلَافُ عَلَى عَكْسِهِ
ترجمہ اور اگر کوئی چیز خریدنی اور تجارت کے واسطے اس کی نیت کی تو وہ تجارت کی ہوگئی کیونکہ نیت عمل کے ساتھ متصل ہے۔ برخلاف اس کے اگر میراث میں کوئی چیز پائی اور تجارت کے لئے نیت کر لی کیونکہ اس کی طرف سے کوئی عمل نہیں ہوا۔ اور اگر وہ ہبہ سے کسی چیز کا مالک ہوا۔ یا وصیت سے مالک ہوا یا نکاح کے ذریعہ مالک ہوا۔ یا خلع کے ذریعہ مالک ہوا یا قصاص کے عوض صلح کر کے مالک ہوا اور اس چیز میں تجارت کی نیت کر لی تو ابو یوسف کے نزدیک وہ تجارت کے واسطے ہو جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ نیت عمل کے ساتھ متصل ہے اور امام محمد کے نزدیک وہ چیز تجارت کے واسطے نہ ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ نیت عمل تجارت کے ساتھ متصل نہیں ہوتی۔ اور کہا گیا کہ اختلاف اس کے برعکس ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے تجارت کی نیت سے کوئی چیز خریدی تو وہ چیز تجارت کی ہوگئی کیونکہ اس صورت میں نیت عمل اشتراء کے ساتھ متصل ہو گئی ہے۔ اور ظاہر ہے کہ اشترا بھی تجارت ہی کے لئے ہے تو گویا نیت تجارت کے ساتھ متصل ہوگئی۔ اور جونیت کسی چیز کی تجارت کے ساتھ متصل ہو تو وہ چیز تجارت ہی کے لئے شمار ہو گی ۔ اس کے برخلاف اگر کوئی چیز میراث میں پائی اور تجارت کی نیت کی تو وہ چیز تجارت کے لئے نہ ہوگی کیونکہ میراث اس کی ملک میں بغیر کسی عمل کے داخل ہوئی ہے۔ پس چونکہ نیت عمل تجارت کے ساتھ متصل نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے میراث کی چیز تجارت کی نیت کرنے کے با وجود تجارت کے لئے نہ ہوگی۔
کوئی شخص کسی چیز کا بطور ہبہ، وصیت نکاح ، خلع وغیرہ کے مالک ہوا اور تجارت کی نیت کی ، زکوۃ کا حکم: اور اگر کوئی شخص ہبہ سے کسی چیز کا مالک ہوا یعنی کسی نے اس کو کوئی چیز جبہ کی اور اس پر قبضہ دے دیا ، یا وصیت سے مالک ہوا۔ بائیں طور کہ کسی نے اس کے لئے کسی چیز کی وصیت کی ہو ۔ یا نکاح کے ذریعہ مالک ہوا۔ اس طور پر کہ اس نے اپنی باندی کا کسی کے ساتھ نکاح کیا اور اس کے مبر پر قبضہ کر کے مالک ہو گیا۔ یا خلع کے ذریعہ سے مالک ہوا ۔ اس طور پر کہ اس نے اپنی بیوی کا کسی عوض پر خلع کیا یا قصاص کے عوض مصلح کر کے مالک ہوا۔ اس طور پر کہ یہ شخص مقتول کا ولی ہے۔ پس قاتل سے کسی چیز کو عوض ٹھہرا کر صلح کر لی۔ بہر حال ان تمام صورتوں میں اگر اس شخص نے تجارت کی نیت کی تو امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک یہ چیز تجارت کے لئے ہو جائے گی کیونکہ یہاں تمام صورتوں میں نیت عمل کے ساتھ متصل ہو گئی ہے اور عمل یہ ہے کہ اس کی طرف سے ان چیزوں کا قبول کرنا پایا گیا۔ اور قبول کرنا اس کی طرف سے ایک عمل ہے۔ اور امام محمد کے نزدیک یہ چیز تجارت کے لئے نہ ہو گی ۔ کیونکہ نیت عمل تجارت کے ساتھ متصل نہیں ہوئی۔ اس لئے کہ یہ عقود یعنی ہبہ، وصیت وغیرہ تجارت نہیں ہیں۔ بعض حضرات نے کہا ہے کہ اختلاف بر عکس ہے یعنی مذکورہ صورتوں میں امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک نیت تجارت کے باوجود وہ چیز تجارت کے واسطے نہ ہوگی۔ اور امام محمد کے نزدیک تجارت کے لئے ہو جائے گی۔
صاحب عنایہ نے حاصل کے طور پر ذکر کیا ہے کہ جو چیز کسی آدمی کی ملک میں داخل ہوتی ہے۔ اس کی دوقسمیں ہیں ایک یہ کہ بغیر اس کے عمل کے داخل ہو جائے جیسے میراث کی چیز ۔ دوم یہ کہ اس کے عمل سے داخل ہو۔ پھر اس کی بھی دو قسمیں ہیں۔ ایک یہ کہ بدل مالی کے ساتھ داخل ہو جیسے شراء اور اجارہ یا بدل غیر مالی کے ساتھ داخل ہوا جیسے مہر ، بدل خلع بدل صلع عن دم العمد ۔ دوم یہ کہ بغیر بدل کے داخل ہو جیسے ہبہ، صدقہ اور وصیت پس جو چیز بغیر اس کے عمل کے اس کی ملک میں داخل ہوتی ہے۔ اس میں بالاتفاق محض نیت تجارت معتبر نہیں ہے اور جو چیز بدل مال کے ساتھ داخل ہوتی ہے۔ اس میں بالاتفاق نیت تجارت معتبر ہے۔ اور جو چیز بدل غیر مالی یا بغیر بدل کے ملک میں داخل ہوئی ہے اس میں اختلاف ہے جیسا کہ کتاب میں مذکور ہے۔
If someone buys something with the intention of trade, it is for trade, because the intention is connected to the action. Unlike if he inherits something and intends trade, because there is no action from him. If he owns something by gift, bequest, marriage, khul', or settlement for blood-money (qawd) and intends trade, according to Abu Yusuf it becomes for trade because the intention is connected to the action, but according to Muhammad it does not become for trade because the intention is not connected to a trade action. It is said the difference is opposite. Explanation: The issue is that if someone buys something with intention of trade, it becomes trade goods because the intention is connected to the act of purchase, which itself is trade. If he inherits and intends trade, it does not become trade goods because inheritance enters his ownership without any action from him. Therefore, since the intention is not connected to a trade action, the inherited item does not become trade despite the intention. For items acquired by gift, bequest, marriage, khul', or settlement for blood-money: according to Imam Abu Yusuf, if the person intends trade, the item becomes trade goods because in all these cases the intention is connected to the action of acceptance (qabul), which is an action from him. According to Imam Muhammad, the item does not become trade goods because the intention is not connected to a trade action, since these contracts (gift, bequest, etc.) are not trade. Some have said the difference is reversed i.e. in the mentioned cases, according to Abu Yusuf the item does not become trade despite intention, and according to Muhammad it becomes trade. Sahib 'Inayah summarized: Whatever enters a person's ownership is of two types: (1) Without his action, like inheritance; (2) With his action. The second type is further divided into: (a) with a financial exchange (like purchase and lease) or with a non-financial exchange (like mahr, khul' compensation, diyat); (b) without exchange (like gift, charity, bequest). For items entering without action, intention is not considered by consensus. For items entering with financial exchange, intention is considered by consensus. For items entering with non-financial exchange or without exchange, there is difference as stated in the book.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya discusses a key issue in zakat on trade goods: when does an item become considered 'trade goods' ('urud al-tijarah) subject to zakat? The ruling hinges on the connection between the intention to trade and the action by which the item is acquired. The text first presents the agreed ruling from the original matn: purchase with intent makes it trade goods; inheritance with intent does not. This is because purchase is itself a trade action, so intention is directly connected; inheritance involves no action from the heir. The commentary then expands into an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad over items acquired through other means like gift, bequest, marriage, khul', or settlement for blood-money. Abu Yusuf considers the act of acceptance (qabul) as an action sufficient to connect the intention, making the item trade goods. Muhammad argues that these contracts are not trade-related, so the intention is not properly connected. A reverse narration of the dispute is also mentioned. Finally, Sahib 'Inayah provides a helpful categorization: items entering ownership without action (inheritance) never become trade goods by intention; items with financial exchange always do; items with non-financial exchange or no exchange are disputed. This analytical framework is essential for understanding zakat obligations on various types of property.

Key Terms
نية التجارة (niyyat al-tijarah): The intention to trade with a specific property.
عروض تجارة (‘urud al-tijarah): Goods intended for trade and subject to zakat.
اتصال النية بالعمل (ittisal al-niyyah bi al-‘amal): The principle that intention must be directly connected to an action for it to be effective.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if someone inherits property and intends to trade with it, does the property become trade goods subject to zakat?
A) Yes, because intention alone suffices.
B) No, because no action accompanied the acquisition.
C) Yes, but only according to Muhammad.
D) No, but Abu Yusuf disagrees.

Key Takeaway
Intention must be connected to an action of acquisition for property to become trade goods; the dispute among Hanafi scholars concerns which actions qualify.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate
8 min
Condition of Intention in Giving Zakat
Explaining the necessity of intention and the permissible times for it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition of intention for zakat and explain the concession of intending at the time of setting aside the amount.

Core Idea
Intention is required for zakat; but to avoid hardship, the intention at setting aside suffices for later distributions.

Zakat is an act of worship, and all worship requires intention (niyyah). However, the practical difficulty of renewing intention with each payment led the Hanafi school to allow the intention to be made when one first separates the zakat amount. This lesson unpacks the proof from the Quran and the juristic preference (istihsan) that eases the obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule and its condition
The matn states zakat is invalid without intention. The condition is that intention must either accompany the act of giving (ada') or accompany the act of setting aside (azl).
2
Examine the proof
The commentator invokes Quran 98:5, which commands sincerity. Sincerity requires intention, so intention is necessary for any worship, including zakat.
3
Consider the qiyas objection
One might argue that setting aside is not an act of worship, so intention there shouldn't count. This is the expected qiyas.
4
Apply istihsan to resolve
Istihsan overrides the qiyas to avoid hardship, since people often give zakat in multiple installments. The intention at azl covers all subsequent distributions.
5
Draw the analogy with fasting
Just as advance intention suffices for fasting, the intention at azl suffices for zakat.

وَ لَا يَجُوزُ أداء الزكوةِ إلَا بِنِيَّةٍ مُقَارِنَةٍ لِلْأدَاء أَوْ مُقَارِنَةً لِعَزْلِ مِقْدَارِ الْوَاجِبِ لِأَنَّ الزَّكَوةَ عِبَادَةً فَكَانَ مِنْ شَرْطِهَا النِّيَةُ وَالْأَصْلُ فِيهَا الْاِقْتِرَانُ إِلَّا أَنَّ الدَّفَعَ يَتَفَرَّقُ فَاكْتُفِي بِوُجُودِهَا حَالَةُ الْعَزْلِ تَيْسِيرًا كَتَقْدِيمِ النِّيَّةِ فِي الصُّوْمِ
ترجمہ اور زکوۃ ادا کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ مگر ایسی نیت کے ساتھ جو ادا سے متصل ہو یا مقدار واجب جدا کرنے سے متصل ہو۔ کیونکہ زکوة عبادت ہے۔ لہذ اس کی شرط میں سے نیت ہے۔ اور نیت میں اصل اتصال ہے۔ مگر فقیروں کو دینا متفرق واقع ہوتا ہے تو مقدار واجب کو نصاب سے جدا کرنے کے وقت نیت ہونے پر اکتفاء کیا گیا۔ آسانی کے پیش نظر جیسے روزہ میں تقدیم نیت کافی ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ادائے زکوۃ کے لئے نیت شرط ہے کیونکہ فعل زکوۃ عبادت ہے اور عبادت کے لئے نیت شرط ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے زکوۃ ادا کرنے کے لئے نیت کرنا شرط ہو گا۔ اور عبادت کے لئے نیت اس لئے شرط ہے کہ کوئی عبادت بغیر اخلاص کے ادا نہیں ہوتی ۔ کیونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ کا ارشاد ہے وَمَا أُمِرُوا إِلَّا لِيَعْبُدُوا اللهَ مُخْلِصِينَ لَهُ الدِّينَّ ۔ یعنی ان کو حکم یہی ہوا کہ بندگی کریں اللہ کی خالص کر کے اس کے واسطے بندگی اور اخلاص بغیر نیت کے نہیں پایا جاتا۔ پس ثابت ہوا کہ عبادت کے لئے نیت کرنا ضروری ہے اور چونکہ زکوۃ ادا کرنا بھی عبادت ہے اس لئے زکوۃ ادا کرنے کے لئے بھی نیت کرنا ضروری ہوگا۔ رہی یہ بات کہ ادائے زکوۃ کے لئے نیت کا وقت کیا ہے؟ تو امام قدوری نے فرمایا کہ نیت یا تو زکوۃ ادا کرتے وقت کی جائے یا مقدار واجب کو مال سے جدا کرتے وقت کی جائے یعنی جب پورے مال کا حساب کر کے زکوۃ کی جو مقدار نکلتی ہے اس کو مال سے جدا کر کے الگ رکھتے ہوئے ارادہ کیا تو جدا کرتے وقت نیت کرلے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ نیت کے اندر اصل عبادت کے ساتھ متصل ہونا ہے۔ جیسے نماز میں نیت نماز سے متصل ہو تی ہے۔ اس کا تقاضا تو یہ ہے کہ زکوۃ ادا کرتے وقت کی نیت تو معتبر ، کیونکہ زکوۃ کا ادا کرنا عبادت ہے اور نیت کا عبادت کے ساتھ متصل ہونا ضروری ہے لیکن مقدار زکوۃ کو مال سے جدا کرتے وقت کی نیت معتبر نہ ہو۔ کیونکہ مقدار زکوۃ کو مال سے جدا کر کے اپنے ہی گھر میں رکھ لینا یہ کوئی عبادت نہیں ہے۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ مقدار واجب کو مال سے جدا کرتے وقت کی نیت کا اعتبار ضرورۃ حرج دور کرنے کے لئے کیا گیا ہے۔ اس طور پر کہ بسا اوقات انسان متفرق اوقات میں متفرق لوگوں کو زکوۃ دیتا ہے۔ پس اگر ہر بار دیتے وقت نیت کرنا لازم قرار دے دیا جائے تو یہ شخص حرج اور ضرر میں مبتلا ہو جائے گا۔ پس آسانی کے پیش نظر مال سے جدا کرتے وقت کی نیت پر اکتفاء کر لیا گیا۔ جیسے روزہ میں تقدیم نیت کافی ہے۔
It is not permissible to give zakat except with an intention that accompanies the giving or accompanies the setting aside of the obligatory amount. Because zakat is a worship, so intention is among its conditions. The principle regarding intention is that it must accompany the act, except that giving is often done in separate instances, so the presence of intention at the time of setting aside is deemed sufficient for ease, just as the advance intention is sufficient in fasting. Explanation: The issue is that intention is a condition for giving zakat because the act of zakat is worship, and intention is a condition for worship. This is because no worship is performed without sincerity, as Allah says: 'And they were not commanded except to worship Allah, being sincere to Him in religion.' Sincerity cannot be found without intention. Thus it is established that intention is necessary for worship, and since giving zakat is worship, intention is also necessary for it. As for the time of intention: Imam Quduri stated that intention should be made either at the time of giving or at the time of setting aside the obligatory amount from the wealth. This is because the principle is that intention should accompany the act of worship, as in prayer. The requirement would be that intention at the time of giving is valid, but intention at the time of setting aside would not be valid because setting aside is not in itself worship. However, the validity of intention at the time of setting aside is allowed out of necessity to avoid hardship, since a person may give zakat to multiple people at different times. Requiring intention at each giving would cause hardship, so it is sufficient to intend at the time of setting aside, just as advance intention is sufficient for fasting.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage deals with the condition of intention (niyyah) in the payment of zakat. The author begins with the ruling from the matn: zakat is not valid without intention, which must either accompany the actual payment or accompany the act of physically separating (azl) the zakat amount from one's total wealth. The reason given is that zakat is an act of worship, and worship requires intention. The commentary then provides the Quranic proof from Surah Al-Bayyinah (98:5) that sincerity is commanded, which implies intention. A potential objection is raised: why is intention at the time of setting aside sufficient, when setting aside is not itself worship? The answer is istihsan (juristic preference) to avoid hardship, since people often give zakat in installments to multiple recipients. Requiring a fresh intention for each payment would be burdensome, so the intention made when setting aside the amount carries forward. This is analogous to fasting, where intention made before dawn (tahqiq al-niyyah) suffices even though the act of fasting lasts all day. The discussion clarifies that while the original principle is that intention must be concomitant with the act of worship, necessity allows for a broader application in the case of zakat.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): The mental resolve to perform an act of worship for the sake of Allah.
عزل ('azl): The act of physically separating the calculated zakat amount from one's wealth, before distributing it.
إستحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; a secondary source of law that permits departure from qiyas due to exceptional need.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi fiqh, when can the intention for zakat be made?
A) Only at the moment of giving to the poor.
B) Any time before giving, including the night before.
C) At the time of giving or at the time of setting aside the obligatory amount.
D) Intention is not required for zakat.

Key Takeaway
Intention for zakat can be made at the time of setting aside the amount, easing the obligation for multiple payments.

Intention for Zakat: Condition and Concession
Ruling that intention is required and can be at setting aside amount

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the timing of intention for zakat and explain the rationale for the concession based on istihsan.

Core Idea
Intention for zakat is a condition; it can be made at payment or at isolation of the amount, easing hardship.

This passage from the Hidayah establishes that intention is a condition for zakat, citing the Quranic command for sincerity. However, recognizing the practical difficulty of intending at every payment, a concession is provided: intention at the time of setting aside the obligated amount suffices. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proof, and the Hanafi method of juristic preference (istihsan) that underlies the concession.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act is paying zakat. The ruling is that intention is a condition (shart) and is wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the Quranic verse (98:5) commanding sincere worship. This proves intention is required for all acts of worship.
The verse is dalil for the principle that intention is a condition.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Sincerity (ikhlas) requires intention. Since zakat is worship, it requires intention. The proof is from the general command, but the specific timing is derived from other considerations.
The connection between the verse and the ruling is through the necessity of niyyah for ikhlas.
4
Note the ikhtilaf and the concession
The general rule is that intention must be concurrent with the act (like in salah). However, because zakat payments are often dispersed, a concession is made based on istihsan: intention at the time of isolating the amount suffices.
The concession avoids hardship (haraj).
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is that intention at isolation is sufficient. This is the mufta bihi, supported by al-Quduri and others.
The ruling is based on zahir al-riwayah.

وَ لَا يَجُوزُ أَدَاءُ الزَّكَاةِ إِلَّا بِنِيَّةٍ مُقَارِنَةٍ لِلْآدَاءِ أَوْ مُقَارِنَةً لِعَزْلِ مِقْدَارِ الْوَاجِبِ لِأَنَّ الزَّكَاةَ عِبَادَةً فَكَانَ مِنْ شَرْطِهَا النِّيَّةُ وَالْأَصْلُ فِيهَا الْاِقْتِرَانُ إِلَّا أَنَّ الدَّفْعَ يَتَفَرَّقُ فَاكْتُفِيَ بِوُجُودِهَا حَالَةَ الْعَزْلِ تَيْسِيرًا كَتَقْدِيمِ النِّيَّةِ فِي الصُّوْمِ

فقیروں کو دینا متفرق واقع ہوتا ہے تو مقدار واجب کو نصاب سے جدا کرنے کے وقت نیت ہونے پر اکتفاء کیا گیا آسانی کے پیش نظر جیسے روزہ میں تقدیم نیت کافی ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ادائے زکوۃ کے لئے نیت شرط ہے کیونکہ فعل زکوۃ عبادت ہے اور عبادت کے لئے نیت شرط ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے زکوۃ ادا کرنے کے لئے نیت کرنا شرط ہوگا۔ اور عبادت کے لئے نیت اس لئے شرط ہے کہ کوئی عبادت بغیر اخلاص کے ادا نہیں ہوتی ۔ کیونکہ اللہ جدا کرتے وقت نیت کرلے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ نیت کے اندر اصل عبادت کے ساتھ متصل ہونا ہے۔ جیسے نماز میں نیت نماز کے شروع ہونے سے متصل ہوتی ہے۔ اس اصول کا تقاضا تو یہ ہے کہ زکوۃ ادا کرتے وقت کی نیت تو معتبر، کیونکہ زکوۃ کا ادا کرنا عبادت ہے اور نیت کا عبادت کے ساتھ اتصال ہونا ضروری ہے لیکن مقدار زکوۃ کو مال سے جدا کرتے وقت کی نیت معتبر نہ ہو۔ کیونکہ مقدار زکوۃ کو مال سے جدا کر کے اپنے ہی گھر میں رکھ لینا یہ کوئی عبادت نہیں ہے۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ مقدار واجب کو مال سے جدا کرتے وقت کی نیت کا اعتبار ضرورۃً حرج دور کرنے کے لئے کیا گیا ہے۔ اس طور پر کہ بسا اوقات انسان متفرق اوقات میں متفرق لوگوں کو زکوۃ دیتا ہے۔ پس اگر ہر بار دیتے وقت نیت کرنا لازم قرار دے دیا جائے تو یہ شخص حرج اور ضرر میں مبتلا ہو جائے گا۔ پس آسانی کے پیش نظر مال سے جدا کرتے وقت کی نیت پر اکتفاء کر لیا گیا۔ جیسے روزہ کے اندر تقدیم نیت پر اکتفاء کیا گیا ہے۔ اس لئے کہ اصل تو یہ ہے کہ روزہ کی نیت صبح صادق کے اول جزء کے ساتھ متصل ہو لیکن چونکہ انسان اس سے عاجز ہے اور اس کی پوری پوری رعایت کرنے میں اس کو حرج بھی لاحق ہوگا ۔ اس لئے کہا گیا کہ نیت اگر اس پر مقدم ہو گئی تو بھی کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے اس کا اعتبار کر لیا جائے گا۔
Condition for payment of zakat: It is not permissible to pay zakat except with an intention that is concurrent with the payment or concurrent with the isolation of the obligated amount, because zakat is an act of worship, so intention is among its conditions, and the principle regarding intention is concurrence, except that payment is dispersed, so it is sufficed with its existence at the time of isolation for facilitation, like the advancement of intention in fasting.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage establishes the ruling that intention (niyyah) is a condition for paying zakat, as it is an act of worship requiring sincerity. The author states the general principle that intention must be concurrent with the act of worship. However, due to practical hardship if one had to intend at each separate payment, the ruling provides a concession: intention may be made at the time of setting aside the obligated amount from the total wealth, similar to the permissibility of making intention for fasting before dawn. The commentary elaborates by citing the Quranic verse on sincerity (Bayyinah 5) and explains the rationale of removing hardship. It also contrasts with prayer, where intention must be at the start of the prayer. The discussion follows the order: condition of intention, general rule, exception for zakat due to multiple payments, analogy with fasting, and refutation of a potential objection regarding the timing of intention.

Key Terms
نیت (niyyah): Intention; the mental determination to perform an act of worship with sincerity for Allah.
استحسان (istihsan): This term is used in the explanation of the ruling: the concession to intend at the time of setting aside is based on istihsan (juristic preference) to avoid hardship.
